Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling of Tahlil: Second Husband Creates New Lawfulness
Hanafi response to Shafi'i objection about the verse 'hatta tankiha' and proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument for tahlil by distinguishing the dalil from the verse and the hadith, and apply the concept of isharat al-nass to derive the ruling that the second husband creates new lawfulness.

Core Idea
The second husband creates independent lawfulness through intercourse, not merely removes prohibition.

This lesson examines a classic usul dispute: does the second husband merely remove the prohibition, or does he create a new lawful state? The passage presents the Hanafi response to an objection based on the verse 'hatta tankiha', clarifying that the real evidence is the well-known hadith of Rifa'ah's wife. Through this dispute, we explore the usul principle of isharat al-nass and how a hadith can add a condition to the apparent meaning of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and its basis
The objector claims that the verse 'hatta tankiha' with the particle 'hatta' only indicates the end of prohibition, not that the second husband creates new lawfulness. Understand the linguistic argument.
The word 'hatta' means 'until', marking an endpoint.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to the verse
The Hanafi scholar responds that they do not rely on this verse; indeed, the verse cannot be used as evidence because 'tankiha' means marriage, not intercourse. If it were the end, mere marriage would suffice, which is false.
The Hanafi position is that the verse does not prove the opponent's claim.
3
Locate the Hanafi dalil: the hadith
The primary evidence is the hadith of Rifa'ah's wife, where the Prophet said: 'No, until you taste his honey and he tastes yours.' This hadith is well-known and can add to the Quran.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Apply isharat al-nass to derive the ruling
The hadith uses the word 'ta'udi' (return) instead of 'remove prohibition'. The Hanafi principle of isharat al-nass (implicit indication) shows that the woman returns to a previous lawful state, meaning the second husband creates a new, independent halal status.
The word 'awd' implies restoration of a prior condition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If no intercourse occurs, Hanafis say she does not become lawful; opponents say she does. This practical difference stems from the usul principles used.
This highlights the real-world impact of the dispute.

Source Text

كسی نے کہا: اضربك حتى يجيء حامد، میں تجھ کو مارتا رہوں گا یہاں تک کہ حامد آ جائے، یعنی حامد کے آنے کے بعد مارنا ختم کر دوں گا۔ پس 'حتی' کے معنی کی روشنی میں آیت کا مطلب ہوگا کہ پہلے شوہر کے تین طلاق دینے کی وجہ سے جو حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہوگئی تھی، دوسرے شوہر کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے وہ حرمت ختم ہو گئی ہے۔ كلمہ 'حتی' صرف اس معنی پر دلالت کرتا ہے، اس پر قطعا دلالت نہیں کرتا کہ دوسرا شوہر پہلے شوہر کے لئے جدید اور از سر نو حلت پیدا کرتا ہے۔ پس شیخین کا یہ کہنا کہ زوج ثانی زوج اول کے لئے حلت جدید پیدا کرتا ہے، یہ خاص كلمہ 'حتی' کے موجب کو باطل کرنا ہے۔ اور جس صورت میں مغیا موجود ہے یعنی تین طلاقوں کی وجہ سے حرمت غلیظہ موجود ہے، اس صورت میں دوسرا شوہر پہلے شوہر کے لئے محلل یعنی حلت جدیدہ پیدا کرنے والا نہ ہو سکا، تو جس صورت میں مغیا بھی موجود نہیں یعنی تین طلاقوں سے کم کی صورت میں دوسرا شوہر بدرجہ اولی پہلے شوہر کے لئے محلل نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ اگر حرمت غلیظہ ہی نہ پائی جائے تو اس کی انتہاء بھی نہیں ہوگی، اس لیے یہاں اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ دو یا دو سے کم طلاقوں کے بعد ہونے والی حرمت کی انتہاء بھی زوج ثانی کے ساتھ نکاح سے ہو جائے گی تو خاص کے موجب پر عمل نہیں ہو گا۔

جواب: آپ کا اعتراض تب درست تھا جب ہم نے زوج اول کے لیے عورت کی حلت جدیدہ پر اسی آیت یعنی 'حتی تنكح' سے دلیل پکڑی ہو، حالانکہ ہم نے اس سے دلیل نہیں پکڑی بلکہ اس آیت سے دلیل پکڑنا تو درست ہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں 'تنكح' کا لفظ ہے اور اس سے مراد عقد نکاح ہے، وطی نہیں، کیونکہ اس کی نسبت عورت کی طرف کی ہے اور وطی عورت نہیں کرتی مرد کرتا ہے، تو نکاح مراد ہے۔ تو جب 'تنكح' سے مراد عقد نکاح ہے تو اس سے دلیل پکڑنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر اس سے دلیل پکڑتے ہوئے اس کو حرمت غلیظہ کی انتہاء بنائیں تو لازم آئے گا کہ صرف عقد نکاح ہی سے عورت زوج اول کے لیے حلال ہو جائے اور یہ درست نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اس آیت سے دلیل نہیں پکڑی جاسکتی، بلکہ اس عورت کے زوج اول کے لیے حلال ہونے کی دلیل حدیث عسیلہ ہے کہ جس میں رفاعہ قرظی کی بیوی حضور اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس حاضر ہوئی اور آپ سے عرض کیا کہ میرے خاوند رفاعہ قرظی نے مجھے تین طلاق دیں، تو میں نے عدت گزارنے کے بعد عبد الرحمن بن زہیر سے نکاح کیا لیکن میں نے ان کو نامرد پایا، تو حضور نے فرمایا: 'لا حتى تذوقي عسيلته و يذوق عسيلك' یعنی تم رفاعہ کے پاس اس وقت تک نہیں لوٹ سکتی جب تک تم جماع کی لذت اور حلاوت حاصل نہ کر لو۔ یہ حدیث اس بات کو بیان کرنے کے لئے لائی گئی ہے کہ حلالہ کے لئے زوج ثانی کا وطی کرنا شرط ہے اور محض نکاح جیسا کہ ظاہر آیت سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے وہ کافی نہیں۔ اور یہ حدیث مشہور ہے اور اس جیسی مشہور حدیث سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادت بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ یہ حدیث جس طرح عبارت النص سے حلالہ کے لئے وطی شرط ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہے، اسی طرح اشارۃ النص سے زوج ثانی کے محلل ہونے پر بھی دلالت کرتی ہے، اس طور پر کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے فرمایا تھا: 'أتریدین أن تعودی إلی رفاعہ؟' کیا تم رفاعہ کے پاس لوٹنا چاہتی ہو؟ اور آپ نے یہ نہیں فرمایا: 'أتریدین أن تختی حرمتک؟' بہر حال رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے 'أن تعودی' کا لفظ فرمایا اور 'عود' کہتے ہیں پہلی حالت کی طرف لوٹنے کو، اور پہلی حالت میں رفاعہ کے پاس اس کے لئے حلت ثابت تھی۔ لہذا اب جب یہ پہلی حالت کی طرف لوٹے گی تو اس کی حلت بھی لوٹے گی اور مستقل نئی حلت پیدا ہو گی۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زوج ثانی مطلقہ مغلظہ کو زوج اول کے لئے مستقل حلال کر دیتا ہے اور زوج ثانی زوج اول کے لئے محلل ہے۔ اور جب اس صورت میں حلت ثابت ہوگئی جب زوج اول نے تین طلاقیں دی ہوں اور حالت بالکل معدوم تھی، تو جس صورت میں زوج اول نے ایک یا دو طلاق دی ہوں اور حلت ناقص ہو، معدوم نہ ہو، تو اس صورت میں بدرجہ اولی زوج ثانی زوج اول کے لئے حلت ثابت کرے گا، کیونکہ معدوم کو وجود میں لے آنے سے ناقص کو مکمل کرنا آسان ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ ہم نے استدلال حلت جدیدہ پر اس حدیث سے کیا ہے، آیت سے نہیں۔ كیافلا اعتراض۔
Someone said: 'I will strike you until Hamid comes' — meaning I will continue striking you until Hamid arrives, then I will stop. So based on the meaning of 'hatta', the interpretation of the verse is that the severe prohibition (hurmat ghalizah) resulting from the first husband's three divorces is removed by marriage to the second husband. The word 'hatta' only indicates this meaning; it does not at all indicate that the second husband creates a new, fresh lawfulness for the first husband. Therefore, the statement of the two shaykhs that the second husband creates a new lawfulness for the first husband invalidates the implication of the word 'hatta'. In the case where the limit (moghayya) exists — i.e., the severe prohibition due to three divorces — the second husband cannot be a muhallil (creator of new lawfulness) for the first husband. So in the case where the limit does not exist — i.e., less than three divorces — a fortiori the second husband will not be a muhallil for the first husband, because if the severe prohibition does not exist, there is no end to it. Therefore, if it is said here that the prohibition after two or fewer divorces also ends with marriage to the second husband, then the implication of 'hatta' would not be acted upon.

Answer: Your objection would be valid if we had used this verse itself (hatta tankiha) as evidence for the new lawfulness for the first husband. However, we did not use it as evidence; indeed, it is not correct to use this verse as evidence because the word here is 'tankiha' and it means marriage contract (nikah), not intercourse, because it is attributed to the woman, and a woman does not perform intercourse; a man does. So 'tankiha' means marriage. Since 'tankiha' means marriage, using it as evidence is not correct, because if we take it as evidence for the end of the severe prohibition, it would entail that merely the marriage contract makes the woman lawful for the first husband, which is incorrect. Therefore, this verse cannot be used as evidence. Rather, the evidence for the woman becoming lawful for the first husband is the hadith of 'asilah', in which the wife of Rifa'ah al-Qurazi came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'My husband Rifa'ah divorced me three times. After completing my 'iddah, I married 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Zuhayr, but I found him impotent.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'No, until you taste his honey and he tastes your honey' (la hatta tadhūqī 'usaylatahu wa yadhūq 'usaylatik). This means you cannot return to Rifa'ah until you have experienced the pleasure and sweetness of intercourse. This hadith is brought to show that for tahlil, intercourse with the second husband is a condition, and mere marriage, as understood from the apparent meaning of the verse, is not sufficient. This hadith is well-known, and it is unanimously permissible to add to the Book of Allah through such well-known hadith. Just as this hadith indicates by its express wording ('ibarat al-nass) that intercourse is a condition for tahlil, so too it indicates by its implication (isharat al-nass) that the second husband is a muhallil. This is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to this woman: 'Do you wish to return to Rifa'ah?' He did not say: 'Do you wish to remove your prohibition?' In any case, the Prophet used the word 'ta'udi (return)', and 'awd' means returning to a previous state. In the previous state, she had lawfulness with Rifa'ah. Therefore, when she returns to that state, her lawfulness also returns, and a new, independent lawfulness is created. From this hadith, it is understood that the second husband makes the woman with a severe divorce permanently lawful for the first husband, and the second husband is a muhallil for the first husband. Since this lawfulness is established in the case where the first husband gave three divorces and the state of lawfulness was completely absent, then in the case where the first husband gave one or two divorces and the lawfulness is deficient but not absent, a fortiori the second husband will establish lawfulness for the first husband, because completing a deficient thing is easier than bringing something from non-existence. In summary, we have based our argument for new lawfulness on this hadith, not on the verse. So no objection.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi reply to an objection regarding the interpretation of the verse 'hatta tankiha' in the context of tahlil (making a woman lawful for her first husband after being divorced by a second husband). The objector argued that using the verse to prove that the second husband creates a new lawfulness for the first husband is invalid because the word 'hatta' (until) only indicates the end of the prohibition, not the creation of a new status. The Hanafi response clarifies that they do not rely on this verse at all; rather, they rely on the well-known hadith of the wife of Rifa'ah al-Qurazi. In that hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) stipulated that the woman must taste the honey of her second husband (i.e., intercourse) before she can return to her first husband. This hadith is used to establish two points: first, that intercourse (not mere marriage) is necessary for tahlil; second, that the second husband is a muhallil who creates a new and independent lawfulness for the first husband. The Hanafi author explains this through the Prophet's use of the word 'ta'udi (return)', which implies a return to a previous state of lawfulness, thus creating a new halal status. Moreover, by analogy, if this holds for three divorces (complete removal of lawfulness), it holds even more strongly for fewer divorces (where lawfulness is merely deficient). Thus, the passage defends the Hanafi position that the second husband is a muhallil and that the condition for tahlil is actual intercourse, not just the marriage contract.

Key Terms
حتی (hatta): A particle meaning 'until', indicating the end point of a preceding action or state.
محلل (muhallil): The second husband who, by consummating the marriage, makes the woman lawful for her first husband after three divorces.
عود ('awd): Returning to a previous state; in this context, returning to the state of being lawful for the first husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for a woman to become lawful for her first husband after being divorced by the second husband?
A) Merely marrying the second husband
B) The second husband divorcing her
C) Consummating the marriage with the second husband
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Rifa'ah's wife is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position that the second husband creates a new, independent lawfulness through intercourse.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Ruling of the General ('Amm): Three Views
Matn presenting three views on the ruling of 'amm with illustrative examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions on the ruling of 'amm (tawaqquf, adna, all) and apply the Hanafi principle that 'amm is decisive in indicating generality unless specified.

Core Idea
The general term ('amm) is decisive and binding on all its individuals — it is not ambiguous and does not only establish a minimum.

This passage from Al-Tawdih presents three classical views on how to understand the general term in scripture. You will see why the Hanafi school, alongside Imam al-Shafi'i, insists on the full generality of the text, and how this principle plays out in concrete rulings. The passage also provides examples that illustrate the practical consequences of each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and list the three views presented: tawaqquf (suspension), adna (minimum), and 'all' (generality for all individuals). Note which scholars hold each view.
The passage mentions 'some' for the first two and 'us and al-Shafi'i' for the third.
2
Understand the tawaqquf view
Analyze the argument that 'amm is ambiguous (mujmal) because plural numbers vary (3-10 for jam' al-qillah, 10+ for jam' al-kathrah). This leads to suspending the ruling until evidence clarifies.
The proof given is that the plural can be interpreted in multiple ways.
3
Understand the adna view
Examine the claim that only the minimum is certain (mutayaqqan): three for plural, one for non-plural. The example of 'dirhams' is used to show that only three are owed unless specified otherwise.
This view prioritizes certainty over generality.
4
Analyze the Hanafi-Shafi'i position
This position holds that 'amm necessitates the ruling for all individuals. The proof is that generality is a meaning intended in discourse, and words are placed for such meanings. The use of emphasis (kull, ajma') confirms, not creates, generality.
The passage argues that even if the plural can refer to one, that is metaphorical, not the primary meaning.
5
Examine the illustrative examples
Look at the examples of 'Ali on combining sisters and Ibn Mas'ud on the pregnant widow. How do they apply general verses? Note that these examples also involve conflict (ta'arud) and abrogation (naskh), but they demonstrate how the principle of 'amm is used in practice.
The examples show that the general is taken as comprehensive until a specific indication (qarinah) or conflict is resolved.

Source Text

فَصْلٌ : (حُكُمُ الْعَامُ التَّوَقُفُ عِندَ الْبَعْضِ حَتَّى يَقُومَ الدَّلِيلُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ مُجْمَلٌ لاخْتِلَافِ أَعْدَادِ الْجَمْعِ فَإِنَّ جَمْعَ الْقِلَّةِ يَصِحُ أَنْ يُرَادَ مِنْهُ كُلُّ عَدَدٍ مِنْ الثَّلَاثَةِ إلَى الْعَشَرَةِ ، وَجَمْعُ الْكَثُرَةِ يَصِحُ أَنْ يُرَادَ مِنْهُ كُلُّ عَدَدٍ مِنْ الْعَشَرَةِ إِلَى مَا لَا نِهَايَةَ لَهُ ، فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا قَالَ لِزَيْدٍ عَلَى أَفْلُسٌ يَصِحُ بَيَانُهُ مِنَ الثَّلَاثَةِ إِلَى الْعَشَرَةِ فَيَكُونُ مُجْمَلًا ) وَإِنَّهُ يُوَكَّدُ بِكُلِّ وَأَجْمَعَ وَلَوْ كَانَ مُسْتَغْرِفًا لَمَا أُحْتِيجَ إِلَى ذَلِكَ وَلَأَنَّهُ يُذْكَرُ الْجَمْعُ وَيُرَادُ بِهِ الْوَاحِدُ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ) الَّذِينَ قَالَ لَهُمُ النَّاسُ إِنَّ النَّاسَ قَدْ جَمَعُوا لَكُمْ الْمُرَادُ مِنْهُ نُعَيْمُ بْنُ المَسْعُودِ أَوْ أَعْرَابِيٌّ آخَرُ ، وَالنَّاسُ الثَّانِي أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ
( وَعِندَ الْبَعْضِ يَثْبُتُ الْأدْنَى ، وَهُوَ الثَّلاثَةُ فِي الْجَمْعِ وَالْوَاحِدُ فِي غَيْرِهِ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَيَقَّنُ ) فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا قَالَ لِقَلانِ عَلَيَّ دَرَاهِمُ تَجِبُ ثَلاثَةٌ بِاتِّفَاقٍ بَيْنَنَا ، وَبَيْنَكُمْ لَكِنا نَقُولُ إِنَّمَا تَثْبُتُ الثَّلاثَةُ ؛ لأنَّ الْعُمُومَ غَيْرُ مُمْكِن فَيَثْبُتُ أَحَصُّ الْخُصُوصِ وَعِندَنَا وَعِندَ الشَّافِعِي رَحِمَهُ اللهُ يُوجِبُ الحُكْمَ فِى الْكُلِّ ) نَحْو جَاءَنِي الْقَوْمُ يُوجِبُ الْحُكْمَ وَهُوَ نِسْبَةُ الْمَجِىء إِلَى كُلِّ أَفْرَادٍ تَنَاوَلَهَا الْقَوْمُ . ( لأنّ العُمُومَ مَعْنَى مَقْصُودٌ فَلا بُدَّ أَن يَكُونَ لَفُظْ يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ) فَإِنَّ الْمَعَانِيَ الَّتِي هِيَ مَقْصُودَةٌ فِي التَّحَاطُبِ قَدْ وُضِعَ الْأَلْفَاظُ لَهَا .
( وَقَدْ قَالَ عَلِيٌّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُ فِي الْجَمْعِ بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ وَطُلًّا بِمِلْكِ الْيَمِينِ أَحَلَّتْهُمَا آيَةً وَهِيَ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) أَوْ مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُكُمْ ) ( فَإِنَّهَا تَدُلُّ عَلَى حِلٌ وَطْء كُلِّ أَمَةٍ مَمْلُوكَةٍ سَوَاءٌ كَانَتْ مُجْتَمِعَةٌ مَعَ أُخْتِهَا فِي الْوَطْء أَوْلَا. ) وَحَرَّمَتْهُمَا آيَةً وَهِيَ ) أَنْ تَجْمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْأَخْتَيْنِ ) ( تَدُلُّ عَلَى حُرُمَةِ الْجَمْعِ بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ الْجَمْعُ بِطَرِيقِ النِّكَاحِ ، أَوْ بِطَرِيقِ الْوَطْء بِمِلْكِ الْيَمِينِ ) فَالْمُحَرِّمُ رَاجِحٌ) كَمَا يَأْتِي فِى فَصْلِ التَّعَارُضِ أَنَّ الْمُحَرِّمَ رَاجِحٌ عَلَى الْمُبِيحِ ) وَابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُ جَعَلَ قَوْله تَعَالَى ( وَأُولَاتُ الْأَحْمَالِ ) نَاسِخًا لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنْكُمْ) حَتَّى جَعَلَ عِدَّةَ حَامِلٍ تُوُفِّيَ عَنْهَا زَوْجُهَا بِوَضْعِ الْحَمْلِ اخْتَلَفَ عَلِيٌّ وَابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا فِي حَامِلٍ تُوُفِّيَ عَنْهَا زَوْجُهَا ， فَقَالَ عَلِيٌّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُ تَعْتَدُّ بِأَبْعَدِ الْأَجَلَيْنِ تَوْفِيقًا بَيْنَ الْآيَتَيْنِ إِحْدَاهُمَا فِي سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ وَهِيَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنْكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنْفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا) وَالْأُخْرَى فِي سُورَةِ النِّسَاءِ الْقُصْرَى وَهِيَ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) وَأُولَاتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ أَنْ يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ
Section: The ruling of the general: Suspension (tawaqquf) according to some until evidence is established, because it is ambiguous (mujmal) due to the differing numbers of the plural. For the plural of paucity (jam' al-qillah) can be intended for any number from three to ten, and the plural of multitude (jam' al-kathrah) can be intended for any number from ten to infinity. For example, when he says 'Zaid owes me fulus (multiple dirhams),' it can be explained as from three to ten, so it is ambiguous. And it is emphasized by 'kull' and 'ajma''. If it were comprehensive, there would be no need for that. And because the plural is mentioned and the singular is intended, as Allah's statement: 'Those to whom the people said: Indeed, the people have gathered against you.' The intended is Nu'aym ibn Mas'ud or another bedouin, and the second 'people' refers to the people of Makkah. And according to some, the minimum is established: three in the plural and one in other than the plural, because that is the certain (mutayaqqan). For example, when he says 'So-and-so owes me dirhams,' three are obligatory by agreement between us and you, but we say: only three are established because generality is not possible, so the most specific of the specific is established. And according to us and according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), it necessitates the ruling for all individuals, like 'the people came to me' necessitates the ruling, which is the attribution of coming to every individual that 'people' encompasses. Because generality is a meaning that is intended, so there must be a word that indicates it. Indeed, the meanings that are intended in discourse have words placed for them. And 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said regarding combining two sisters and intercourse by right of possession: one verse made them lawful, which is His saying 'Or what your right hands possess' for it indicates the permissibility of intercourse with every owned slave girl, whether she is combined with her sister in intercourse or not. And another verse made them forbidden, which is 'that you combine between two sisters' for it indicates the prohibition of combining between two sisters, whether the combination is by marriage or by intercourse by right of possession. So the prohibiter is preponderant (rajih) as will come in the section on conflict that the prohibiter is preponderant over the permissive. And Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) made His saying 'And those who are pregnant' abrogating (nasikh) for His saying 'And those who die among you' such that he made the waiting period of a pregnant woman whose husband dies to be by giving birth. 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with them) differed regarding a pregnant woman whose husband died. 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: She observes the longer of the two periods, reconciling between the two verses: one in Surat al-Baqarah which is His saying 'And those who die among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten [days],' and the other in the shorter Surat al-Nisa' which is His saying 'And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth to their pregnancy.'
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is from the matn (likely Al-Tawdih) and presents three views on the ruling of the general ('amm) when it comes to plural forms. Some hold that the general is ambiguous (mujmal) and requires suspension (tawaqquf) until evidence clarifies, because the plural can vary from three to ten (plural of paucity) or from ten to infinity (plural of multitude). Others hold that the minimum is established: three for the plural and one for non-plural (like 'dirhams'), because that is the certain number. The preferred Hanafi view (and according to Imam al-Shafi'i) is that the general necessitates the ruling for all individuals, because generality is a meaning intended for discourse, and there are words that indicate it. The passage then provides two examples to illustrate principles. The first is 'Ali's view on combining two sisters in marriage and by right of possession: he used two verses—one permissive ('or what your right hands possess') and one prohibitive ('do not combine between two sisters'). He ruled that the prohibitive is preponderant because the prohibiter takes precedence over the permissive (as in the section on conflict). The second example is the dispute between 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud on the waiting period of a pregnant widow. 'Ali reconciled the two verses (four months and ten days vs. until delivery) by taking the longer period. Ibn Mas'ud considered the pregnancy verse as abrogating (nasikh) the widow verse, so the waiting period ends with delivery. This illustrates how general texts can be qualified by specific or abrogating evidence.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A word that by its linguistic meaning encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.
مجمل (mujmal): A word that is ambiguous because its meaning is not clearly determined, such as the plural that could indicate various numbers.
جمع القلة (jam' al-qillah): Plurals that indicate a range of three to ten (e.g., aqlam, aydi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is the ruling of the general ('amm) when no specification is present?
A) It is suspended until evidence clarifies its meaning.
B) It establishes the minimum (three for plural, one for others).
C) It necessitates the ruling for all individuals it encompasses.
D) It is considered ambiguous (mujmal).

Key Takeaway
The general term ('amm) in Hanafi usul is decisive and applies to all individuals it encompasses, unless evidence of specification is established.

Hanafi Refutation of al-Jubba'i's Argument on 'Amm
Refutes Jubba's proof by showing it relies on invalid analogy from fiqh to language

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi refutation of al-Jubba'i's claim that 'amm yields a minimum of three individuals, and explain why the presence of a qarina invalidates the argument.

Core Idea
Language is conventional; you cannot use qiyas (analogy) from fiqh to derive linguistic rules.

In this passage, the author responds to Abu Ali al-Jubba'i, who used a fiqh example—'he owes me three dirhams'—to argue that a general term (amm) yields at least three individuals. The Hanafi response makes two essential points: first, establishing linguistic rules through rational analogy (qiyas) is invalid because language is conventional; second, the cited example actually contains a qarina (indication) that specifies the number three, so it is not a case of a general term without restriction. Therefore, the example does not support al-Jubba'i's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim under refutation
What exactly does al-Jubba'i argue? He claims that from a general term (amm), at least three individuals are meant, using the fiqh example as proof.
The example is: 'He owes me three dirhams.'
2
Recognize the Hanafi methodological critique
The Hanafi response first states that language cannot be proven by qiyas (analogy); it is conventional (wad'iy). Hence, using a fiqh analogy to establish a linguistic principle is methodologically unsound.
This is a key usul point: al-umur al-lughawiyyah la tuthbat bi al-qiyas.
3
Examine the fiqh example closely
The example 'He owes me three dirhams' has an explicit number (three). This number acts as a qarina (contextual indicator) that specifies the intended meaning.
A qarina can restrict a general term; here it leaves no ambiguity.
4
Contrast with the subject of the dispute
The debate about 'amm concerns terms without any qarina. Since the example has a qarina, it cannot be used to prove anything about unrestricted general terms.
Thus, al-Jubba'i's proof fails—it does not apply to the matter under discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب دليل : لكنا نقول انما يثبت الثلاثة : یہاں سے مصنف نے ابو علی جبائی کی دلیل کا جواب دیا ہے کہ یہ لغت کو قیاس سے ثابت کرنا ہے حالانکہ لغت کو عقل یا قیاس سے ثابت کرنا باطل ہے باقی رہا فقہی مسئلہ تو آپ کا اس مسئلہ سے یہ دلیل پکڑنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس مسئلہ میں تین افراد علی الاطلاق اس لئے مراد لیے جاتے ہیں کہ یہاں عام کے تمام افراد مراد نہیں لیے جاسکتے۔ لہذا کم از کم جتنے افراد مراد لیے جا سکتے تھے وہ مراد لیے گئے ہیں اور وہ تین ہیں تو یہاں تین افراد کے مراد ہونے پر قرینہ پایا گیا ہے اور بحث اس عام میں چل رہی ہے جس کے افراد کی تعیین پر کوئی قرینہ نہ ہو لہذا آپ کا اس مسئلہ سے دلیل پکڑ کر یہ کہنا عام سے کم از کم افراد جو یقینی ہوں وہ مراد لیے جائیں گے درست نہیں ہے۔
Answer to the proof: But we say that the three are only established here. The author responds to Abu Ali al-Jubba'i's proof by saying that this is establishing language by analogy, while establishing language by reason or analogy is invalid. As for the fiqh issue, your holding onto this issue as a proof is not correct, because in that issue the three individuals are absolutely meant because all individuals of the general term cannot be meant. Therefore, the minimal individuals that could be meant were taken, and they are three. Thus, here a qarina was found indicating that three are meant, whereas the discussion is about a general term for which there is no qarina determining its individuals. Hence, your argument that from a general term the minimal certain individuals are meant is incorrect.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi response to Jubba'i's use of the fiqh example. The response makes two points: First, it is invalid to derive linguistic rules (like the meaning of 'amm) through logical analogy (qiyas). Language is conventional, not rational. Second, the fiqh example actually has a qarina (indication) that three are meant, because the phrase 'he owes me three dirhams' cannot be applied to more than three—the number three is explicitly specified. In contrast, a general term like 'al-qawm' (the people) has no such qarina. Therefore, the example does not support Jubba'i's claim. The Hanafi view holds that 'amm includes all individuals unless a qarina limits it.

Key Terms
قرینہ (qarīna): An indication or contextual clue that specifies the intended meaning of a general term

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi refutation, why does the example 'he owes me three dirhams' not prove al-Jubba'i's view?
A) Because the example involves a singular term
B) Because the example has a qarina specifying three
C) Because the example is from fiqh not language
D) Because the example uses a different plural form

Key Takeaway
Language is conventional and cannot be proven by rational analogy; a general term without a qarina includes all of its individuals, not a minimum number.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Ahl al-Sunnah View on 'Amm: Inclusivity and Proofs
States Ahl al-Sunnah position on 'amm with rational and transmitted proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on 'amm, explain the rational and transmitted proofs, and apply the principle to interpret general texts and resolve conflicts.

Core Idea
'Amm includes all individuals unless a qarina limits it; language coins words for intended meanings.

In this lesson, we study the foundational Hanafi usul principle that a general term ('amm) covers all its individuals without exception until a valid indicator (qarina) excludes some. The source presents two proofs: a rational argument based on the nature of language and a transmitted proof from the practice of Imam Ali. Understanding this rule is crucial for correctly applying general Quranic commands and avoiding arbitrary restriction.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Read the first paragraph to grasp the standalone ruling: 'amm includes all individuals in its scope. Note that this applies when no qarina is present to limit it.
This is the default position of Ahl al-Sunnah (Hanafis and Shafi'is).
2
Examine the rational proof
The rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) argues that words are coined for intended meanings. Since 'amm is coined for generality, it must include all individuals; otherwise, the meaning of generality would lack a dedicated word.
This is a linguistic argument, not a logical syllogism.
3
Analyze the transmitted proof
The transmitted proof (dalīl naqlī) cites Ali's application of Quranic verses. He interpreted 'wa mā malakat aymānukum' as permitting intercourse with all women under possession, including sisters, showing he considered the term 'amm.
Ali's method demonstrates that the Sahaba understood 'amm comprehensively.
4
Resolve apparent conflict
Ali also invoked the verse 'wa lā tajmaʿū bayna al-ukhtayn' as a general prohibition. When two general texts conflicted, he gave precedence to the prohibition over the permissibility.
This shows that even when 'amm applies, conflict resolution follows established usul rules.
5
Apply to new cases
Practice applying the rule: any general Quranic or hadith command includes all its potential referents unless a specific qarina (e.g., another verse, hadith, or rational evidence) restricts it.
This principle impacts many fiqh rulings, from inheritance to criminal penalties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذہب اہل سنت
وعندنا وعند الشافعی یوجب الحكم في الكل مذهب اهل سنت : اہلسنت احناف اور شوافع کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ عام کے اطلاق کے وقت وہ اپنے تمام افراد کو شامل ہوگا یعنی اس کے تمام افراد کو حکم شامل ہو جائے گا بغیر توقف کے ہاں اگر بعض افراد کے مراد نہ ہونے پر دلیل یا قرینہ قائم ہو جائے تو پھر تمام افراد مراد نہیں ہوں گے۔ لیکن دلیل اور قرینہ کے نہ ہونے کے وقت تمام افراد ہی مراد ہوں گے مثال جیسے جاء فی القوم میں قوم عام ہے تو یہاں مجعیت والا حکم ان تمام افراد میں ثابت ہو گا جن کو لفظ قوم شامل ہے البتہ اگر بعض کے مراد نہ ہونے پر قرینہ قائم ہو جائے تو وہ مراد نہیں ہوں گے۔
دلائل اہل سنت :۔ اہل سنت کی دو دلیلیں ہیں ایک دلیل عقلی اور دوسری دلیل نقلی ہے۔
دليل عقلى : . لان العموم معنی مقصود عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عام سے مقصود عموم والا معنی ہوتا ہے اور تخاطب میں جو معانی مقصود ہوتے ہیں ان کے لیے ضرور کوئی نہ کوئی لفظ لغت میں وضع کیا گیا ہے تو یہاں بھی عام کی وضع عموم والے معنی کے لیے ہے لہذا عام سے عموم والا معنی علی الاطلاق مراد ہوگا۔ اور تمام افراد میں حکم ثابت ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ عام سے تمام افراد میں حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا تو لازم آئے گا کہ عموم والے معنی کے لیے کوئی لفظ بھی وضع نہ کیا گیا ہو اور یہ باطل ہے۔ دلیل نقلی : دلیل نقلی میں مولف نے دو مسئلے ذکر کیے ہیں۔
مسئله اول: وقد قال على فى الجمع بين الاختين وطيا بملک الیمین : قرآن پاک کی ایک آیت ہے و ما ملکت ایمانکم“ کہ وہ عورتیں جو ملک یمین کے تحت ملک میں آئی ہوں ان سے وطی کرنا حلال ہے حضرت علی نے اس بارے میں فرمایا ہے کہ اس آیت سے دو بہنوں کو ملک یمین کے تحت وطی میں جمع کرنے کی حلت ثابت ہو رہی ہے حالانکہ اس آیت میں دو بہنوں کا کوئی ذکر نہیں ہے تو حضرت علی نے جو اس آیت سے حلت کو سمجھا ہے وہ اس لیے کہ یہ مملکت عام ہے کہ ملک یمین کے تحت آنے والی عورتوں سے وطی کرنا حلال ہے چاہے ایک عورت ہو یا زیادہ عورتیں ہوں چاہے بہنیں ہوں یا نہ ہوں اور حضرت علی نے اس عموم کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے حالت کو سمجھا ہے اور فرمایا ہے کہ یہ آیت دو بہنوں کو ملک یمین کے تحت وطی میں جمع کرنے کو حلال قرار دے رہی ہے۔ اور ایک دوسری آیت ہے وان تجمعوا بين الاختين " کہ دو بہنوں کو جمع کرنا حرام ہے یہاں ملک نکاح یا ملک یمین کا تذکرہ نہیں ہے لیکن حضرت علیؓ نے فرمایا ہے کہ آیت دو بہنوں کو ملک یمین کے تحت وطی میں جمع کرنے کو حرام کر رہی ہے اس سے بھی یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حضرت علی نے یہاں ان تجمعوا " میں بھی عموم کا اعتبار کیا ہے کہ یہ آیت دو بہنوں کو جمع کرنے کی حرمت بتلا رہی ہے چاہے ان کو جمع کرنا ملک نکاح کے تحت ہو یا ملک یمین کے تحت۔ اس کے بعد حضرت علی نے یہ فرمایا کہ اول آیت مباح ہے اور ثانی محرم ہے تو دو بہنوں کو ملک یمین کے تحت وطی میں جمع کرنے کے حق میں یہ دونوں متعارض ہو گئیں اور تعارض کے وقت محرم کو مباح پر ترجیح ہوتی ہے اس لیے دوسری آیت "وان تجمعوا بين الاختين " کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے ہم کہیں گے کہ دو بہنوں کو ملک یمین کے تحت وطی میں جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔ تو اس ساری بحث سے یہ معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت علیؓ نے عام میں عموم اور استغراق کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔
Madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah: According to us and according to al-Shafi'i, it necessitates the ruling in all. The madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah (Hanafis and Shafi'is) is that when a general term is applied, it includes all its individuals, meaning the ruling applies to all its individuals without hesitation. However, if a proof or qarina is established that some individuals are not meant, then not all individuals are meant. But when there is no proof or qarina, then all individuals are meant. Example: In 'he came among the people' (jāʾa fī al-qawm), 'al-qawm' is general. Here, the ruling of coming is established in all individuals that the word qawm includes, unless a qarina is established that some are not meant, then they are not meant.
Proofs of Ahl al-Sunnah: They have two proofs: one rational and one transmitted proof.
Rational proof: Because 'umum (generality) is a meaning intended. The rational proof is that from the general term, the meaning of generality is intended, and in speech, for meanings that are intended, there must be some word in the language that is coined for them. Here too, the general term is coined for the meaning of generality. Therefore, the meaning of generality is absolutely meant from the general term, and the ruling is established in all individuals. Because if it were said that from the general term the ruling is not established in all individuals, then it would necessitate that no word has been coined for the meaning of generality, and this is false.
Transmitted proof: In the transmitted proof, the author mentions two issues.
First issue: And Ali said concerning marrying both sisters through sexual intercourse by right hand possession: There is a verse in the Qur'an, 'And those whom your right hands possess' stating that it is halal to have sexual intercourse with women who come under possession by right hand. Regarding this, Ali said that from this verse the permissibility of combining two sisters in sexual intercourse under right hand possession is established, even though the verse does not mention two sisters. Ali understood permissibility from this verse because the phrase is general: it is halal to have sexual intercourse with women under right hand possession, whether one woman or many, whether sisters or not. Ali considered this generality and understood the ruling, stating that the verse declares it halal to combine two sisters in sexual intercourse under right hand possession. And another verse is 'And do not combine between two sisters' which states that combining two sisters is haram. Here, neither marriage nor right hand possession is mentioned. But Ali said that the verse makes it haram to combine two sisters under right hand possession. This also shows that Ali here considered generality in 'do not combine' that this verse forbids combining two sisters, whether the combination is through marriage or right hand possession. Then Ali said that the first verse is mubah (permissible) and the second is muharram (forbidden). So regarding combining two sisters under right hand possession, these two became conflicting. In case of conflict, the forbidden takes precedence over the permissible. Therefore, giving preference to the second verse, we say that combining two sisters under right hand possession is haram. So from this entire discussion, it becomes clear that Ali considered generality and comprehensiveness (istighraq) in the general term.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage presents the Ahl al-Sunnah (Hanafi and Shafi'i) position on the scope of 'amm. The rule is: when a general term is used without any qarina (indication) or proof otherwise, it includes all possible individuals. The proof is twofold: (1) Rational: language coins words for intended meanings; the meaning of generality is intended in 'amm, so it must include all. If it didn't, that meaning would lack a proper word, which is invalid. (2) Transmitted: The example of Ali ibn Abi Talib using the verses on right hand possession. Ali understood the verse 'And those whom your right hands possess' (Qur'an 4:24) as permitting intercourse with all such women, including sisters, due to its generality. He also interpreted the verse 'Do not combine between two sisters' (Qur'an 4:23) as forbidding combination in any context (marriage or possession). He then resolved the apparent conflict by giving priority to the prohibition. This demonstrates that Ali considered 'amm to include all individuals. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that 'amm is comprehensive and includes all individuals until a qarina indicates otherwise.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A general term that includes all individuals that fall under its meaning when used without a qarina
استغراق (istighrāq): Comprehensiveness; 'amm covers every single individual without exception
دلیل عقلی (dalīl ʿaqlī): Rational proof based on linguistic convention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunnah, when does a general term include all its individuals?
A) Only when explicitly stated
B) Only when there is no qarina limiting it
C) Only when the term is singular
D) Always, regardless of qarina

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: 'amm includes all individuals by default; restriction requires a valid qarina.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Proof of 'Umum: Rational Evidence and Companion Practice
Establishing 'umum through rational proof and two Companion examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that 'umum is qat'i by identifying the rational and textual proofs for 'umum and distinguish how Companions used 'umum in conflicting texts.

Core Idea
The general term binds all its instances until a contextual indication specifies otherwise — the Companions proved this through their practice.

This lesson explores how the Hanafi school establishes the principle of 'umum (generality) through both rational argument and the practice of the Companions. You will examine the rational proof that language requires words for general meanings, and then analyse two key examples from 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud that demonstrate their application of 'umum even when texts appeared to conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of proof
The passage presents a rational proof (dalīl 'aqlī) and a textual proof (dalīl naqlī). Read the rational proof and understand its logical structure: the general term is coined for the meaning of generality; if it did not indicate all individuals, no word would exist for generality.
The rational proof is a logical argument, not a revelation.
2
Examine the first textual example: 'Alī on two sisters in milk yamīn
'Alī considered both the permission verse (mā malakat aymānukum) and the prohibition verse (an tajma'ū bayna al-ukhtayn) as general, creating a conflict that he resolved by preferring prohibition. This shows he assumed each verse covered all cases within its scope.
3
Examine the second textual example: 'Alī and Ibn Mas'ūd on 'iddah of a pregnant widow
Both Companions saw a conflict between Sūrat al-Ṭalāq (delivery) and Sūrat al-Baqarah (four months ten days). 'Alī reconciled by taking the longer term; Ibn Mas'ūd held that Sūrat al-Ṭalāq abrogated. Both treatments rely on interpreting each verse as general.
Note: Their differing resolution methods (jam' vs naskh) still required 'umum.
4
Derive the usūl principle
From these examples, conclude that the Companions consistently applied 'umum, supporting the Hanafī position that 'umum is a definitive (qat'ī) indication until takhṣīṣ.
This principle is foundational in Hanafī uṣūl.

سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ اس کی عدت وضع حمل ہے اور سورہ بقرہ کی آیت سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ اس کی عدت چار ماہ دس دن ہے تو ان آیات کے اس تعارض میں تو حضرت علی اور حضرت ابن مسعود متفق ہیں لیکن تعارض کو ختم کرنے کی کیفیت میں اختلاف ہے۔ حضرت علی یہ فر ماتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں آیتوں میں سے ناسخ منسوخ کا علم نہیں ہے کہ جو ناسخ ہو اس کو ترجیح دی جائے لہذا ان کے درمیان موافقت پیدا کی جائے گی اور اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت کی عدت ابعد الاجلین ہوگی کہ دونوں آیات پر عمل ہو جائے کہ اگر وضع حمل پہلے ہو جائے تو اس کی عدت چار ماہ دس دن ہوگی اور اگر چار ماہ دس دن پہلے پورے ہو جائیں اور وضع حمل نہ ہوا ہو تو اس کی عدت وضع حمل ہوئی ہے اس لیے ان کے نزدیک جب سورۃ طلاق بعد میں نازل ہوئی تو واولات الاحمال اجلهن ان يضعن حملهن والى آيت والذين يتوفون منكم ويذرون ازواجا کے لیے تاریخ ہو گی اس لیے یہ صرف تاریخ پر عمل کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا (جو حاملہ ہو ) کی عدت وضع حمل ہوگی۔ اب ساری بحث سے یہ بات معلوم ہوگی کہ حضرت علی اور حضرت ابن مسعودؓ عام میں عموم کے قائل تھے کیونکہ انہوں نے آیات میں تعارض کا قول کیا ہے اور یہ تعارض کا قول کرنا عموم مراد لینے کے بغیر نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اگر عموم مراد نہ ہو تو کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ و اولات الاحمال اجلبن مطلقہ حاملہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور والذين يتوفون منكم... متوفى عنها زوجها
It will be established in all individuals that the word 'qawm' includes, but if there is a qarina that some are not intended, then they will not be intended. The proofs of Ahl al-Sunnah: Ahl al-Sunnah have two proofs: one rational proof and one textual proof. Rational proof: because 'umum is the intended meaning. The rational proof is that the general term intends the meaning of generality, and in discourse, for the intended meanings, some word must have been coined in the language for them. So here too, the general term is coined for the meaning of generality. Therefore, the general term will refer to the meaning of generality absolutely. And the ruling will be established in all individuals, because if it were said that the general term does not establish the ruling in all individuals, it would necessitate that no word had been coined in the language for the meaning of generality, and that is false. Textual proof: In the textual proof, the author has mentioned two issues. First issue: And 'Ali said regarding combining two sisters in intercourse by right hand possession: There is a verse in the Holy Quran: 'and what your right hands possess' that intercourse is permissible with women who have come into your possession through right hand possession. Regarding this, 'Ali said that this verse establishes permissibility of combining two sisters in intercourse by right hand possession, even though there is no mention of two sisters in the verse. So 'Ali understood permissibility from this verse because it is general: intercourse is permissible with women under right hand possession, whether one woman or many women, whether sisters or not. And 'Ali gave consideration to this generality and understood the situation, and he stated that this verse declares combining two sisters in intercourse by right hand possession as permissible. And another verse is: 'and do not combine between two sisters' that combining two sisters is forbidden. Here there is no mention of marriage or right hand possession, but 'Ali said that this verse prohibits combining two sisters in intercourse by right hand possession. From this also, it is known that 'Ali gave consideration to generality in 'do not combine', meaning this verse indicates the prohibition of combining two sisters, whether the combination is under marriage or under right hand possession. After that, 'Ali said that the first verse is permissible and the second is forbidden, so regarding combining two sisters in intercourse by right hand possession, these two become conflicting. And at the time of conflict, the forbidden is given precedence over the permissible. Therefore, giving precedence to the second verse 'and do not combine between two sisters', we say combining two sisters in intercourse by right hand possession is forbidden. So from this entire discussion, it is known that 'Ali gave consideration to 'umum and istighraq in the general term. Second issue: And Ibn Mas'ud made qawl (statement) regarding the saying of Allah 'and those with burdens': The second issue is a statement regarding the ruling of generality, and it is the second textual proof for Ahl al-Sunnah. The issue is: if a woman's husband dies and she is pregnant, then 'Ali's view is that her 'iddah will be the longer of the two terms, meaning whichever ends later between delivery and four months ten days, that will be her 'iddah. And Ibn Mas'ud says that her 'iddah is only delivery. This difference arose because in Surah al-Talaq it says: 'and those with burdens, their term is that they deliver their burden'. From this, it is established that the 'iddah of pregnant women is delivery—general whether they have been divorced or their husband died; this detail is not in the verse. And in Surah al-Baqarah: 'and those who die among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves four months and ten days'. From this, it is established that women whose husband has died—whether pregnant or not—their 'iddah is four months and ten days. And both 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud affirm that these two verses conflict regarding a deceased husband's pregnant wife: the Surah al-Talaq verse indicates her 'iddah is delivery, and the Surah al-Baqarah verse indicates her 'iddah is four months ten days. So regarding this conflict of verses, 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud agree, but they differ on the method of resolving the conflict. 'Ali says that there is no knowledge of which is abrogating and which is abrogated to give precedence to the abrogator. Therefore, reconciliation will be made between them, and the way is that the woman's 'iddah will be the longer of the two terms, so that both verses are acted upon: if delivery occurs first, then her 'iddah is four months and ten days; and if four months and ten days are completed first and delivery has not occurred, then her 'iddah is delivery. But Ibn Mas'ud says that Surah al-Talaq was revealed after Surah al-Baqarah, and he would challenge to mubahalah: 'I am ready to do mubahalah that Surah al-Talaq was revealed after Surah al-Baqarah.' Therefore, in his view, since Surah al-Talaq was revealed later, it will be abrogating for the verse 'and those who die among you and leave wives'. Thus, acting only on the abrogator, he says that for a deceased husband's pregnant wife, her 'iddah is delivery. Now from the entire discussion, it will be known that 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud were proponents of 'umum in general terms, because they affirmed a conflict between the verses, and this affirmation of conflict is not possible without taking the meaning of generality. Because if generality were not intended, it could be said that 'and those with burdens' was revealed concerning a divorced pregnant woman, and 'and those who die among you'... concerning a deceased husband's wife.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is a usul discussion proving that the general term (al-'am) includes all individuals of its category unless a specific indication (qarina) excludes some. The author presents two types of evidence: rational and textual. The rational proof (dalil 'aqli) argues that language must have words for general meanings; since the general term is coined for generality, it absolutely indicates that meaning. The textual proof (dalil naqli) consists of two examples from the Companions. First, the example of 'Ali regarding two sisters in milk yamin: 'Ali understood the verse 'and what your right hands possess' as general, allowing intercourse with all such women, and the verse 'do not combine between two sisters' as general, forbidding any combination. He saw a conflict and resolved it by giving precedence to the prohibition. This shows that 'Ali treated both verses as general. Second, the example of 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud on the 'iddah of a pregnant widow. Both saw conflict between Surah al-Talaq (delivery) and Surah al-Baqarah (four months ten days). 'Ali, not knowing which is later, reconciled by taking the longer period. Ibn Mas'ud believed Surah al-Talaq was later and thus abrogated, so only delivery applies. Both Companions' handling of the conflict proves they believed both verses were general; otherwise, there would be no conflict. The passage establishes the principle that 'umum is a valid concept and that the Salaf applied it consistently.

Key Terms
عموم ('umum): Generality: the meaning that encompasses all individuals that the word applies to.
قرينہ (qarina): A contextual indication that specifies or restricts the general term.
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict between two evidences that appear contradictory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Ibn Mas'ud believe that the 'iddah of a pregnant widow is only delivery, while 'Ali believed it is the longer of the two terms?
A) Ibn Mas'ud did not know about the verse in Surah al-Baqarah.
B) 'Ali thought both verses were revealed at the same time, Ibn Mas'ud knew Surah al-Talaq was later.
C) Ibn Mas'ud considered the verse in Surah al-Talaq as khass (specific), not general.
D) 'Ali did not accept the principle of 'umum.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' practice confirms that the general term is binding on all its instances, and conflict between two general texts requires either abrogation or reconciliation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
The Generality of 'Amm: The Pregnant Widow's 'Iddah as a Proof
Dispute over the definitive nature of 'amm using a fiqh example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that 'amm is qat'i in indicating all individuals by analyzing the conflict between Q 65:4 and Q 2:234, and evaluate the opponents' arguments against generality.

Core Idea
A general term includes every subset; conflict between two general texts proves their generality.

In this lesson, we examine a classical usul dispute: is the general term ('amm) definitive and all-encompassing, or is it ambiguous requiring specification? The Hanafi school holds that 'amm without a contextual indicator includes all its individuals. To prove this, the author invokes the example of the pregnant widow, where both Imam 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud recognized a conflict between two Quranic verses on 'iddah. Their recognition of conflict demonstrates that they treated each verse as generally applicable, otherwise no conflict would arise. We will retrace this argument and then see how the Hanafis rebut three counterarguments claiming that 'amm is ambiguous.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Quranic verses and their apparent conflict
Read Surah al-Talaq (65:4) which says the 'iddah of pregnant women is childbirth, and Surah al-Baqarah (2:234) which says the 'iddah of widows is four months and ten days. Note the overlap: a pregnant widow falls under both verses, creating a conflict.
The verses are general: first covers all pregnant women (divorced or widowed), second covers all widows (pregnant or not).
2
Understand how 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud resolved the conflict
Both Companions agreed there is a conflict. 'Ali reconciled by taking the later of the two terms. Ibn Mas'ud argued that 65:4 abrogated 2:234 for pregnant widows because it was revealed later.
Despite different resolutions, both based their reasoning on the generality of each verse.
3
Connect the conflict to the nature of 'amm
Ask: why did they see a conflict? If either verse were not general, one could say 65:4 applies only to divorced pregnant women and 2:234 only to non-pregnant widows, avoiding conflict. Their acknowledgment of conflict proves they considered each verse generally applicable to all its possible instances.
This is the core argument: conflict only arises when both texts are general and overlap.
4
Examine the opponents' three arguments against generality
The opponents claim 'amm is ambiguous. Their proofs: (1) 'ala al-fulus' (upon the coins) requires specification; (2) 'amm is emphasized by 'kull' showing it does not inherently include all; (3) plural can refer to a single individual (e.g., Q 2:275).
These arguments are drawn from the passage's second part.
5
Apply the Hanafi refutation to each argument
For (1): the coin example has a contextual indicator (impossibility of all coins); absolute 'amm has none. For (2): emphasis presupposes prior generality, not the opposite. For (3): metaphorical use for singular does not negate literal generality; it is due to a qarinah.
Thus, 'amm without qarinah remains definitive and all-inclusive.

زوجها غیر حاملہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے لہذا کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے تعارض اسی صورت میں لازم آئے گا جب عموم کو مانا جائے اور یہ کہا جائے کہ اول آیت حاملہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے خواہ وہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا دلائل و اقفین کے جوابات:۔ (i) پہلی دلیل یھی کہ عام مجمل ہوتا ہے۔ اور اسکے افراد میں سے کوئی فرد بھی مراد ہوسکتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ علی الفلس میں جب تک متکلم فلوس کی تعداد کو بیان نہیں کرے گا ہم حکم کو ثابت نہیں کر سکتے ۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب کوئی وجہ ترجیح موجود نہ ہو تو ایسی جمع کو کل پر محمول کیا جائے گا اس صورت میں بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح دینا بھی لازم نہیں آئے گا اور اجمال بھی باقی نہیں رہے گا خلاصہ یہ کہ جمع کا مختلف اعداد کو شامل ہونا توقف کا مقتضی نہیں بلکہ استغراق اور تمام افراد مراد لینے کا مقتضی ہے تا کہ ترجیح بلا مرجح سے بچ جائیں ہاں اگر تمام افراد کے مراد نہ ہونے پر قرینہ پایا جائے تو پھر تمام افراد مراد نہیں لیے جاتے اور آپ نے جو مثال بطور دلیل پیش کی ہے یہاں تمام افراد کے مراد نہ ہونے پر قریبہ پایا جاتا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ ظاہر ہے ایک آدمی پر دنیا کے تمام فلوس لازم نہیں ہو سکتے ۔ اور ہم بات کر رہے ہیں قرینہ کے نہ ہونے کے وقت مطلق عام کی لہذا اس مثال سے استدلال درست نہیں ہے۔
(ii) دوسری دلیل یہ تھی کہ عام کی تاکید کل اور اجمع“ کے ساتھ لائی جاتی ہے جو اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ عام تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوتا ہے لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ تو اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ عام اپنے تمام افراد کو شامل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ تاکید اس معنی کی لائی جاتی ہے جو پہلے مؤکد میں پایا جا رہا ہو اگر عام میں عموم نہ پایا جائے تو اس کی تاکید کل اور اجمع کے ساتھ درست نہ ہوتی یہ تاکید درست ہی اس لیے ہے کہ عام میں پہلے سے عموم پایا جاتا ہے یعنی یہ اپنے تمام افراد کو شامل ہوتا ہے لہذا کل اور اجمع کے ساتھ عام کی دلیل لانا یہ ہماری دلیل ہے نہ کہ تمہاری (ii) تیسری دلیل یہ تھی کہ کبھی جمع سے ایک فرد مراد ہوتا ہے کبھی زیادہ افراد مراد ہوتے ہیں جیسا کہ ” قال لہم الناس ان الناس قد جمعو الکم " تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جمع کا اطلاق حقیقہ کثیر کے لئے ہوتا ہے لیکن مجازا اس سے فرد واحد مراد لے سکتے ہیں آئمہ لغت نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ جمع سے ایک مراد لیا جاتا ہے مجازا اور تمام افراد مراد لئے جاتے ہیں حقیقہ تو بھی اجمال یا اشتراک باقی نہیں رہے گا نیز اس طرح یہاں جمع سے مراد جو ایک فرد مراد لیا گیا ہے یہ بھی قرینہ کی وجہ سے کہ ظاہر ہے
Second issue and Ibn Mas'ud took the verse 'And those pregnant women, their term is that they deliver their burden': The second issue is an expression of the second branch of the ruling on the general, and the proof of the Ahl al-Sunnah is transmitted. The issue is that if a woman's husband dies and she is pregnant, 'Ali's school is that her 'iddah is the later of the two terms, i.e., whichever of childbirth or four months and ten days occurs later is her 'iddah. Ibn Mas'ud says that her 'iddah is childbirth. This difference arose because in Surah al-Talaq it says: 'And those pregnant women, their term is that they deliver their burden' from which it is established that the 'iddah of pregnant women is childbirth, general whether they are divorced or their husband has died. And in Surah al-Baqarah it says: 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days' which establishes that the 'iddah of a woman whose husband has died, whether pregnant or not, is four months and ten days. Both 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud agree that these two verses conflict regarding the pregnant widow: Surah al-Talaq indicates her 'iddah is childbirth, Surah al-Baqarah indicates her 'iddah is four months and ten days. They agree on the conflict but differ on how to resolve it. 'Ali says we do not know which is abrogating and which abrogated, so we reconcile by taking the later of the two terms, thus both verses are acted upon: if childbirth comes first, her 'iddah is four months and ten days; if four months and ten days finish first, her 'iddah is childbirth. Ibn Mas'ud says that Surah al-Talaq was revealed after Surah al-Baqarah, and he would offer to invoke a curse (mubahalah) that Surah al-Talaq came after, so it abrogates the earlier verse, thus the pregnant widow's 'iddah is childbirth. From this discussion it becomes clear that both 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud believed in the general application of the general term ('amm), because they acknowledged the conflict between the verses. This acknowledgment of conflict is impossible without taking the general meaning, because if general meaning was not intended, one could say that the first verse was revealed about pregnant divorced women and the second about non-pregnant widows, so no conflict. Conflict only arises when the general is accepted and it is said that the first verse is about pregnant women whether widowed or not, and the second about widows whether pregnant or not. Thus it is established that the general term absolutely indicates generality, and the ruling applies to all its individuals. That is the meaning of Ma'in's statement 'wa dhalika 'ammun kulluhu.'

Responses to the opponents' arguments: (i) The first argument is that the general is ambiguous and any individual could be intended, like 'upon the coins' where until the speaker specifies the number we cannot establish the ruling. The response is that when there is no reason for preference, such a plural is taken to indicate all, thus there is no need to prefer some over others and no ambiguity remains. In summary, a plural covering different numbers does not necessitate suspension but rather comprehends all individuals to avoid preference without preponderance. However, if there is evidence that not all are intended, then not all are intended. Your example of coins has evidence that not all are intended because obviously a person cannot be liable for all the coins in the world. But we are discussing the absolute general without a contextual indicator, so your example is not valid.

(ii) The second argument was that the general is emphasized by 'all' and 'whole' which indicates that the general does not include all individuals. But we say this actually indicates that the general does include all individuals, because emphasis is brought for a meaning already present in the emphasized thing. If the general did not have generality, emphasizing it with 'all' and 'whole' would not be valid. The validity of such emphasis proves that the general inherently contains generality. So using 'all' and 'whole' as argument is our proof not yours.

(iii) The third argument was that sometimes the plural refers to a single individual, sometimes to more, as in 'The people said to them, indeed the people have gathered against you.' The response is that the plural is originally used for many, but metaphorically it can be used for a single individual. The scholars of language have clarified this. In summary, a single individual is intended metaphorically, while all individuals are intended literally. Thus no ambiguity or commonality remains. And the instance where a single individual is intended is due to a contextual indicator.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about whether the general (عام) term is definitive (qat'i) in indicating all its individuals or is ambiguous (mujmal). The author uses the example of the pregnant widow's 'iddah to demonstrate that the Companions 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud both accepted the generality of the verses, otherwise no conflict would arise. The author then refutes three arguments of those who claim that the general is ambiguous: (1) the example of 'upon the coins' is irrelevant because it has a contextual indicator; (2) emphasis with 'all' actually proves inherent generality; (3) metaphorical use of plural for a single individual does not negate the literal meaning of generality. The passage reaffirms the Hanafi position that 'amm is decisive in indicating all its members unless there is a contextual indicator to the contrary.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A term that linguistically encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict between two textual proofs that cannot both be applied simultaneously without reconciliation.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.
قرينة (qarinah): A contextual indicator that restricts the general meaning.
تأكيد (tawkid): Emphasis; here used as evidence that 'amm already implies generality before emphasis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did both 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud consider the two verses (65:4 and 2:234) to be conflicting regarding the pregnant widow?
A) Because they believed the verses were abrogated.
B) Because they took both verses as general, so they overlapped on pregnant widows.
C) Because they were uncertain about the meaning of the verses.
D) Because they followed different Qur'anic readings.

Key Takeaway
The general term (ʿāmm) in Arabic is decisive and includes all its individuals unless a clear contextual indicator restricts it; this is proven by the Companions' recognition of text conflict and their immediate attempts at reconciliation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Definitiveness of ʿĀmm: Hanafi Refutation of Shāfiʿī and Wāqifī Views
Hanafi refutation of Waqifiyya and Shafiʿi views on ʿāmm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that ʿāmm is qaṭʿī and evaluate the Shāfiʿī and Wāqifī arguments against it using the principles of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The general term is definitive (qaṭʿī) until a clear contextual indicator specifies otherwise.

This passage delves into a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute: is a general term (ʿāmm) definitive or merely apparent? The Hanafi school holds that without a contextual indicator (qarīna), the general encompasses all its individuals with certainty. The Shāfiʿī school and the Wāqifiyya argue that it is open to specification by weaker evidence. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to derive rulings from textual sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Schools and Their Positions
First, note that the text refutes two opposing views: the Wāqifiyya who claim ʿāmm is ambiguous (mujmal), and al-Shāfiʿī who considers it a proof with doubt (shubha). State each position clearly.
The Wāqifiyya suspend judgment on ʿāmm until specification; al-Shāfiʿī allows specification by khabar al-wāḥid or qiyās.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Response to the Wāqifiyya
Examine the three arguments of the Wāqifiyya and the Hanafi rebuttals. Focus on the principle that without a qarīna, the plural must encompass all to avoid arbitrary preference.
The Hanafis argue that emphasis (tawkīd) with 'kull' or 'ajmaʿ' only reinforces the existing generality, not the opposite.
3
Contrast the Hanafi and Shāfiʿī Views on Definitiveness
The text explicitly states: 'عندنا هو قطعي مساو للخاص' (According to us, it is definitive, equivalent to the specific). Understand why Hanafis require a qatʿī proof for specification, while Shāfiʿīs accept zannī evidence.
The key difference lies in whether a mere possibility of specification weakens certainty.
4
Apply the Linguistic Principle
The Hanafi argument rests on the rule: 'When a word is placed for a meaning, that meaning is necessary unless a qarīna indicates otherwise.' Trace how this principle underpins the whole dispute.
This is a qiyās jaliy from the nature of language and legal discourse.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify a concrete example where the difference matters, such as the verse on theft (5:38). Hanafis would not specify it by a solitary report, while Shāfiʿīs would.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is whether a general Quranic verse can be narrowed by a single-narrator hadith.
