غیر مستقل ) یعنی ایسا کلام جس کا تعلق صدر کلام سے ہوگا اور بذات خود وہ نام نہیں ہوگا اور مستقل وہ ہے جو اس طرح نہ ہو برابر ہے کہ کلام ہو یا نہ ہو (اور وہ) یعنی غیر مستقل (استثناء ہے اور شرط ہے اور صفت ہے اور غایت ہے ) پس استثناء واجب کرتا ہے عام کے بند ہونے
Section: Restricting the general to some of what it includes is inevitably either by non-independent (i.e., speech that is attached to the beginning of the statement and is not complete by itself; independent is that which is not like that, whether it is speech or not) or by independent. Non-independent includes: exception, condition, attribute, and limit. Exception necessitates restricting the general to some of its individuals. Condition necessitates restricting the beginning of the statement to some quantities, such as 'You are divorced if you enter the house.' Attribute necessitates restriction to what possesses the attribute, such as 'In pasturing camels there is zakat.' Limit necessitates restriction to the part for which the limit is made a boundary, such as His statement (So wash your faces and your hands up to the elbows), and to what is beyond the limit, such as 'Complete the fast until night.' Or by independent, and that is takhsis (specification). It is either by speech or other. Other includes: reason, as in 'Creator of everything' — it is known necessarily that Allah is excluded; also the specification of the child and the insane from the addresses of Sharia is of this kind. Or by sense, as in 'And she was given of everything.' Or by custom, as in 'He does not eat an animal's head' applies to the customary. Or by some individuals being deficient, so the word applies more to others, as in 'Every slave of mine is free' does not include the mukatab; this is called mushakkal. Or by some individuals being excessive, like 'fruit' does not include grapes. Translation: Section: restricting the general to some of what it includes is inevitably either by non-independent, i.e., speech that is attached to the beginning of the statement and is not a noun by itself; independent is that which is not like that, whether it is speech or not. Non-independent includes: exception, condition, attribute, and limit. So exception necessitates restricting the general.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage is a section heading that defines the concept of 'qasr al-'aam' (restricting a general statement) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It first divides the methods of restriction into two types: non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Non-independent methods are those that are attached to the statement itself and do not form a complete independent sentence. These include: exception (istithna), condition (shart), attribute (sifah), and limit (ghayah). Each is defined with examples: exception excludes some individuals from the general; condition ties the ruling to a contingency; attribute adds a qualification; limit sets a boundary. The independent method is 'takhsis' (specification), which can be done through external evidence such as reason (aql), as in the verse 'Creator of everything' where Allah is excluded, or through sense (hiss), custom (adah), or by considering some individuals as deficient or excessive in relation to the general term. The text includes examples like 'every slave of mine is free' not including the mukatab (a slave who has made a contract for manumission) and 'fruit' not including grapes. This classification is foundational for understanding how general texts in the Quran and Sunnah are to be interpreted and applied, a key feature of Hanafi legal theory.

Key Terms
قصر العام (qasr al-'aam): Restricting a general term to only some of its potential referents.
استثناء (istithna): An exception that excludes a part from the general rule.
شرط (shart): A condition added to a statement that restricts its application to when that condition is met.
صفة (sifah): An attribute that limits the general to those possessing that attribute.
غاية (ghayah): A limit that marks a boundary for the ruling.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term by independent evidence, including reason, sense, custom, or intrinsic deficiency/excess.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered a non-independent method of restricting a general statement?
A) Takhsis by reason.
B) Istithna (exception).
C) Takhsis by custom.
D) Takhsis by sense.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a general statement can be restricted both by non-independent means (exception, condition, attribute, limit) and by independent means (reason, sense, custom, inherent deficiency/excess).

Classification of Restrictors (Takhsis al-'Amm) into Independent and Non-Independent
Classification of restrictors into dependent and independent types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main categories of restrictors (ghayr mustaqill and mustaqill) and apply the Hanafi rule that only qat'i restrictors can remove the definitiveness of a general term.

Core Idea
Restrictors are either speech-dependent (exception, condition, adjective, limit) or independent (intellect, sense, custom, deficiency/excess preference).

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi classification of how a general term ('amm) can be restricted. The passage distinguishes between restrictors that depend on the preceding speech (ghayr mustaqill) and those that stand alone (mustaqill). You will learn the four types of dependent restrictors and five types of independent restrictors, with examples from the Qur'an and customary usage. This classification is essential for correctly applying the principle that 'amm remains qat'i until a definitive restrictor is found.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two broad categories
The passage divides restrictors into non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Non-independent restrictors are clauses that cannot stand alone; independent restrictors are separate evidence.
Ghayr mustaqill includes exception, condition, adjective, and limit.
2
Enumerate the non-independent restrictors
List the four: exception (istithna'), condition (shart), adjective (sifa), and limit (ghaya). For each, note how it restricts: exception removes individuals, condition ties the ruling to a circumstance, adjective isolates those with the attribute, limit sets an endpoint.
Examples: 'you are divorced if you enter' (condition), 'on grazing camels zakat' (adjective).
3
Enumerate the independent restrictors
List the five: intellect ('aql), sense (hiss), custom ('urf), deficiency (nuqsan), and excess (ziyada). Intellect includes necessary exceptions like 'Creator of everything' excluding Allah; sense limits to what is perceptible; custom relies on common usage; deficiency and excess relate to word usage.
E.g., 'every slave of mine is free' does not include mukatab (deficiency).
4
Understand the Hanafi requirement of definitiveness
In Hanafi usul, 'amm is qat'i until a definitive (qat'i) restrictor is found. All these restrictors must be definitive in transmission and meaning to override the general.
This contrasts with the Mutakallimin view that 'amm is zanni.
5
Apply the classification to a textual example
Take the verse 'wash your faces and hands to the elbows' (al-Ma'idah:6). Identify 'to the elbows' as a ghaya (limit), a non-independent restrictor, and explain how it restricts the general 'hands' to only up to the elbows.
This demonstrates practical application of takhsis.

Chapter: Restricting the general to some of its individuals [that it includes] is not free from the fact that [the restrictor] will be either non-independent, i.e., speech that is related to the introductory speech and is not itself a noun, and independent is that which is not like that, whether it is speech or not. And the non-independent are: exception, condition, adjective, and limit. So exception causes the general to be restricted to some of its individuals; condition causes the introductory speech to be restricted to some probabilities, like 'you are divorced if you enter the house'; adjective causes restriction to those individuals in which the adjective is found, like 'on grazing camels zakat'; and limit causes restriction to those individuals for which the limit is made a boundary, like the Almighty's saying 'wash your faces and hands to the elbows', and regarding what is beyond the limit, like 'complete the fast until night'. Or [the restrictor] will be independent, and that is specification (takhsis), and it is either by speech or by other than speech. That other than speech is either intellect, like 'Creator of everything' – it is known necessarily that Allah Almighty is excluded from it, and specifying the child and the insane from the addresses of the Shariah is of this type; or sense, like 'and she was given of everything'; or custom, like 'he does not eat a head' applies to the customary [type]; or some individuals being deficient, so the word applies more to the other individuals, like 'every slave of mine is free' does not apply to the mukatab, and it is called mushakkal; or some individuals being excessive, like fruit does not apply to grapes. [These are] the ways of restricting the general to some individuals.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tawdih (commented upon by Al-Talwih) explains the methods by which a general term ('amm) can be restricted (takhsis) to some of its individuals. The commentator first defines two broad categories of restrictors: non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Non-independent restrictors are clauses that depend on the preceding speech and cannot stand alone. They include: 1) exception (istithna'), which excludes individuals from the general; 2) condition (shart), which limits the application to a specific circumstance; 3) adjective (sifa), which restricts to individuals possessing that attribute; and 4) limit (ghaya), which defines an endpoint. The author gives examples for each: exception: 'you are divorced if you enter the house' (condition restricts the divorce to entry); adjective: 'on grazing camels zakat' (only grazing camels); limit: 'wash your faces and hands to the elbows' (elbows are the limit; beyond is not included) and 'complete the fast until night' (after night, no fast). The independent restrictors are those that do not depend on the preceding speech. They include: 1) intellect (aql): e.g., 'Creator of everything' necessarily excludes Allah Himself; similarly, children and the insane are excluded from legal addresses by rational necessity. 2) sense (hiss): e.g., 'she was given of everything' (but obviously not everything). 3) custom (urf): e.g., 'he does not eat a head' is understood based on customary usage. 4) the word being more appropriate for some individuals due to deficiency: e.g., 'every slave of mine is free' does not include a mukatab (slave under contract) because he is not a full slave; such terms are called 'mutashabbih' (ambiguous). 5) the word being more appropriate for others due to excess: e.g., 'fruit' does not usually include grapes in some contexts. The passage emphasizes that the general remains qat'i (definitive) until restricted by a definitive proof, and these methods clarify how restriction operates.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A word that encompasses all individuals within its scope without restriction.
تخصیص (takhsis): The act of restricting a general term to some of its individuals.
غیر مستقل (ghayr mustaqill): A clause that depends on preceding speech and cannot form an independent statement.
مستقل (mustaqill): An independent indicator that can stand alone, such as intellect, sense, or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is considered a non-independent restrictor (ghayr mustaqill) for a general term?
A) Intellect ('aql)
B) Exception (istithna')
C) Custom ('urf)
D) Sense (hiss)

Key Takeaway
The restriction of a general term takes specific forms — either speech-dependent (exception, condition, adjective, limit) or independent (intellect, sense, custom, deficiency, excess) — and each must be definitive to override the default inclusiveness.

Non-Independent Methods of Takhsis: Istithna', Shart, Sifat, and Ghayah
Enumeration of four attached specification methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four non-independent methods of takhsis and apply them to determine the scope of a general term.

Core Idea
Takhsis of a general term occurs through attached qualifiers: exception, condition, description, and limit.

In usul al-fiqh, a general term ('amm) includes all its individuals unless specified. Specification (takhsis) can be achieved through various means. The commentator first distinguishes between non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill) methods. This lesson focuses on the four non-independent methods: istithna', shart, sifat, and ghayah. Each attaches to the original statement and restricts its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of takhsis methods
The passage divides methods into non-independent (attached to the original statement) and independent (not attached). Recognize that non-independent methods cannot stand alone in meaning.
Ghayr mustaqill depends on the sadr kalam (prior statement) for its full meaning.
2
Define each non-independent method
Istithna' (exception) removes individuals using words like 'illa. Shart (condition) makes the ruling contingent. Sifat (description) limits to those possessing a quality. Ghayah (limit) marks an endpoint.
Ghayah has two subtypes depending on whether the limit is of the same genus.
3
Examine the examples in the passage
For istithna': 'اقتلوا المشركين إلا أهل الذمة'. For shart: 'أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار'. For sifat: 'في الإبل السائمة زكوة'. For ghayah: 'إلى المرافق' (same genus) and 'إلى الليل' (different genus).
Note how each example restricts the general term to a subset.
4
Understand the function of ghayah's two forms
When the limit is of the same genus (e.g., 'إلى المرافق'), it excludes beyond the limit. When it is not (e.g., 'إلى الليل'), it includes up to but not beyond the limit, effectively restricting to the opposite.
5
Apply the method to a new general statement
Given a general ruling like 'أكرم الطلاب' (honor the students), add a condition 'إن نجحوا' (if they pass). The ruling now only applies to passing students.

Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a usul al-fiqh matn discussing the methods (turuq) of specifying a general term ('amm). The commentator begins by recalling the matn's earlier statement: a general term includes all its individuals with certainty until a definitive proof of specification appears. Now, the matn proceeds to explain what happens when specification does occur. The commentator first lists the possible means of restricting the general to some of its parts, dividing them into two main categories: non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Non-independent means are those that are attached to the original statement and cannot stand alone; these are four: istithna' (exception), shart (condition), sifat (description), and ghayah (limit). Each is explained with examples from the Quran and legal rulings. Istithna' removes certain individuals, e.g., 'قتلوا المشركين إلا أهل الذمة' (kill the polytheists except the dhimmi). Shart restricts the ruling to a specific scenario, e.g., 'أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار' (you are divorced if you enter the house). Sifat limits to those possessing a quality, e.g., 'في الإبل السائمة زكوة' (on grazing camels is zakat). Ghayah has two forms: when the limit is of the same genus (e.g., 'إلى المرافق' in ablution, which excludes beyond the elbows), and when it is not (e.g., 'إلى الليل' for fasting, which restricts the fast to daytime only). The independent category (mustaqill) includes that which is not attached to the original statement; it can be independent speech (kalam), like the verse 'وإن أحد من المشركين استجارك فأجره' which specifies who is excluded from the general command to kill polytheists. Or it can be non-speech (ghayr kalam), which includes five sub-types: 'aql (reason, e.g., 'الله خالق كل شيء' is understood by reason to exclude Allah Himself), hiss (senses), 'adah (custom), naqis (deficiency, e.g., 'كل مملوك لي فهو حر' does not include a mukatab slave), and za'id (excess, e.g., 'فاكهة' does not include grapes). The passage systematically presents these methods, emphasizing that the general term is only truly general until specified, and the specification must be valid.

Key Terms
عام ('Amm): A term that is general, covering all its individuals unless specified.
تخصيص (Takhsis): The act of restricting a general term to some of its individuals.
غير مستقل (Ghayr Mustaqill): That which is dependent on a prior statement (sadr kalam) for its meaning, such as istithna', shart, sifat, and ghayah.
استثناء (Istithna'): Exception; a particle that removes part of the general term, e.g., 'illa'.
شرط (Shart): Condition; a clause that makes the ruling contingent on its fulfillment.
صفت (Sifat): Description; a qualifying adjective that limits the general to individuals possessing that quality.
غایت (Ghayah): Limit; a term indicating an endpoint or boundary, often with 'ila'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a non-independent method of takhsis?
A) Istithna' (exception)
B) Shart (condition)
C) Sifat (description)
D) 'Aql (reason)

Key Takeaway
The four non-independent methods of takhsis—istithna', shart, sifat, and ghayah— are attached to the original statement and restrict a general term to a subset of its individuals.

Independent Methods of Takhsis: Speech and Non-Speech
Classification of independent specification methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the independent methods of takhsis (speech and non-speech) and apply them to cases where the specifying factor is not attached to the original statement.

Core Idea
Specification of a general term can be achieved by an independent text or by reason, senses, custom, deficiency, or excess.

After discussing non-independent methods, the passage turns to independent methods (mustaqill) of takhsis. These are not attached to the original statement and can stand alone. They are divided into two categories: independent speech (kalam mustaqill) and independent non-speech (ghayr kalam). The latter includes five sub-types: 'aql (reason), hiss (senses), 'adah (custom), naqis (deficiency), and za'id (excess). This lesson explains these methods with examples.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between independent and non-independent methods
Independent methods are not attached to the original statement; they provide specification from outside. Recognize that they can be words or non-verbal factors.
Independent speech is a separate verse or hadith that restricts a general ruling.
2
Understand the first subcategory: Independent speech
Example from the passage: the general command 'اقتلوا المشركين' is specified by the independent verse 'وإن أحد من المشركين استجارك فأجره' (if a polytheist seeks asylum, grant it). This independent verse excludes those seeking asylum from the general kill command.
The specifying text is a standalone revelation, not an attached clause.
3
Learn the second subcategory: Independent non-speech
The passage lists five types: 'aql (reason), hiss (senses), 'adah (custom), naqis (deficiency), za'id (excess). Each restricts the general via an external factor.
These are not linguistic but practical or conceptual.
4
Analyze the example of 'aql
The general term 'كل شيء' (everything) in 'الله خالق كل شيء' (Allah is the Creator of everything) includes even Allah Himself, but reason (‘aql) dictates that Allah cannot be His own creation, so the general is specified to exclude Allah's essence and attributes.
This shows that reason can serve as a valid mukhassis.
5
Examine other non-speech types
Though not elaborated in this passage, examples: hiss (senses) like sight specifies that 'everything' in a visual context excludes invisible things; 'adah (custom) like 'we eat food' excludes sand; naqis (deficiency) like a slave's ownership is deficient; za'id (excess) like 'fruit' excludes nutritious but non-fruit items.
These are less common but valid in usul.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a usul al-fiqh matn discussing the methods (turuq) of specifying a general term ('amm). The commentator begins by recalling the matn's earlier statement: a general term includes all its individuals with certainty until a definitive proof of specification appears. Now, the matn proceeds to explain what happens when specification does occur. The commentator first lists the possible means of restricting the general to some of its parts, dividing them into two main categories: non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Non-independent means are those that are attached to the original statement and cannot stand alone; these are four: istithna' (exception), shart (condition), sifat (description), and ghayah (limit). Each is explained with examples from the Quran and legal rulings. Istithna' removes certain individuals, e.g., 'قتلوا المشركين إلا أهل الذمة' (kill the polytheists except the dhimmi). Shart restricts the ruling to a specific scenario, e.g., 'أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار' (you are divorced if you enter the house). Sifat limits to those possessing a quality, e.g., 'في الإبل السائمة زكوة' (on grazing camels is zakat). Ghayah has two forms: when the limit is of the same genus (e.g., 'إلى المرافق' in ablution, which excludes beyond the elbows), and when it is not (e.g., 'إلى الليل' for fasting, which restricts the fast to daytime only). The independent category (mustaqill) includes that which is not attached to the original statement; it can be independent speech (kalam), like the verse 'وإن أحد من المشركين استجارك فأجره' which specifies who is excluded from the general command to kill polytheists. Or it can be non-speech (ghayr kalam), which includes five sub-types: 'aql (reason, e.g., 'الله خالق كل شيء' is understood by reason to exclude Allah Himself), hiss (senses), 'adah (custom), naqis (deficiency, e.g., 'كل مملوك لي فهو حر' does not include a mukatab slave), and za'id (excess, e.g., 'فاكهة' does not include grapes). The passage systematically presents these methods, emphasizing that the general term is only truly general until specified, and the specification must be valid.

Key Terms
عام ('Amm): A term that is general, covering all its individuals unless specified.
تخصيص (Takhsis): The act of restricting a general term to some of its individuals.
مستقل (Mustaqill): That which is independent, not requiring attachment to another statement for its own meaning.
عقل ('Aql): Reason; a rational proof that can specify a general term when textual evidence is general but reason dictates limitation.
حس (Hiss): Senses; perceptual evidence that can specify a general term, e.g., sight limits 'every visible thing'.
عادة ('Adah): Custom; prevailing practice that can specify a general term, e.g., 'food' excludes stones by custom.
ناقص (Naqis): Deficiency; a factor that limits because the subject lacks full capacity, e.g., a slave's ownership is deficient.
زائد (Za'id): Excess; an additional element that excludes what is normally included, e.g., 'fruit' excludes dates if excess is present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of independent speech method of takhsis?
A) 'اقتلوا المشركين' specified by 'إلا أهل الذمة'
B) 'الله خالق كل شيء' specified by 'aql
C) 'اقتلوا المشركين' specified by 'وإن أحد من المشركين استجارك فأجره'
D) 'أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار'

Key Takeaway
Independent methods of takhsis include separate texts and non-verbal factors like reason, senses, and custom, each capable of restricting a general term from outside the original statement.

Four Types of Connected Restrictives
Classifies and exemplifies the four muttasil mukhassisat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify each of the four connected restrictives (mukhassisat muttasila) and correctly apply them to specify a general term ('amm) in Quranic and juristic examples.

Core Idea
Connected restrictives narrow a general term within the same utterance and are four: exception, condition, adjective, and limit.

In Hanafi usul, a general term ('amm) can be restricted by a 'connected' (muttasil) qualifier—part of the same speech. This lesson unpacks the four categories: istithna', shart, sifat, and ghayah, each with distinct mechanisms. Understanding these is essential for correctly deriving rulings from primary texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the passage, list the four types of muttasil mukhassisat: exception (istithna'), condition (shart), adjective (sifat), and limit (ghayah).
2
Understand each mechanism
For each type, note how it restricts the general: exception excludes individuals; condition restricts to a circumstance; adjective restricts to bearers of the attribute; limit either excludes beyond or marks an endpoint.
Focus on the example given for each type.
3
Distinguish the two forms of ghayah
Ghayah has two subtypes: when the limit is of the same genus (min jins) as the limited term, it excludes beyond; when not of the same genus, it sets the endpoint without exclusion.
Example: 'to the elbows' (same genus) vs 'until night' (different genus).
4
Apply to a new example
Given a new general statement with a connected restrictor (e.g., 'Free the believing slaves' — 'believing' is sifat), identify the 'amm, the restrictor type, and the resulting restricted meaning.
This solidifies the analytical skill.

Source Text

مستقل ہو تو اس کی چار اقتسام ہیں استثناء شرط صفت اور غایت۔ ان میں سے استثناء عام کو اس کے بعض افراد پر محصور کر دیتا ہے اس کی مثال جیسے اقتلوا المشركين الا اهل الذمة خواه ذمی ہوں یا غیر ذمی لیکن اہل الذمة نے اس حکم کو بعض افراد یعنی غیر ذمی ہونے پر محصور کر دیا۔ اور شرط کسی کلام (جو عام ہو) کو اس کی بعض صورتوں کے ساتھ خاص کر دیتی ہے جیسے انت طالق ان دخلت الدار۔ یہاں انت طالق کا حکم تمام صورتوں میں عام تھا لیکن ان دخلت الدار شرط نے اس حکم کو بعض صورتوں کے ساتھ خاص کر دیا اور وہ صورت ہے دخول دار والی۔ اور صفت عام کو ان افراد میں محصور کرتی ہے جن افراد میں وہ صفت پائی جاتی ہے جیسے فی الابل السائمة زکوة۔ یہاں الابل عام تھا اور زکوۃ کا حکم ابل کے تمام افراد کو شامل تھا خواہ وہ چرنے والے ہوں یا گھر میں رہ کر چارہ کھانے والے ہوں لیکن السائمہ صفت نے اس حکم کو ابل کے ان افراد میں محصور کر دیا جن میں السائمہ والی صفت پائی جاتی ہے یعنی چرنے والے اونٹوں میں۔ اور غایت کی دو صورتیں ہیں بعض صورتوں میں یہ مغیی کی جنس میں سے ہوتی ہے اور اس وقت یہ مغیی کے حکم کو غایت کے ماوراء سے ساقط کر دیتی ہے تو یہ غایت عام کو انہی افراد میں محصور کر دیتی ہے جن کے لیے اس کو حد بنایا گیا ہوتا ہے جیسے فاغسلوا وجوهكم وايديكم الى المرافق۔ یہاں المرافق ایدی کی جنس سے ہے اور یہاں یہ المرافق کے ماوراء کو حکم سے ساقط کرنے کے لیے ہے اس لیے یہاں ایدیکم چونکہ عام تھا اور غسل کا حکم ہاتھ کی انگلیوں سے لے کر بغل تک کو شامل تھا لیکن الی المرافق نے اس کو انگلیوں سے لے کر کہنی سمیت تک محصور کر دیا کہنی سے بغل والے حصے کو اس حکم سے خارج کر دیا۔ اور بعض دفعہ غایت مغیی کی جنس میں سے نہیں ہوتی اور اس وقت یہ حکم کی انتہاء کے لیے آتی ہے تو یہ غایت عام کو غایت کے ماوراء افراد میں محصور کر دیتی ہے جیسے ثم اتموا الصيام الى اللیل۔ یہاں لیل صیام کی جنس میں سے نہیں ہے اس لیے چونکہ روزہ کو پورا کرنے والا حکم پہلے عام تھا تو الی اللیل نے آکر اس کو لیل کے ماوراء یعنی نہار کے ساتھ خاص کر دیا۔
If it is connected, then it has four divisions: exception, condition, adjective, and limit. Among them, exception restricts the general to some of its individuals, like 'kill the polytheists except the people of the covenant' – whether they are dhimmis or non-dhimmis, but the people of the covenant restricts the ruling to non-dhimmis. Condition specifies a general statement to some of its situations, like 'you are divorced if you enter the house' – the ruling of divorce was general to all situations, but the condition restricts it to the situation of entering the house. Adjective restricts the general to those individuals that possess that adjective, like 'on grazing camels, zakat' – camels were general, but the adjective 'grazing' restricts it to grazing camels. Limit has two forms: sometimes it is of the same genus as the limited term, like 'wash your faces and hands up to the elbows' – elbows are of the same genus as hands, so it restricts the washing to up to the elbows, excluding beyond. Sometimes it is not of the same genus, like 'complete the fast until night' – night is not of the genus of fasting, so it sets the endpoint, restricting the general ruling of completing the fast to the daytime.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage defines the four types of connected restrictives (mukhassisat muttasila) that specify a general term ('amm) within the same utterance. The first is istithna' (exception), which excludes some individuals from the general ruling, as in the Quranic verse 'kill the polytheists except the people of the covenant' – here the exception restricts the general command to non-dhimmis. The second is shart (condition), which restricts a general ruling to a specific circumstance, as in the divorce conditional on entering the house. The third is sifat (adjective/adjective clause), which restricts the general to those bearing the attribute, as in 'grazing camels' excluding non-grazing ones from zakat. The fourth is ghayah (limit/terminus), which has two subtypes: when the limit is of the same genus as the general term, it excludes what is beyond the limit (e.g., washing up to the elbows excludes the upper arm); when it is not of the same genus, it marks the end point (e.g., fasting until night excludes night from the fasting period). The author illustrates each with clear Quranic or juristic examples, showing how specification operates in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): A grammatical exception that excludes some individuals from the general ruling.
شرط (sharṭ): A condition that restricts a general ruling to the occurrence of that condition.
صفت (ṣifat): An adjective or description that restricts the general to individuals possessing that attribute.
غایت (ghāyah): A limit or terminus that restricts the general ruling either by excluding beyond or marking an endpoint.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four connected restrictives (mukhassisat muttasila) mentioned in the passage?
A) Exception (istithna')
B) Condition (shart)
C) Custom ('adah)
D) Adjective (sifat)

Key Takeaway
Connected restrictives—exception, condition, adjective, and limit—narrow a general term within the same utterance; correctly identifying them is essential for accurate legal interpretation.

Takhsis by Intellect ('Aql)
Explains how intellect restricts a general term without external text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which intellect ('aql) can specify a general term (takhsis bi-l-'aql) and apply this principle to a new Quranic verse.

Core Idea
Intellect specifies a general term when literal interpretation leads to rational absurdity.

This lesson introduces a distinctive principle of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: specification by rational necessity (takhsis bi-l-'aql). The passage explains that when a general expression (amm) appears in a text, but its literal scope includes something logically impossible, human intellect can restrict that general to exclude the absurd. The classic example is the verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' – intellect excludes Allah's own essence and attributes from being created.

Guided Path
1
Locate the general term (amm)
Identify the word 'كل شيء' in the verse 'الله خالق كل شيء' from Surah al-Zumar (39:62).
This is the term that is general in form.
2
Test the literal scope
If taken literally, 'everything' includes all things, including Allah's essence and attributes.
3
Detect logical impossibility
Including the Creator in 'everything created' would imply self-creation, which is impossible (takhliq al-shay' li nafsih).
This impossibility triggers the need for specification.
4
Apply the intellect
Intellect blocks this absurdity by specifying the general to exclude Allah's essence and attributes, restricting it to creatures.
The specification is based on rational necessity, not on another text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور دوسرا احتمال تھا کہ عام کو بعض افراد میں منحصر کرنے والی چیز مستقل ہو اور یہ تخصیص بھی ہے اس میں پھر دو احتمال ہیں کہ وہ مستقل کلام ہوگی یا کلام کے علاوہ کوئی اور چیز ہوگی۔ کلام ہو جیسا کہ ارشاد باری ہے فاقتلوا المشركين من حيث وجدتموهم قتل کا حکم تمام مشرکین کو عام تھا دوسری آیت نے وان احد من المشرکین استجارک فاجرہ کہ مشرکین میں سے کوئی اگر تم سے پناہ چاہے تو اس کو پناہ دے دو یہ آیت مستقل ہے اور کلام ہے اور اس آیت نے قتل والے حکم میں سے ان مشرکین کو خاص کر دیا جو پناہ طلب کر لیں۔ لہذا عام باقی افراد میں محصور ہو گیا۔ اور اگر وہ مستقل غیر کلام ہو تو اس میں پانچ صورتیں ہیں (i) عام کو بعض افراد میں محصور کرنے والی چیز عقل ہو جیسے اللہ خالق کل شئی۔ یہاں کل شئی عام ہے ہر شے کو شامل ہے خود ذات وصفات باری تعالیٰ کو بھی شامل ہے لیکن عقل یہ حکم لگاتی ہے کہ کل شئی میں ذات وصفات باری تعالی داخل نہیں ہیں کیونکہ اگر داخل ہوں تو اللہ تعالیٰ کا اپنی ذات وصفات کا خالق ہونا لازم آئے گا اور یہ تخلیق الشیء لنفسہ ہے جو باطل ہے تو یہاں عقل نے عام (کل شئی) کو اللہ کی ذات وصفات کے علاوہ دوسرے افراد میں محصور کر دیا۔
And the second possibility is that the thing restricting the general to some individuals is independent, and this is also specification. Then there are two possibilities: it may be independent speech or something other than speech. If it is speech, like the divine command: 'kill the polytheists wherever you find them' – the ruling of killing was general to all polytheists; another verse says: 'and if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection' – this verse is independent and is speech, and it specifies from the killing ruling those polytheists who seek protection. So the general becomes restricted to the remaining individuals. And if it is independent and non-speech, then there are five forms: (i) The thing restricting the general to some individuals may be intellect, like 'Allah is the Creator of everything.' Here 'everything' is general, encompassing all things, including the essence and attributes of Allah the Exalted. But intellect rules that the essence and attributes of Allah are not included in 'everything', because if they were included, it would necessitate that Allah is the creator of His own essence and attributes, which is 'creating a thing from itself', which is invalid. So here intellect restricted the general ('everything') to individuals other than Allah's essence and attributes.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage introduces independent (munfasil) restrictors, beginning with a classification: either independent speech (other verses) or non-speech. The non-speech category has five types, the first being 'aql (intellect). The example is the verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' (al-Zumar 39:62). Intellect dictates that Allah's own essence and attributes cannot be created, so intellect restricts the general term 'everything' to exclude the Divine essence and attributes. This shows that rational necessity can override the apparent generality of a text. This is a distinctive Hanafi usul principle, allowing reason as a valid mukhassis.

Key Terms
تخصیص بالعقل (takhṣīṣ bi-l-ʿaql): Specification of a general term by rational necessity, excluding what is logically impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does intellect exclude Allah's essence and attributes from the general term 'everything' in the verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything'?
A) Because the Prophet said so
B) Because including them would imply that Allah creates Himself, which is impossible
C) Because the word 'everything' is ambiguous
D) Because consensus excludes them

Key Takeaway
Intellect ('aql) is a valid independent mukhassis in Hanafi usul when the literal scope of a general term leads to rational impossibility.

Takhsis by Sensory Observation (Hiss) – A Non-Textual Mukhassis
Explains specification by empirical observation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when sensory observation can serve as a mukhassis for a general term and distinguish it from textual specification.

Core Idea
Empirical observation can restrict a general Quranic term if it contradicts reality, even without specific text.

In Hanafi usul, a general text (amm) can be specified by independent evidence that is not part of the Quran or Sunnah. One such non-textual mukhassis is sensory observation (hiss wa mushahadah). This lesson examines how empirical knowledge about the Queen of Sheba restricts the general phrase 'given of everything' to exclude prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term (amm)
Locate the word or phrase that has a general meaning (umum). In the Quranic verse about Queen Bilqis, the phrase 'everything' (kull shay') is the amm.
The amm here is 'kull shay' which literally covers all things.
2
Recognize the empirical fact
Determine what sensory observation (hiss) tells us about the specific case. Observation of the Muslim community confirms that Bilqis was not a prophet.
This is a historical fact known through tawatur or consensus of historians, not through revelation.
3
Apply the restriction (takhsis)
Because the empirical fact contradicts the literal inclusion of prophethood under 'everything', sensory observation serves as a mukhassis: it excludes prophethood from the general term.
This is a valid takhsis even without a specific textual exemption.
4
Contrast with textual specification
Understand that this differs from takhsis by a separate text (e.g., Quran or hadith). Here, the mukhassis is not a revealed statement but an observable reality.
Hanafi usul accepts this because empirical certainty overrides literal generality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ii) یا وہ مستقل شئی حس اور مشاہدہ ہوگی جیسے ملکہ بلقیس کے بارے میں قرآن پاک میں ارشاد ہے واوتیت من كل شئی۔ یہاں کل شئی میں تمام چیزیں داخل ہیں حتی کہ نبوت بھی داخل ہے لیکن امتوں کے مشاہدے سے ثابت ہے کہ اس کو نبوت نہیں ملی تھی تو یہاں کل شئی میں نبوت داخل نہیں ہے اب یہاں حس اور مشاہدہ نے کل شئی کے بعض افراد یعنی نبوت کو اس حکم سے خاص اور خارج کر دیا۔
(ii) Or that independent thing may be sense and observation, like concerning the Queen of Sheba, the Holy Quran says: 'and she was given of everything.' Here 'everything' includes all things, even prophethood is included. But it is established by the observation of the community that she was not given prophethood. So here 'everything' does not include prophethood. Thus sense and observation specified 'everything' by excluding prophethood from this ruling.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
The second type of independent non-speech restrictor is hiss wa mushahadah (sensory observation). The example is the Quranic statement about the Queen of Sheba (Bilqis) in Surah al-Naml 27:23: 'and she was given of everything.' Literally, 'everything' is general and would include prophethood. However, historical observation confirms she was not a prophet. Therefore, sense/observation restricts the general term 'everything' to exclude prophethood. This demonstrates that empirical knowledge can serve as a mukhassis.

Key Terms
تخصیص بالحس (takhṣīṣ bi-l-ḥiss): Specification of a general term by sensory evidence, excluding what is empirically false.
حس و مشاہدہ (ḥiss wa mushāhadah): Sensory observation or empirical evidence that is certain (e.g., historical facts known through tawatur).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is prophethood excluded from 'everything' given to the Queen of Sheba?
A) Because the Quran explicitly says so
B) Because observation shows she was not a prophet
C) Because general terms never include prophethood
D) Because consensus excludes it

Key Takeaway
Sensory observation (hiss wa mushahadah) is a valid mukhassis in Hanafi usul, allowing empirical facts to restrict general terms when they conflict.

Specification by Custom ('Adah) in Hanafi Usul
Explains specification by prevalent custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of takhṣīṣ bi-l-ʿādah to specify a general term in oaths and identify its conditions.

Core Idea
Custom (ʿādah) restricts general terms in law to their customary scope.

In Hanafi usul, a general term (ʿāmm) can be specified by factors beyond the text itself. One such factor is prevalent custom (ʿādah). This lesson examines how custom narrows the application of an oath, as illustrated by the example of eating a 'head'. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly interpreting oaths and contracts in light of common practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term
Locate the general word in the utterance — in the example, 'ra's' (head) — and note its literal range covering all animal heads.
The general term is 'amm shumuli, including every individual of its kind.
2
Assess the custom
Determine whether a prevalent custom (ʿurf ʿāmm) exists in that context that limits the term to a subset. In the example, only certain animal heads (sheep, goat, buffalo) are customarily eaten.
Custom must be general, consistent, and not contradicted by a stronger evidence.
3
Apply specification (takhsis)
The custom narrows the general term to its customary referents. The non-customary individuals (e.g., sparrow heads) are excluded from the legal effect of the oath.
Thus, eating a sparrow's head does not break the oath because it is outside the custom.
4
Derive the ruling
The resulting ruling: the speaker is not considered ḥānith (oath-breaker) for eating a non-customary head. This shows the legal consequence of takhsis bi-l-ʿādah.
Custom functions as a mukhassis in Hanafi usul, similar to a textual indicator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(iii) یا وہ شئی عادت ہوگی جیسے کوئی آدمی کہے لا ياكل راسا اب ویسے تو راسا عام ہے ہر جاندار کے سر کو شامل ہے لیکن عادتا ہر شئی کا سر کھایا ہی نہیں جاتا بلکہ انہی سروں کو کھایا جاتا ہے جو تنور میں بھونے جاتے ہوں مثلاً بھیڑ، بکری، بھینس وغیرہ کا سر اس لیے یہاں راسا سے مراد بھی یہی سر ہوں گے تو یہاں عادت نے راسا (عام) کو اس کے بعض افراد پر محصور کر دیا اور باقی افراد کو اس عدم اکل والے حکم سے خارج کر دیا لہذا اگر متکلم چڑیا وغیرہ کے سر کو کھالے گا تو حانث نہ ہو گا۔
(iii) Or that thing may be custom, like a man says: 'I will not eat a head.' Now, 'a head' is general, including the head of every living creature. But customarily, not every head is eaten; rather, only those heads that are roasted in an oven, e.g., sheep, goat, buffalo, etc. So here 'head' refers only to these heads. Thus custom restricted the general term 'head' to some of its individuals and excluded the remaining from the ruling of not eating. Therefore, if the speaker eats the head of a sparrow, etc., he will not have broken his oath.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
The third type of independent non-speech restrictor is 'adah (custom). The example is an oath: 'I will not eat a head.' The word 'head' is general, covering all animal heads. However, customary practice ('urf) in that society only considers certain heads (like those of sheep, goats, buffalo roasted) as edible. Hence, the general term is customarily restricted to those heads, and eating a sparrow's head would not violate the oath. This illustrates how custom can specify a general term in legal contexts, such as oaths and contracts.

Key Terms
تخصیص بالعادة (takhṣīṣ bi-l-ʿādah): Specification of a general term by prevalent custom, limiting its application to what is customary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person swears 'I will not eat a head,' and then eats a sparrow's head, why is he not considered to have broken his oath?
A) Because sparrow heads are not meat
B) Because custom only considers certain animal heads as 'heads' for eating
C) Because the word 'head' is ambiguous
D) Because the person did not specify

Key Takeaway
Custom (ʿādah) is a valid and independent mukhassis in Hanafi usul, narrowing general terms to their customary scope.

Takhsis by Deficiency: When Incomplete Ownership Excludes from a General Ruling
Explains specification due to incomplete ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a case of takhsis bi-l-nuqsan in a general text and explain why deficiency of a characteristic (ownership) excludes an individual from the ruling.

Core Idea
Deficiency in a quality that completes the general term can serve as a cause for specification (takhsis).

In Hanafi usul, general words include all individuals that fit the definition. However, when some individuals lack a necessary attribute for the ruling, they are automatically excluded. This lesson explores the fourth type of independent mukhasis: deficiency (nuqsan) in some individuals, using the example of a master's declaration that all his slaves are free, where the mukatab is not freed due to incomplete ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term and its individuals
Look at the general term 'mamluk' (slave) in the master's declaration. It includes three categories: full slaves (mamluk mutlaq), mudabbar (slaves promised freedom upon master's death), and mukatab (slaves under contract to purchase their freedom).
The general term covers all these individuals prima facie.
2
Recognize the attribute required for the ruling
The ruling of freedom is conditional on complete ownership by the master. The declaration applies to 'every slave I own' – complete ownership is implicit.
3
Identify the individual deficient in that attribute
Among the three, the mukatab has a deficient ownership status because the mukatab owns his own earnings. Thus, the master's ownership over the mukatab is incomplete.
Proof: earnings of mukatab belong to him, not the master.
4
Derive the specification (takhsis) due to deficiency
Because the mukatab lacks complete ownership by the master, he is excluded from the general ruling of freedom. This exclusion is not due to an external text but due to the intrinsic deficiency in the individual.
The cause (illah) is the deficiency itself.
5
Confirm the cause is intrinsic deficiency
The deficiency is a quality inherent in the mukatab's status, not something added by context. Hence, it is a valid independent mukhasis in Hanafi usul.
Other schools may require an explicit textual exclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(iv) بعض اوقات عام کے بعض افراد کا ناقص ہونا بھی تخصیص کا سبب بن جاتا ہے جیسے کوئی آدمی کہے کل مملوک لی فهو حر مملوک میں غلام، مدبر، مکاتب سب شامل ہیں لیکن ان سے مدبر وغیرہ میں تو ملکیت کامل ہے لیکن مکاتب میں ملکیت ناقص ہے اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کے مکاسب اس کی ملک ہوتے ہیں مالک کی ملک نہیں ہوتے تو محل مملوک لی فهو حر میں مکاتب داخل نہیں ہوگا اور اس کا سبب مکاتب میں ملکیت کا ناقص ہوتا ہے اس لیے یہ آزاد نہیں ہوگا۔ تو یہاں عام کی تخصیص کا سبب اس کے بعض افراد کا ناقص ہونا بن رہا ہے۔
(iv) Sometimes the deficiency of some individuals of the general also becomes a cause of specification, like a man says: 'Every slave I own is free.' In 'slave' are included the absolute slave, the mudabbar (slave promised freedom upon master's death), and the mukatab (slave under contract of manumission). But among these, the mudabbar etc. have complete ownership (by the master), while the mukatab has incomplete ownership (by the master). And the proof is that the earnings of the mukatab belong to him, not to the master. Therefore, in the expression 'every slave I own is free,' the mukatab is not included, and the cause is the deficiency of ownership in the mukatab. Thus, he will not be freed. So here the cause of specification of the general is the deficiency of some of its individuals.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
The fourth type of independent non-speech restrictor is nuqsan (deficiency) in some individuals of the general term. The example is an owner declaring: 'Every slave I own is free.' The general term 'mamluk' (slave) includes three categories: full slaves (mamluk mutlaq), mudabbar (slaves whose freedom is deferred to the master's death), and mukatab (slaves who have a contract to purchase their freedom). The master's ownership over the mukatab is deficient because the mukatab owns his own earnings, unlike the other two categories. Thus, the mukatab is excluded from the manumission by this deficiency. This demonstrates that intrinsic deficiency in an individual can be a valid cause for specification.

Key Terms
تخصیص بالنقصان (takhṣīṣ bi-l-nuqṣān): Specification of a general term by the deficiency of some of its individuals, excluding them from the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mudabbar (slave promised freedom upon master's death)
B) The mukatab (slave under contract to purchase freedom)
C) The full slave (mamluk mutlaq)
D) All slaves are freed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, intrinsic deficiency in an individual can be a valid cause for specification of a general term, as seen in the exclusion of the mukatab from the master's manumission declaration.

Mushakkak: The Graded Term in Hanafi Usul
Defines and explains the concept of mushakkak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mushakkak, identify its characteristics, and distinguish it from mutawati' and mushtarak.

Core Idea
A mushakkak term applies to its referents with varying intensity, unlike univocal or equivocal terms.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, terms are classified by how they apply to their individuals. One important category is mushakkak (graded term), where the same word applies to different referents with varying strength. This lesson defines mushakkak and explains its distinguishing features through examples. Understanding mushakkak helps in interpreting legal texts where a single term may carry different weights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining characteristic
Note that a mushakkak word involves inequality among its individuals in intensity, priority, or precedence.
2
Examine the examples
Understand why 'mamluk' and 'wujud' are mushakkak: they apply to different referents with different strengths.
The example of 'wujud' is particularly important for theological contexts.
3
Distinguish from related categories
Know the difference between mushakkak (graded), mutawati' (equal), and mushtarak (different meanings).
The name 'mushakkak' itself hints at the doubt it creates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ ویسمی مشکک یعنی لفظ جب ایسے معنی کے لئے موضوع ہو جس کے افراد متساوی نہ ہوں بلکہ اس کے افراد میں شدت و ضعف یا اولویت اور عدم اولویت کے اعتبار سے یا تقدم تاخر کے اعتبار سے تفاوت اور اختلاف ہو جیسے لفظ مملوک کا اطلاق مملوک پر شدت کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور مکاتب پر اس کا اطلاق اضعفیت کے ساتھ ہے اور وجود کا اطلاق باری تعالی پر تقدم اور اولویت کے ساتھ ہے اور ممکن پر اطلاق تاخر اور غیر اولویت کے ساتھ ہے تو ایسے لفظ کو مشکک کہتے ہیں۔ وجہ تسمیہ: اور اس کو مشکک اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ یہ ناظر کو شک میں ڈال دیتا ہے کہ یہ لفظ مشترک کے قبیل سے ہے یا متواطی (جس کے افراد مساوی ہوں) کے معنی میں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Benefit: And it is called mushakkak, meaning a word that is used for a meaning whose individuals are not equal, rather among its individuals there is difference in intensity and weakness, or priority and non-priority, or precedence and delay. For example, the word 'mamluk' (owned/slave) applies to the absolute slave with intensity, and to the mukatab with weakness; and the word 'wujud' (existence) applies to the Exalted Creator with precedence and priority, and to contingent beings with delay and non-priority. Such a word is called mushakkak. Reason for naming: And it is called mushakkak because it casts the observer into doubt as to whether this word is of the category of mushtarak (equivocal) or mutawati' (univocal whose individuals are equal). And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This fa'idah (benefit) defines the term 'mushakkak' (graded term). A mushakkak word is one that applies to its referents with varying degrees of intensity, priority, or strength. For example, 'mamluk' applies more strongly to a full slave than to a mukatab (whose freedom is pending). Similarly, 'wujud' applies primarily to Allah's necessary existence and derivatively to contingent beings. The term is called mushakkak because it creates doubt (shakk) for the observer: is it like mushtarak (homonym) or mutawati' (univocal)? This concept is crucial in Hanafi usul for understanding how a single term can have different legal effects when applied to different subjects.

Key Terms
مشکک (mushakkak): A word that applies to its individuals with varying intensity, priority, or precedence.
متواطی (mutawāṭi'): A word whose individuals are equal in the meaning, opposite of mushakkak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the word 'mamluk' considered mushakkak?
A) Because it has multiple unrelated meanings
B) Because it applies to a full slave and a mukatab with different strength
C) Because it is ambiguous
D) Because it is specific to one individual

Key Takeaway
A mushakkak term has one meaning but applies with varying strength to its referents.

Four Causes of Takhsis al-Amm in Hanafi Usul
Explains four non-textual causes that specify general terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four causes of takhsis al-amm as recognized in Hanafi usul and apply them to determine the scope of general terms in legal texts.

Core Idea
General terms are specified by intellect, observation, custom, and deficiency—not only by textual evidence.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary presents four causes that specify general terms. These causes are not limited to textual indicators but include reason, sensory evidence, custom, and inherent deficiency in the subject. Understanding them helps you correctly interpret general commands and avoid erroneous extensions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four causes
List the four causes mentioned: intellect (aql), sense/observation (hiss wa mushahada), custom (adah), and deficiency (nuqsan).
2
Understand each cause's basis
For each cause, note the specific reason that triggers specification: intellect prevents absurdity, observation contradicts inclusion, custom defines common usage, deficiency limits ownership.
These are all non-textual mukhassis.
3
Apply to the examples
Work through each example: the general 'everything' is restricted by intellect for Allah, by observation for Bilqis, by custom for heads, and by deficiency for mukatab in emancipation.
4
Compare with other madhahib
Reflect that some schools accept only textual specifiers; Hanafis include these additional causes, giving broader interpretive tools.
This is a key Hanafi feature.
5
Derive the fiqh ruling
For each example, state the resulting ruling: e.g., swearer not breaking oath if eating a rare head, mukatab not freed by general declaration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفات باری تعالی داخل نہیں ہیں کیونکہ اگر داخل ہوں تو اللہ تعالیٰ کا اپنی ذات وصفات کا خالق ہونا لازم آئے گا اور یہ تخلیق الشني لنفسه “ ہے جو باطل ہے تو یہاں عقل نے عام ( کل بی) کو اللہ کی ذات وصفات کے علاوہ دوسرے افراد میں محصور کر دیا ۔ (ii) یا وہ مستقل شئی حس اور مشاہدہ ہوگی جیسے ملکہ بلقیس کے بارے میں قرآن پاک میں ارشاد ہے "و اوتیت من كل شئی " یہاں کل شئی میں تمام چیزیں داخل ہیں حتی کہ نبوت بھی داخل ہے لیکن امتوں کے مشاہدے سے ثابت ہے کہ اس کو نبوت نہیں ملی تھی۔ تو یہاں کل شئی میں نبوت داخل نہیں ہے اب یہاں حس اور مشاہدہ نے کل شی کے بعض افراد یعنی نبوت کو اس حکم سے خاص اور خارج کر دیا۔ (iii) یا وہ کئی عادت ہوگی جیسے کوئی آدمی کہے " لا ياكل راسا اب ویسے تو راسا عام ہے ہر جاندار کے سر کو شامل ہے لیکن عادتا ہر شئی کا سر کھایا ہی نہیں جاتا بلکہ انہی سروں کو کھایا جاتا ہے جو تنور میں بھونے جاتے ہوں مثلاً بھیڑ ، بکری، بھینس وغیرہ کا سر اس لیے یہاں راسا سے مراد بھی یہی سر ہوں گے تو یہاں عادت نے راسا ( عام ) کو اس کے بعض افراد پر محصور کر دیا اور باقی افراد کو اس عدم اکل والے حکم سے خارج کر دیا لہذا اگر متکلم چڑیا وغیرہ کے سر کو کھالے گا تو حانث نہ ہو گا۔ (iv) بعض اوقات عام کے بعض افراد کا ناقص ہونا بھی تخصیص کا سبب بن جاتا ہے جیسے کوئی آدمی کہئے کل مملوک لی فهو خراب مملوک میں غلام ، مدیر ، مکاتب سب شامل ہیں لیکن ان سے تن مد بر وغیرہ میں تو ملکیت کامل ہے لیکن مکاتب میں ملکیت ناقص ہے اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کے مکاسب اس کی ملک ہوتے ہیں مالک کی ملک نہیں ہوتے تو محل مملوک لی فهو حر میں مکاتب داخل نہیں ہوگا اور اس کا سبب مکاتب میں ملکیت کا ناقص ہوتا ہے اس لیے یہ آزاد نہیں ہوگا۔ تو یہاں عام کی تخصیص کا سبب اس کے بعض افراد کا ناقص ہونا بن رہا ہے۔
The attributes of Allah are not included because if they were included, it would necessitate that Allah is the creator of His own essence and attributes, and that is 'creating oneself' which is false. So here the intellect restricted the general (every thing) to other than Allah's essence and attributes. (ii) Or it may be an independent thing of sense and observation, like regarding the Queen of Sheba, the Holy Quran says 'And she was given of everything.' Here 'everything' includes all things, even prophethood is included, but it is established by the observation of nations that she was not given prophethood. So here 'everything' does not include prophethood. So here sense and observation specified and excluded some individuals of 'everything', namely prophethood, from this ruling. (iii) Or it may be custom, like a person says 'He does not eat a head.' So 'head' is general, includes the head of every living being, but customarily not every head is eaten; rather only those heads that are roasted in the oven are eaten, e.g., sheep, goat, buffalo etc. So here 'head' will refer to these heads. So here custom restricted the general 'head' to some of its individuals and excluded the remaining individuals from the ruling of non-eating. Hence if the speaker eats the head of a sparrow etc., he will not be an oath-breaker. (iv) Sometimes the deficiency of some individuals of the general also becomes a cause of specification. As if a person says 'Every slave that I own is free.' Slaves include full slaves, mudabbars, mukatabs etc. But in mudabbars etc., ownership is complete, but in mukatabs, ownership is deficient. And its proof is that the earnings of the mukatab are his property, not the owner's property. So in the phrase 'every slave that I own is free', the mukatab will not be included. And the reason is the deficiency of ownership in the mukatab, so he will not be free. So here the cause of specification of the general is the deficiency of some of its individuals.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) explains four causes (asbab) that specify a general term (takhsis al-amm). The author lists them: (i) intellect (aql): the general term 'everything' cannot include Allah's essence and attributes because that would entail Him creating Himself, which is impossible; thus intellect restricts it. (ii) sense and observation (hiss wa mushahada): the Quranic 'everything' in the story of Bilqis does not include prophethood because empirical evidence shows she was not a prophet. (iii) custom (adah): the common practice determines which heads are eaten, so an oath not to eat 'head' only applies to those commonly eaten. (iv) deficiency (nuqsan): a mukatab lacks complete ownership, so he is not included in 'every slave I own' for emancipation. All these causes serve as mukhassis (specifiers) that limit the scope of the general. The discussion follows the Hanafi usul method of identifying textual and contextual indicators that restrict general terms.

Key Terms
تخصیص العام (takhsis al-amm): Specification of a general term to some of its individuals by a separate indicator.
عقل (aql): Intellect as a specifier when the general would otherwise imply an impossibility.
عادت (adah): Customary practice as a specifier of a general term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a cause for specifying a general term?
A) Ijma
B) Qiyas
C) Custom (adah)
D) Naskh

Key Takeaway
General terms are not always absolute; their scope is often narrowed by intellect, observation, custom, or inherent deficiency.

Mushakkik: The Graded Term in Hanafi Usul
Defines the technical term mushakkik with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mushakkik, distinguish it from mutawati' and mushtarak, and identify its role in causing doubt in textual interpretation.

Core Idea
A mushakkik term applies to its individuals with varying intensity, creating ambiguity between univocal and homonymous meanings.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding how a word relates to its meanings is crucial for correct interpretation. This lesson introduces the concept of mushakkik, a term whose application to different individuals is not uniform. This category sits between mutawati' (univocal) and mushtarak (homonym), and recognizing it helps the jurist determine whether a general text can be specified or applied uniformly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of words based on relationship to meaning
Words can be mutawati' (equal application), mushtarak (multiple unrelated meanings), or mushakkik (graded application). Recognize the key features of each.
Mushakkik is not always listed as a separate category in all usul works but is a nuance important in the Hanafi tradition.
2
Define mushakkik by its key features
A mushakkik word is placed for a meaning whose individuals are not equal; there is difference in intensity, priority, or precedence among them.
The term itself comes from shakk (doubt) because it creates uncertainty.
3
Analyze the examples given
Examine the two examples: 'mamluk' (owned) applies more intensely to a full slave than to a mukatab; 'existence' applies primarily to Allah and secondarily to contingent beings.
These examples show how the same word can have a core meaning but with gradation.
4
Understand the reason for the naming
The word is called mushakkik because it casts the observer into doubt: is it mushtarak (different meanings) or mutawati' (same meaning for all)?
This doubt is the key practical implication; the jurist must resolve it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائده ویسمی مشکک یعنی لفظ جب ایسے معنی کے لئے موضوع ہو جس کے افراد متساوی نہ ہوں بلکہ اس کے افراد میں شدت و ضعف یا اولویت اور عدم اولویت کے اعتبار سے یا تقدم تاخر کے اعتبار سے تفاوت اور اختلاف ہو جیسے لفظ مملوک کا اطلاق من پر اشدیت کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور مکاتب پر اس کا اطلاق اضعفیت کے ساتھ ہے اور وجود کا اطلاق باری تعالی پر تقدم اور اولویت کے ساتھ ہے اور ممکن پر اطلاق تا خر اور غیر اولویت کے ساتھ ہے تو ایسے لفظ کومشلک کہتے ہیں۔ وجہ تسمیہ:۔ اور اس کو مشلک اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ یہ ناظر کو شک میں ڈال دیتا ہے کہ یہ لفظ مشترک کے قبیل سے ہے یا متواطی (جس کے افراد مساوی ہوں) کے معنی میں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Benefit: It is called mushakkik, meaning a word that is placed for a meaning whose individuals are not equal; rather among its individuals there is difference and variation in terms of intensity and weakness, or priority and non-priority, or precedence and lateness. Like the application of the word 'mamluk' (owned) to a full slave is with intensity, and to a mukatab is with weakness. And the application of 'existence' to Allah is with precedence and priority, and to contingents is with lateness and non-priority. Such a word is called mushtakkik. Reason for naming: It is called mushakkik because it casts the observer into doubt whether this word is of the category of mushtarak (homonym) or mutawati' (univocal). And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained benefit (fa'ida) defining the term 'mushakkik' (or mushtakkik). The author distinguishes it from mushtarak (one word with multiple unrelated meanings) and mutawati' (one word with equal application to all individuals). Mushakkik applies to individuals with varying degrees of strength, intensity, or priority. Examples: 'mamluk' applies more strongly to a full slave than to a mukatab; 'existence' applies primarily to Allah and secondarily to created beings. The name mushakkik comes from the doubt (shakk) it creates: is it a mushtarak (different meanings) or mutawati' (same meaning)? This discussion is important in usul al-fiqh for understanding how general terms can have graded applicability, which can affect specification in certain contexts.

Key Terms
مشکک (mushakkik): A word that signifies its meaning but with varying intensity or priority among its individuals.
متواطئ (mutawati'): A word whose application to all its individuals is equal, without variation.
مشترک (mushtarak): A homonym: one word with multiple unrelated meanings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the term 'mushakkik' so named?
A) Because it causes doubt whether the word is mushtarak or mutawati'.
B) Because it applies equally to all individuals.
C) Because it has multiple unrelated meanings.
D) Because it always requires specification.

Key Takeaway
Mushakkik is a term that applies to its referents with graded intensity, casting doubt on its category and requiring the jurist to resolve this doubt through context or further analysis.

Specification Due to Excess Meaning
Explains takhsis due to extra meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an extra meaning (za'id ma'na) in some individuals of a general term causes specification (takhsis) and apply this to oath scenarios.

Core Idea
A general term is specified when some individuals carry an extra meaning beyond the core definition.

This lesson introduces a subtle but important cause of specification (takhsis) in Hanafi usul: the presence of an extra meaning in certain individuals of a general term. By understanding this, you will be able to analyze how oaths and general statements can be restricted based on nuanced semantic and customary considerations.

Guided Path
1
Define the General Term
Start by identifying the general term (amm) in the example: 'fakiha' (fruit). Recognize its default scope—everything commonly called fruit.
In the example, 'fakiha' includes dates, grapes, cucumbers, etc.
2
Extract the Core Meaning
Determine the essential attribute of the term: 'fakiha' refers to something eaten purely for pleasure (taladhdhudhan). This is the core meaning.
This definition is based on customary usage ('urf).
3
Identify the Extra Meaning
Among the individuals, some (dates and grapes) have an additional characteristic: they are also eaten as nourishment (ghidha). This extra meaning (za'id ma'na) goes beyond the core pleasure-only definition.
The extra meaning is not present in cucumbers or wood, which are purely for pleasure or other uses.
4
Apply the Takhsis Rule
Because of the extra meaning, these individuals are excluded from the general term in the context of the oath. Eating them does not violate the oath.
The rule: A general term is specified when some individuals possess an attribute that the speaker's usage implicitly excludes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض اوقات عام کی تخصیص کا سبب اس کے بعض افراد کا زائد ہونا بھی بن جاتا ہے جیسے کوئی آدمی کہے کہ "لا ياكل فاكهة" اب فاکہہ کا اطلاق ویسے تو کھجور، انگور، کھیرا، لکڑی وغیرہ سب پر ہوتا ہے لیکن ان میں سے کھجور اور انگور میں زائد معنی پایا جاتا ہے کیونکہ فاکہتہ اسے کہتے ہیں جو محض تلذذا کھایا جاتا ہو اور یہ معنی کھیرہ اور لکڑی میں تو بالکل پورا پورا ہے لیکن کھجور اور انگور کو چونکہ بطور غذائیت بھی کھایا جاتا ہے اس لیے ان میں زائد معنی پایا گیا اسی لیے متکلم کے قول لا ياكل فاكهة“ میں یہ داخل نہیں ہوں گے اور ان کو کھانا اس کی کلام کے خلاف نہیں ہوگا اور وہ اس سے حانث نہیں ہوگا تو یہاں عام (فاكهة) سے بعض افراد کی تخصیص کا سبب اس کے بعض افراد میں زائد معنی کا ہونا ہے۔
Sometimes the cause of specification of the general is the excess of some of its individuals. For example, if a person says, 'He does not eat fruit.' Now the word 'fruit' applies to dates, grapes, cucumber, wood, etc., but among them dates and grapes have an extra meaning because 'fruit' is called that which is eaten purely for pleasure. And this meaning is fully present in cucumber and wood [as consumed for pleasure?], but since dates and grapes are also eaten as nourishment, an extra meaning is found in them. Therefore, they will not be included in the speaker's statement 'he does not eat fruit', and eating them will not violate his statement, and he will not be an oath-breaker. So here the cause of specification of the general (fruit) from some individuals is the presence of an extra meaning in those individuals.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage adds a fifth cause of specification (takhsis): the presence of an extra meaning (ziyadat ma'na) in some individuals. The example: if someone swears not to eat 'fruit' (fakiha), the term generally includes dates, grapes, cucumbers, etc. However, dates and grapes are also eaten for nutrition, which is an additional characteristic beyond mere pleasure. Since the primary meaning of fruit is for pleasure, these extra-nutritious items are excluded from the oath. This shows that general terms can be restricted when certain individuals possess attributes that go beyond the core definition. This is a subtle but important point in Hanafi usul for understanding how context and customary usage interact with general terms.

Key Terms
زائد معنی (za'id ma'na): An extra meaning or characteristic present in some individuals of a general term that leads to their exclusion.
فاكهة (fakiha): Fruit eaten purely for pleasure, not as a staple or nourishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they are not fruits
B) Because they have an extra meaning of being nourishment
C) Because they are not eaten raw
D) Because they are too small

Key Takeaway
Specification can occur due to an extra meaning in some individuals, which excludes them from a general term.

Effect of Mustaqill and Ghayr Mustaqill Mukhassis
Explains whether general remains haqiqah or becomes majaz after specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mustaqill and ghayr mustaqill mukhassis and state whether the general term remains haqiqah or becomes majaz in the remaining individuals.

Core Idea
A non-independent specifier preserves the literal meaning; an independent specifier makes the general metaphorical.

In Hanafi usul, specifying a general term does not always have the same effect on its linguistic status. This passage from al-Tarweeh clarifies that the key factor is whether the specifier (mukhassis) is part of the same utterance (ghayr mustaqill) or an independent proof (mustaqill). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting general Qur'anic and hadith texts and for assessing the strength of arguments derived from them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of mukhassis
The passage divides mukhassis into ghayr mustaqill (non-independent, like an exception or condition within the same utterance) and mustaqill (independent, like a separate text). Identify which category a given specifier falls into.
Ghayr mustaqill is part of the same sentence; mustaqill is separate.
2
Determine the effect on haqiqah/majaz
For ghayr mustaqill, the general remains haqiqah (literal) in the remaining individuals. For mustaqill, the general becomes majaz (metaphorical) in the remaining individuals, by way of applying the name of the whole to a part.
3
Note the condition of the specifier being known
The passage specifies that the exception or specification must be known (ma'lum) for it to be a valid proof. If it is unknown (majhul), it does not constitute a specification.
4
Understand the dual nature for mustaqill
For mustaqill, the general is considered majaz from the perspective of restriction (qasr), but it is still considered haqiqah from the perspective of denotation (tanawul) because the word actually applies to the remaining individuals.
This nuance is important to avoid oversimplification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَفِي غَيْرِ الْمُسْتَقِلْ أَى فِيمَا إِذَا كَانَ الشَّيْءُ الْمُوجِبُ لِقَصْرِ الْعَامِّ غَيْرَ مُسْتَقِلٌ ( وَهُوَ ) أَى الْعَامُ ) حَقِيقَةٌ فِي الْبَاقِي ) لِأَنَّ الْوَاضِعَ وَضَعَ اللَّفْظَ الَّذِى اسْتَثْنَى مِنْهُ لِلْبَاقِي . ( وَهُوَ ) أَى الْعَامُ ) حُجَّةٌ بِلا شُبُهَةٍ فِيهِ) أَيُّ فِي الْبَاقِي ، وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الاسْتِثْنَاء مَعْلُومًا أَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ مَجْهُولًا فَلا ) وَفِي الْمُسْتَقِلْ كَلَامًا أَوْ غَيْرَهُ ) أَى : فِيمَا إذَا كَانَ الْقَاصِرُ مُسْتَقِلًا وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا تَخْصِيصًا سَوَاءٌ كَانَ الْمُخَصْصُ كَلامًا أَوْ غَيْرَهُ ) مَجَارٌ) أَى :لَفْظُ الْعَامِّ مَجَارٌ فِي الْبَاقِي ) بِطَرِيقِ اسْمِ الْكُلِّ عَلَى الْبَعْضِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْقَصْرُ) أَى مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَقْصُورٌ عَلَى الْبَاقِي ( حَقِيقَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ التَّناوُلُ ( أى مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ لَفَظَ الْعَامُ مُتَنَاوِلٌ لِلْبَاقِي يَكُونُ حَقِيقَةٌ فِيهِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي فَصْلِ الْمَجَازِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى وَهُوَ حُجَّةٌ فِيهِ شُبُهَةٌ. ترجمہ:۔ (پس غیر مستقل میں) یعنی اس صورت میں کہ جب ہو وہ شی جو واجب کرنے والی ہے عام کے بند ہونے کو ( ہو وہ ) غیر مستقل ( تو ہو گا وہ ) یعنی عام (حقیقت باقی افراد میں) کیونکہ واضع نے وضع کیا اس لفظ کو جس سے استثناء کر دیا گیا باقی کے لیے (اور وہ ) یعنی عام ( حجت ہوگا بغیر کسی شبہ کے ان میں ) یعنی باقی افراد میں اور یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ وہ استثناء معلوم ہو بہر حال جب کہ ہو وہ مجبول تو پھر نہیں ( اور مستقل میں کلام ہو یا غیر کلام ) یعنی اس صورت میں کہ جب ہو بند کرنے والا مستقل اور نام رکھا جاتا ہے اس کا تخصیص برابر ہے کہ وہ مخصص کلام یا اس کا غیر ( ہو گا مجاز ) یعنی لفظ عام مجاز ہوگا (باقی افراد میں کل کے اسم کا بعض پر اطلاق کرنے کے طریقہ کے ساتھ قصر کی حیثیت سے ) یعنی اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ بند کیا ہوا ہے باقی پر
So in non-independent [case], i.e., when the thing that necessitates the restriction of the general is non-independent, then the general is a reality (haqiqah) in the remaining [individuals], because the coiner placed the word from which an exception was made for the remaining. And it (the general) is a proof without any doubt in them, i.e., in the remaining. This is when the exception is known; but if it is unknown, then not. And in the independent [case], whether [the mukhassis is] speech or other, i.e., when the restrictor is independent, and this is called takhsis, whether the mukhassis is speech or other, [the general becomes] metaphorical (majar [majaz]), i.e., the word of the general becomes metaphorical in the remaining, by way of applying the name of the whole to a part, from the perspective of restriction, i.e., from the perspective that it is restricted to the remaining. It is a reality (haqiqah) from the perspective of denotation, i.e., from the perspective that the general word denotes the remaining, it is a reality in it, as will come in the chapter on majaz, God willing. And it is a proof with any doubt in it. Translation: (So in non-independent) meaning in the case where the thing that necessitates the restriction of the general is non-independent, then the general (is a reality in the remaining) because the coiner placed the word from which exception was made for the remaining. (And it) i.e., the general (is a proof without any doubt in them) i.e., in the remaining. This is when the exception is known; but if it is unknown, then no. (And in the independent, whether speech or other) i.e., in the case where the restrictor is independent, and this is called specification (takhsis), whether the mukhassis is speech or other, (it becomes metaphorical) i.e., the general word becomes metaphorical in the remaining (by way of applying the name of the whole to a part from the perspective of restriction) i.e., from the perspective that it is restricted to the remaining.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of the type of mukhassis (specifier) on the general term. It distinguishes two cases: (1) When the mukhassis is not independent (ghayr mustaqill), for example, when the specifier is a condition, exception, or attribute that is part of the same utterance, the general remains haqiqah (literal) in the remaining individuals. It is also a definitive proof (hujjah) without doubt, provided the specification is known. (2) When the mukhassis is independent (mustaqill), such as a separate textual proof or external indicator, the general becomes majaz (metaphorical) in the remaining individuals, applied by way of using the name of the whole for a part. However, from the perspective of denotation (tanawul), it is still considered haqiqah in the remaining meaning. The passage also notes that if the specification is unknown (majhul), it is not a proof. This distinction is important for determining the legal force and interpretation of general statements in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
غیر مستقل (ghayr mustaqill): A mukhassis that is not independent, i.e., it is part of the same utterance such as an exception or condition.
مستقل (mustaqill): An independent mukhassis, i.e., a separate text or evidence that specifies the general.
حقیقت (haqiqah): Literal meaning; the word is used in its originally intended sense for the remaining individuals.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage; applying the general term to a part after independent specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the linguistic status of a general term specified by an independent (mustaqill) mukhassis?
A) It remains haqiqah in the remaining individuals.
B) It becomes majaz in the remaining individuals.
C) It becomes completely ambiguous and invalid.
D) It becomes a new haqiqah by itself.

Key Takeaway
The type of mukhassis determines whether the general term remains haqiqah (ghayr mustaqill) or becomes majaz (mustaqill), but in both cases it remains a valid proof.
