Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Status of 'Aam after Takhsis: Non-Independent vs Independent Restrictor
Explains the ruling on a general term after restriction by non-independent vs independent restrictors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between non-independent and independent restrictors and apply the Hanafi rule to determine whether the general term is literal (haqīqah) or metaphorical (majāz) and its evidential weight.

Core Idea
A general term after non-independent restriction stays literal and definitive; after independent restriction, it becomes metaphorical and probable.

One of the key distinctions in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh is the treatment of a general term (āmm) after it has been restricted (takhṣīṣ). This passage from a sharḥ on al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ clarifies that the outcome depends crucially on the nature of the restrictor (mukhaṣiṣ): whether it is non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and integrated into the same speech, or independent (mustaqill) and separate. Understanding this distinction is essential for properly assessing the probative force of a restricted general text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of restrictor
Determine whether the restrictor is non-independent (e.g., an exception, condition, description, or goal attached to the same speech) or independent (e.g., a separate verse or hadith).
Non-independent restrictors include istithnā', shart, sifat, and ghāyah.
2
Apply the rule for non-independent restrictors
If the restrictor is non-independent, the general term remains literal (ḥaqīqah) in the remaining individuals and serves as a definitive proof (ḥujjah bilā shubhah), provided the excluded individuals are known.
The coinor (wāḍiʿ) is considered to have coined the word for the remaining scope.
3
Apply the rule for independent restrictors
If the restrictor is independent, the general term becomes metaphorical (majāz) in the remaining individuals by applying the name of the whole to a part. It is only a probable proof (ḥujjah maʿa shubhah).
From the perspective of scope, the word still literally covers the remaining individuals, but due to the independent restriction, it is deemed metaphorical.
4
Check the condition for non-independent restrictors
For the general term to remain literal and definitive, the excluded individuals must be known. If they are unknown (e.g., 'except some of them'), the term does not become literal.
Unknown exclusion renders the restriction ineffective in preserving the literal status.
5
Distinguish the evidential value
A general term after non-independent restriction is qaṭʿī (definitive) evidence; after independent restriction, it is ẓannī (probable). This has practical implications for juristic preference (tarjīḥ) and ijtihād.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school; the Mutakallimūn treat all restricted general terms as ẓannī.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَفِي غَيْرِ الْمُسْتَقِلْ أَى فِيمَا إِذَا كَانَ الشَّيْءُ الْمُوجِبُ لِقَصْرِ الْعَامِّ غَيْرَ مُسْتَقِلٌ ( وَهُوَ ) أَى الْعَامُ ) حَقِيقَةٌ فِي الْبَاقِي ) لِأَنَّ الْوَاضِعَ وَضَعَ اللَّفْظَ الَّذِى اسْتَثْنَى مِنْهُ لِلْبَاقِي . ( وَهُوَ ) أَى الْعَامُ ) حُجَّةٌ بِلا شُبُهَةٍ فِيهِ) أَيُّ فِي الْبَاقِي ، وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الاسْتِثْنَاء مَعْلُومًا أَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ مَجْهُولًا فَلا ) وَفِي الْمُسْتَقِلْ كَلَامًا أَوْ غَيْرَهُ ) أَى : فِيمَا إذَا كَانَ الْقَاصِرُ مُسْتَقِلًا وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا تَخْصِيصًا سَوَاءٌ كَانَ الْمُخَصْصُ كَلامًا أَوْ غَيْرُهُ ) مَجَارٌ) أَى :لَفْظُ الْعَامِّ مَجَارٌ فِي الْبَاقِي ) بِطَرِيقِ اسْمِ الْكُلِّ عَلَى الْبَعْضِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْقَصْرُ) أَى مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَقْصُورٌ عَلَى الْبَاقِي ( حَقِيقَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ التَّناوُلُ ( أى مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ لَفَظَ الْعَامُ مُتَنَاوِلٌ لِلْبَاقِي يَكُونُ حَقِيقَةٌ فِيهِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي فَصْلِ الْمَجَازِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى وَهُوَ حُجَّةٌ فِيهِ شُبُهَة.
ترجمہ:۔ (پس غیر مستقل میں) یعنی اس صورت میں کہ جب ہو وہ شی جو واجب کرنے والی ہے عام کے بند ہونے کو ( ہو وہ ) غیر مستقل ( تو ہو گا وہ ) یعنی عام (حقیقت باقی افراد میں) کیونکہ واضع نے وضع کیا اس لفظ کو جس سے استثناء کر دیا گیا باقی کے لیے (اور وہ ) یعنی عام ( حجت ہوگا بغیر کسی شبہ کے ان میں ) یعنی باقی افراد میں اور یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ وہ استثناء معلوم ہو بہر حال جب کہ ہو وہ مجہول تو پھر نہیں ( اور مستقل میں کلام ہو یا غیر کلام ) یعنی اس صورت میں کہ جب ہو بند کرنے والا مستقل اور نام رکھا جاتا ہے اس کا تخصیص برابر ہے کہ وہ مخصص کلام یا اس کا غیر ( ہو گا مجاز ) یعنی لفظ عام مجاز ہوگا (باقی افراد میں کل کے اسم کا بعض پر اطلاق کرنے کے طریقہ کے ساتھ قصر کی حیثیت سے ) یعنی اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ بند کیا ہوا ہے باقی پر حقیقت ہو گا تناول کی حیثیت سے ) یعنی اس حیثیت سے کہ بے شک لفظ عام شامل ہے باقی افراد کو تو ہو گا حقیقت ان میں
So in the non-independent (i.e., when the thing causing the restriction of the general is non-independent): and it (i.e., the general) is literal in the remaining (individuals), because the coinor coined the word from which the exception was made for the remaining. And it (the general) is a proof without doubt in it (i.e., in the remaining). And this is when the exception is known; but if it is unknown, then not. And in the independent, whether speech or other (i.e., when the restrictor is independent, whether it is speech or not) it is metaphorical: the general word is metaphorical in the remaining (individuals) by the method of applying the name of the whole to the part, from the perspective of restriction (i.e., from the perspective that it is restricted to the remaining). It is literal from the perspective of scope (i.e., from the perspective that the general word encompasses the remaining individuals, it is literal in them, as will come in the chapter on metaphor, if Allah wills. And it is a proof with doubt.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on a general term ('aam) after it has been restricted (takhsis) to some of its individuals. The author distinguishes between two cases: when the restrictor (mukhasis) is non-independent (ghayr mustaqil) and when it is independent (mustaqil). A non-independent restrictor is one that is connected to the general term itself, such as an exception (istithna), a condition (shart), a description (sifat), or a goal (ghayah). For example, 'My slaves are free except Salim.' Here, the exception 'except Salim' is non-independent because it is part of the same speech. In this case, the general term remains literal (haqiqah) in the remaining individuals (i.e., all slaves except Salim) because the coinor (waadi') effectively placed the word for those remaining individuals. The general term becomes a definitive proof (hujjah bila shubhah) for the remaining individuals, provided the excluded individuals are known. If the excluded individuals are unknown (e.g., 'Kill the polytheists except some of them' where 'some' is vague), then the general term is not literal because the remaining individuals cannot be identified. On the other hand, if the restrictor is independent—i.e., a separate text or evidence not part of the same speech—then the general term becomes metaphorical (majaz) in the remaining individuals. This is considered a type of applying the name of the whole to a part (ism al-kull 'ala al-ba'd). From the perspective of restriction, it is metaphorical; from the perspective of scope (i.e., that the word still encompasses those remaining individuals in its original coinage), it is still literal. However, because of the metaphorical aspect, it is only a probable proof (hujjah ma'a shubhah). This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul for determining whether a general text can be relied upon as definitive or only probable after restriction.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A term that encompasses all individuals of its category by linguistic coinage.
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): Restricting a general term to some of its individuals by a specific evidence.
مُسْتَقِل (mustaqill): A restrictor that is independent of the general term, such as a separate verse or hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, if a general term is restricted by a non-independent exception (istithna), what is the status of the general term in the remaining individuals?
A) It becomes metaphorical (majaz) and is a probabilistic proof.
B) It remains literal (haqiqah) and is a definitive proof, provided the excluded are known.
C) It becomes ambiguous and requires further clarification.
D) It is rendered abrogated and no longer applicable.

Key Takeaway
The type of restrictor determines the epistemological status of a restricted general term: non-independent preserves literalness and definitiveness; independent renders it metaphorical and probable.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
Ruling of 'Amm after Takhsis: Non-Independent vs Independent Specification
Explaining rulings of 'amm after takhsis and necessity to distinguish between specification types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between non-independent and independent specification of a general term, evaluate the epistemological weight (qat'i vs zanni) of each, and explain why specification by reason retains qat'i status.

Core Idea
Specification by reason is qat'i because it acts as an implicit exception that the intellect automatically excludes.

When a general term is specified, its legal force may change. The commentator distinguishes two types of specifying causes: non-independent (embedded in speech) and independent (separate from speech). For each, the 'amm after specification may be haqiqah or majaz, qat'i or zanni. A unique point: specification by reason (e.g., excluding children and insane) does not create doubt and remains qat'i, contrary to the undifferentiated view of many scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of specification
Non-independent specification (ghayr mustaqill) includes exception, attribute, limit, or condition embedded in the speech itself. Independent specification (mustaqill) comes from a separate source, like another verse or reason.
The term 'mustaqill' here means the specifying factor is not part of the same utterance.
2
Understand the ruling for non-independent specification
With non-independent specification, the general word becomes haqiqah in the remaining individuals, and thus the evidence is qat'i (definitive). Example: 'My slaves are free except Salim' – 'slaves' is haqiqah for the others.
This requires the excluded to be known; if unknown (e.g., 'except some of them'), the evidence is not qat'i.
3
Understand the ruling for independent specification
For independent specification, the general word is majaz (metaphorical) from the perspective of restriction to the remaining individuals, but haqiqah from the perspective of applicability to them. Thus the evidence is zanni (probable).
A word can be both haqiqah and majaz from different perspectives.
4
Recognize the common scholarly position
Many scholars (including some Hanafis) did not differentiate between specification by speech and by other means; they held that any 'amm specified by an independent cause is zanni.
This is the view the commentator seeks to refine.
5
Appreciate the commentator's unique argument for reason-based specification
Specification by reason (e.g., excluding children/insane from legal obligations) is like an implicit exception. Since reason itself clearly identifies the excluded, no doubt arises. Hence the 'amm remains qat'i. Denying such texts (e.g., prayer obligations) leads to kufr by consensus.
This distinction is necessary to avoid treating all specified 'amm as equally doubtful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

میں حقیقت ہوتا ہے اور اس وقت یہ عام دلیل قطعی ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ وہ لفظ عام جس سے بعض افراد کو استثناء یا صفت یا غایت یا شرط کے ذریعہ سے نکال دیا گیا تو گویا اس لفظ کی وضع باقی افراد کے لئے ہے مثال کے طور پر اگر متکلم نے کہا عبیدی أحرار إلا سالما تو لفظ عبید سالم مخرج کے علاوہ باقی افراد کے لئے موضوع ہے۔ یعنی باقی افراد ہی اس کا معنی موضوع لہ ہیں اور لفظ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں حقیقت ہوتا ہے اس لیے عام (مستثنیٰ منہ ) بقیہ افراد میں حقیقت اور قطعی ہے۔ وفی استقلال : اور اگر عام کو بعض افراد میں منحصر کرنے والی شئی مستقل ہو تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ تخصیص کے بعد عام بقیہ افراد میں من حیث الاقتصار علی البعض مجاز ہے اور من حیث التناول اللباقی حقیقتہ ہے اور مجاز ظنی ہوتا ہے اس لیے اس وقت عام دلیل ظنی ہو گا لیکن یہ جو ہم نے عام کو بقیہ افراد میں مجاز کہا ہے یہ اس حیثیت سے ہے کہ عام انہی افراد میں بَيْنَ كَوْنِهِ) أَى التَّخْصِيصِ ) بِالْكَلَامِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ) فَإِنَّ الْعُلَمَاءَ قَالُوا كُلُّ عَامٍ خُصَّ بِمُسْتَقِلْ فَإِنَّهُ دَلِيلٌ فِيهِ شُبُهَةٌ وَلَمْ يُفَرِّقُوا فِي هَذَا الْحُكْمِ بَيْنَ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُخَصِّصُ كَلَامًا أَوْ غَيْرَهُ . ) لَكِنْ يَجِبُ هُنَاكَ فَرْقٌ وَهُوَ أَنَّ الْمَخْصُوصَ بِالْعَقْلِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ قَطْعِيًّا ; لِأَنَّهُ فِى حكم الاسْتِثْنَاءِ لَكِنَّهُ حَذَفَ الاسْتِثْنَاءَ مُعْتَمِدًا عَلَى الْعَقْلِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ مَفْرُوعٌ عَنْهُ حَتَّى لَا نَقُولَ أَنَّ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى ) يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمُ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ) وَنَظَائِرُهُ دَلِيلٌ فِيهِ شُبُهَةٌ , وَهَذَا فَرْقٌ تَفَرَّدْتُ بِذِكْرِهِ وَهُوَ وَاجِبُ الذِّكْرِ حَتَّى لَا يُتَوَهَّمَ أَنَّ خِطَابَاتِ الشَّرْعِ الَّتِي خُصَّ مِنْهَا الصَّبِيُّ وَالْمَجْنُونُ بِالْعَقْلِ دَلِيلٌ فِيهِ شُبُهَةٌ كَالْخِطَابَاتِ الْوَارِدَةِ بِالْفَرَائِضِ فَإِنَّهُ يَكْفُرُ جَاحِدُهَا إِجْمَاعًا مَعَ كَوْنِهَا مَخْصُوصَةً عَقْلًا , فَإِنَّ التَّخْصِيصَ بِالْعَقْلِ لَا يُورِثُ شُبُهَةً فَإِنَّ ) كُلَّ مَا يُوجِبُ الْعَقْلُ تَخْصِيصَهُ يُخَصُّ وَمَا لَا فَلَا .
Explanation: From here the author intends to explain the ruling of each type. So he says: When the cause of restricting the general to some individuals is non-independent, then at that time the general is haqiqah in the remaining individuals (those that remain in the ruling after specification), and at that time this general is a definitive proof, because that general word from which some individuals have been removed by exception, or attribute, or limit, or condition, it is as if that word is placed for the remaining individuals. For example, if the speaker said 'My slaves are free except Salim', then the word 'slaves' is placed for the remaining individuals other than Salim the excluded one. That is, the remaining individuals are its meaning subject to placement, and a word is haqiqah in its meaning subject to placement. Therefore, the general (that which is excepted from) will be haqiqah in its remaining individuals. But this is when the excluded is known. If the excluded is unknown, then the general will not be haqiqah in the remaining individuals, because when the individuals that are excepted are not known, the remaining individuals also cannot be known, as in 'Kill the polytheists except some of them'. Here exception of 'some' is made, but they are unknown; it is not known which 'some' are not to be killed. When it is not known which 'some' are not to be killed, then specification of those to be killed also cannot be made; rather, every individual has the probability that it may be included in 'except some of them'. Therefore, when the excluded is unknown, then we cannot say that the general (that from which exception is made) is haqiqah and definitive in the remaining individuals. And in the case of independence: And if the thing that restricts the general to some individuals is independent, then its ruling is that after specification the general is majaz in the remaining individuals with respect to restriction to some, and with respect to applicability to the remaining it is haqiqah, and majaz is zanni. Therefore, at that time the general becomes a zanni proof. But what we said that the general is majaz in the remaining individuals is from the perspective that the general is restricted to those individuals; no other individual can be intended by it. And this majaz is of the type of applying the name of the whole to a part, i.e., it is of the category of calling the part by the name of the whole. That is, the word was placed for all individuals; then when some individuals are removed, it is used for the remaining individuals, and that is not its meaning subject to placement, so it is used in something not subject to placement, hence it is majaz. And if we look from the perspective that the general still includes the same individuals that it included before specification, and the attribute of applicability does not change; rather, non-intention of some individuals has occurred, but this non-intention does not harm the attribute of applicability to the remaining individuals, then from this perspective the general is haqiqah in the remaining individuals. And it is possible for a single word to be haqiqah from one perspective and majaz from another. (And they did not differentiate between its being) i.e., the specification (by speech or other than it). For the scholars said: Every general that has been specified by an independent (cause) is a proof in which there is doubt. And they did not differentiate in this ruling between whether the specifying thing is speech or other than it. (But a distinction is necessary here, and it is that the one specified by reason should be definitive, because it is in the ruling of exception, but the exception has been omitted, relying on the intellect, on the basis that it is subsidiary to it, so that we do not say that the saying of Allah Almighty 'O you who believe, when you rise to prayer' and its analogues are proofs in which there is doubt. And this is a distinction that I uniquely mention, and it is necessary to mention so that it may not be conceived that the addresses of Shari'ah from which the child and the insane have been specified by reason are proofs in which there is doubt, like the addresses that come concerning the obligatory duties, for the one who denies them becomes a disbeliever by consensus, despite their being specified by reason. For specification by reason does not engender doubt. Rather, everything that reason necessitates its specification is specified, and what necessitates not is not.)
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's discussion on the ruling of 'amm (general term) after takhsis (specification). The commentator begins by distinguishing between two types of specifications: non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and independent (mustaqill). Non-independent specification refers to exceptions, attributes, limits, or conditions embedded within the speech itself, making the remaining individuals the actual intended meaning of the word, and thus the 'amm becomes qat'i (definitive) in those remaining individuals. The example given is 'My slaves are free except Salim' – the word 'slaves' is haqiqah in the slaves other than Salim. However, if the exception is unknown (e.g., 'Kill the polytheists except some of them'), then the 'amm does not become haqiqah in the remaining individuals because the remaining individuals are also unknown, leading to probability. For independent specification (e.g., a separate independent proof that specifies the 'amm), the 'amm is considered majaz (metaphorical) from the perspective of restriction to some individuals, but haqiqah from the perspective of applicability to the remaining individuals. This duality is possible: a word can be both haqiqah and majaz depending on the perspective. The commentator then addresses a subtle point: scholars generally held that any 'amm specified by an independent cause is zanni (probable) because it raises doubt. They did not differentiate between specification by speech (kalam) or by other means (like reason 'aql). However, the commentator argues that a distinction is necessary: specification by 'aql (reason) yields qat'i evidence, not zanni. He explains that reason-based specification is like an implicit exception that the mind automatically excludes (e.g., children and insane from legal obligations). The verse 'O you who believe, when you rise to prayer' (Q 5:6) is specified by reason to exclude children and the insane, yet it is qat'i and denying its obligation leads to disbelief by consensus. Thus, reason-based specification does not engender doubt; only specification by independent speech or other independent indicators does. This is a unique point the commentator claims to have made, warning against the misconception that all specified 'amm are equally doubtful.

Key Terms
عام (amm): A word that covers all its individuals without restriction.
تخصيص (takhsis): Limiting the general to some of its individuals by evidence.
مستقل (mustaqill): An independent specifying factor that stands on its own, not embedded in the general word.
قطعي (qat'i): Definitive, leaving no room for doubt.
ظني (zanni): Probable, allowing for interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the ruling of a general term after being specified by reason (e.g., 'O you who believe' excluding children and insane)?
A) It is zanni because specification by an independent cause creates doubt.
B) It is qat'i because reason-based specification is like an implicit exception and does not engender doubt.
C) It is not a valid specification because reason cannot specify the general.
D) It is valid only if supported by another textual evidence.

Key Takeaway
Specification by reason yields qat'i evidence; only specification by independent speech or other independent indicators yields zanni.

8 min
Specification by Reason Preserves Certainty of the General
Critical refinement on types of specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the distinction between specification by reason and by speech, and apply the Hanafi rule that rational specification does not weaken the general's definitiveness.

Core Idea
Specification by reason is implicit exception – the general remains qat'i; textual specification (per Karkhi) strips all proof value.

Many Hanafi scholars held that any general specified by an independent evidence becomes presumptive. But the commentator here insists on a critical refinement: specification by reason (like excluding children from obligations) leaves the general definitive, because reason itself dictates the exception. This distinction is vital to avoid wrongly doubting clear Quranic commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common view
The passage states that earlier scholars did not distinguish between specification by speech or non-speech; they said every general specified by an independent proof contains doubt (shubha).
2
Note the commentator's challenge
The commentator asserts that a distinction is necessary: specification by reason ('aql) should be definitive (qat'i) because it functions like an implicit exception (istithna).
Rational specification is based on necessary exclusion, not arbitrary textual evidence.
3
Understand the Quranic example
The verse about wudu (O you who believe, when you rise to prayer...) is cited. Reason excludes children and the insane, yet the verse is qat'i; denying its obligation is kufr by consensus.
This proves rational specification does not create doubt.
4
Contrast with textual specification (Karkhi)
Specification by speech (kalam) – i.e., a separate textual proof – according to al-Karkhi, removes the general's evidentiary value entirely (la yabqa hujjatan aslan).
Even if the specifying text is well-known (ma'lum), the general loses all force.
5
Apply the distinction
When evaluating a general text, first classify the specifying evidence: if it is purely rational (e.g., exclusion of non-mukallaf), the general remains qat'i; if it is another revealed text, additional usul analysis is needed.
This distinction is obligatory to mention (wajib al-dhikr) to prevent misapplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمْ يُفَرِّقُوا بَيْنَ كَوْنِهِ (أَى التَّخْصِيصِ) بِالْكَلَامِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ فَإِنَّ الْعُلَمَاءَ قَالُوا كُلُّ عَامٍ خُصَّ بِمُسْتَقِلٍّ فَإِنَّهُ دَلِيلٌ فِيهِ شُبْهَةٌ وَلَمْ يُفَرِّقُوا فِي هَذَا الْحُكْمِ بَيْنَ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُخَصِّصُ كَلَامًا أَوْ غَيْرَهُ. لَكِنْ يَجِبُ هُنَاكَ فَرْقٌ وَهُوَ أَنَّ الْمَخْصُوصَ بِالْعَقْلِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ قَطْعِيًّا؛ لِأَنَّهُ فِي حُكْمِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ لَكِنَّهُ حُذِفَ الِاسْتِثْنَاءُ مُعْتَمِدًا عَلَى الْعَقْلِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ مَفْرُوعٌ عَنْهُ حَتَّى لَا نَقُولَ أَنَّ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى {يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ} وَنَظَائِرَهُ دَلِيلٌ فِيهِ شُبْهَةٌ. وَهَذَا فَرْقٌ تَفَرَّدْتُ بِذِكْرِهِ وَهُوَ وَاجِبُ الذِّكْرِ حَتَّى لَا يُتَوَهَّمَ أَنَّ خِطَابَاتِ الشَّرْعِ الَّتِي خُصَّ مِنْهَا الصَّبِيُّ وَالْمَجْنُونُ بِالْعَقْلِ دَلِيلٌ فِيهِ شُبْهَةٌ كَالْخِطَابَاتِ الْوَارِدَةِ بِالْفَرَائِضِ فَإِنَّهُ يَكْفُرُ جَاحِدُهَا إِجْمَاعًا مَعَ كَوْنِهَا مَخْصُوصَةً عَقْلًا. فَإِنَّ التَّخْصِيصَ بِالْعَقْلِ لَا يُورِثُ شُبْهَةً. فَإِنَّ كُلَّ مَا يُوجِبُ الْعَقْلُ تَخْصِيصَهُ يُخَصُّ، وَمَا لَا فَلَا. وَأَمَّا الْمَخْصُوصُ بِالْكَلَامِ فَعِنْدَ الْكَرْخِيِّ لَا يَبْقَى حُجَّةً أَصْلًا مَعْلُومًا كَانَ
And they did not distinguish between its (i.e., the specification) being by speech or other than it. For the scholars said: Every general that is specified by an independent (proof) is an evidence that contains doubt. And they did not distinguish in this ruling between the specifying evidence being speech or other than it. But it is necessary here to make a distinction: that the specified by reason should be definitive; because it is in the ruling of exception, but the exception is omitted relying on reason, considering that it is branched from it, so that we do not say that the saying of Allah Most High 'O you who have believed, when you rise to prayer' and its likes are evidence with doubt. And this is a distinction that I alone have mentioned, and it is necessary to mention so that it may not be imagined that the addresses of the Shariah from which the child and the insane are specified by reason are evidence with doubt, like the addresses concerning the obligations; for indeed, the denier of them is unanimously a disbeliever, despite their being specified by reason. So specification by reason does not cause doubt. For everything whose specification reason necessitates, it is specified, and what it does not, is not. As for the specified by speech, according to al-Karkhi, it does not remain a proof at all, whether it is known...
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute within the Hanafi tradition. The common view held by many scholars is that any general term ('amm) specified by an independent evidence (mustaqill) becomes a presumptive (zanni) proof, regardless of whether that evidence is textual (kalam) or non-textual (ghayr kalam). The commentator (likely from the Tawdih/Talwih tradition) challenges this sweeping statement. He insists on a crucial distinction: specification by pure reason (aql) does not render the general uncertain; rather, it remains definitive (qat'i). Why? Because rational specification functions as an implicit exception (istithna). The exception is not verbally stated but is understood by reason, so the general's application to excluded individuals is negated with certainty. The author supports this with the example of the Quranic verse on wudu: it commands all believers, but reason excludes children and the insane from its obligation. Yet this verse is qat'i al-dalala; denying its legal implication is kufr by scholarly consensus. The commentator then contrasts this with specification by speech (kalam), citing Imam al-Karkhi, who holds that such specification strips the general of all evidential value (hujjiyya), even if the specifying text is well-known. Thus, the ruling depends on the nature of the specifying evidence: rational specification preserves certainty, while textual specification (according to Karkhi) destroys proof value.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A term that encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction
تخصیص (takhsis): Excluding some individuals from the scope of a general term based on a specific evidence
مخصص (mukhasis): The evidence that specifies a general term; here it is classified as either 'aql (reason) or kalam (speech)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does specification by reason not cause doubt in a general text?
A) Because the specifying text is always from the Quran
B) Because it functions as an implicit exception, similar to istithna
C) Because the general is not really specified
D) Because reason is weaker than textual evidence

Key Takeaway
Rational specification preserves the certainty of a general text; only textual specification (according to Karkhi) can destroy its evidentiary value.

Specification by Reason Preserves Definitiveness
Author presents his unique view that specification by reason leaves the general definitive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that specification by reason (takhsis bi al-‘aql) leaves a general term definitive (qat‘i) and distinguish it from specification by independent speech.

Core Idea
Specification by reason preserves the general's definitiveness, just like an exception.

This lesson explores a distinctive Hanafi position on the nature of general terms (amm) in revelation. The central question: does specifying a general term by rational evidence (rather than an explicit text) render it speculative (zanni) or leave it definitive (qat‘i)? The author argues that specification by reason is akin to an exception (istithna') and thus does not introduce uncertainty, a view supported by consensus that deniers of commands like 'establish prayer' are disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the majority view
Recognize that many scholars hold that any specification by an independent evidence (mustaqill) makes the general speculative (zanni). They do not distinguish between types of evidence.
2
Understand the author's differentiation
The author contends that specification by reason is fundamentally different: reason is not an independent textual evidence but a rational necessity. It functions like an implicit exception.
The example given: 'Allah is the Creator of everything' implicitly excludes Allah Himself, yet the verse is definitive.
3
Analyze the analogy to exception (istithna')
Exception clarifies that the excepted individuals were never intended by the general term. Reason does the same without explicit wording. Both leave the general term real (haqiqah) and definitive for the remaining individuals.
In exception, the excepted phrase is mentioned; in rational specification, it is omitted relying on reason.
4
Apply the proof from consensus
The consensus that deniers of commands like 'establish prayer' and 'give zakat' are disbelievers proves these commands are definitive, even though children and the insane are excluded by reason. If they were speculative, the denier would not be a disbeliever.
This is the author's key evidence: ijma' establishes qat‘i status.
5
State the practical consequence
Commands such as 'establish prayer' and 'give zakat' remain qat‘i, and denying them constitutes disbelief. This differentiates them from terms specified by independent speech, which become zanni.
This thamarah al-khilaf affects the severity of denial.

مات کا تفرد کہ اگر تخصیص عقل کے ذریعہ ہو تو عام باقی افراد میں قطعی رہے گا تشریح:۔ یہاں سے ماتن اپنا ایک تفرد بیان فرمارہے ہیں اور وہ یہ ہے کہ باقی علماء نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ ہر وہ عام جس میں مستقل کے قطعی ہو گا اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عقل بھی حکما استثناء ہی ہے لیکن فرق اتنا ہے کہ استثناء کے ذریعہ تخصیص میں مستی مذکور ہوتا ہے اور عقل کے ذریعہ تخصیص کے وقت مستقلی کو عقل پر اعتماد کرتے ہوئے حذف کر دیا یعنی شریعت کے دوسرے خطابات دلیل ظنی ہوں کیونکہ ان تمام میں سے بچے اور مجنون کو خاص کیا گیا ہے اور خاص بھی عقل کے ذریعہ کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ جو خطابات فرائض کے بارے میں وارد ہوئے ہیں اقیموا الصلوة اتو الزكوة وغير و يہ تمام احکامات عام ہیں اور ان تمام سے بچے اور مجنون کو معقل کے ذریعہ خاص کر لیا گیا۔ اس کے باوجود یہ ملنی نہیں ہیں قطعی ہیں کیونکہ ملنی چیز کے منکر کو کا فرنہیں کہا جاتا لیکن ان خطابات کا منکر بالا جماع کا فر ہے تو ثابت ہوا کہ عام میں عقل کے ذریعہ تخصیص کرنا شبہ اور ظن کو پیدا نہیں کرتا بلکہ جن افراد کو معقل عام میں سے خاص کرے گی وہ یقیناً خاص ہو جائیں گے اور جن کو خاص نہیں کرے گی وہ. یقینا اسی عام میں داخل رہیں گے۔ تو عام کے ان افراد کو شامل ہونے میں شبہ نہ ہوا اس لیے عام دلیل قطعی ہو گا نہ کہ دلیل ظنی۔
The addresses that come regarding obligations, because the denier of them is a disbeliever by consensus, because their specification is rational. Because specification by reason does not produce doubt. Because every individual that reason obligates its specification becomes specified, and that whose specification it does not obligate is not specified. The author's uniqueness: that if specification is by means of reason, the general will remain definitive in the remaining individuals. Commentary: Here the author states his uniqueness, and it is that other scholars stated that every general that was specified by independent evidence is a speculative proof. They did not differentiate: if the independent is speech, what is the ruling? If it is not speech, what is the ruling? Then among non-speech, what is the ruling for each type? Rather they gave one ruling for all: when specification comes to the general by independent evidence, it becomes a speculative proof. But the author stated that it is not correct to give one ruling for all forms of independent evidence; rather some of its types have different rulings, so it is necessary to differentiate among them. The detail of this difference is: if specification was made in the general by reason, the ruling of the general will be the same as in the case of exception: the general will be real in the remaining individuals and will be a definitive proof. The reason is that reason is also effectively an exception, but the difference is that in exception the excepted is mentioned, while in specification by reason, the independent is omitted relying on reason. For example, 'Allah is the Creator of everything' — this is in the ruling of 'Allah is the Creator of everything except Allah' but the 'except Allah' is omitted relying on reason. Therefore both have the same ruling: the general is a definitive proof and real in the remaining individuals. This differentiation was made because if this difference were not made, it would necessitate that Allah's blessed verse 'O you who believe, when you rise for prayer, wash your faces...' and its parallels — i.e., other shariah addresses — would be speculative proofs, because children and the insane are specified from all of them, and specification is by reason. While the addresses that come regarding obligations — 'establish prayer', 'give zakat', etc. — all these commands are general, and children and the insane are specified from them by reason. Despite this, they are not speculative; they are definitive. Because the denier of a speculative matter is not called a disbeliever, but the denier of these addresses is a disbeliever by consensus. So it is established that specification by reason in the general does not produce doubt and speculation. Rather, the individuals that reason specifies from the general will certainly be specified, and those it does not specify will certainly remain included in the general. So there is no doubt in the inclusion of these individuals, so the general is a definitive proof, not a speculative proof.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage presents a unique position of the author (al-matan) regarding the effect of specification by reason on the definitiveness of a general term. The author argues against the majority of scholars who held that any specification by independent evidence (mustaqill) renders the general speculative (zanni). The author differentiates: when the specifying evidence is reason ('aql), the general remains definitive (qat'i), just like an exception (istithna'). The rationale is that reason effectively operates like an exception but omits the explicit exceptive phrase because it relies on rational necessity. The author supports this by referring to the consensus that deniers of commands like 'establish prayer' are disbelievers, despite these commands being specified by reason to exclude children and the insane. This shows that specification by reason does not introduce doubt. The passage is an expansion probe on the matn's claim that specification by reason leaves the general definitive.

Key Terms
تخصیص بالعقل (takhsis bi al-‘aql): Specification of a general term by rational evidence, not by an independent text.
استثناء (istithna’): An explicit exceptive phrase that excludes some individuals from the general ruling.
قطعی (qat‘i): A proof that conveys certainty and whose denier is a disbeliever if it is a foundational matter.
ظنی (zanni): A proof that is speculative and whose denier is not declared a disbeliever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the effect of specification by reason (takhsis bi al-‘aql) on the general term?
A) It makes the general term speculative (zanni).
B) It renders the general term void.
C) It leaves the general term definitive (qat‘i) like an exception.
D) It has no effect; the general remains as it was.

Key Takeaway
Specification by reason (takhsis bi al-‘aql) does not render a general term speculative; it remains definitive (qat‘i) like an exception, as proven by consensus that deniers of rational obligations are disbelievers.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Specification by Independent Speech: Does the General Remain Authoritative?
Dispute on the effect of specification by independent speech on the general term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and distinguish the Hanafi positions on specification by independent speech (makhsūṣ bi al-kalām) and apply the analogy to exception to determine the effect on the general term.

Core Idea
Specification by a separate text may or may not preserve the general's authority—the dispute hinges on whether it is like exception or independent.

This passage presents a crucial usul dispute within the Hanafi school: what happens to a general (ʿāmm) when a specifying text (mukhaṣṣiṣ) comes as an independent speech? Does the general remain authoritative for the remainder, or does it lose all authority? The answer depends on whether the specifying text is known or unknown, and on how one views the relationship between specification and exception (istithnāʾ). Let's walk through the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main positions
Al-Karakhi holds that the general loses authority entirely, whether the specifying text is known or unknown. Others (al-baʿḍ) differentiate based on whether the specifying text is known or unknown.
The term 'some' (البعض) refers to unnamed Hanafi authorities who oppose al-Karakhi.
2
Understand the analogy to exception
Specification is analogized to exception (istithnāʾ): both clarify that something was never included in the general. This analogy is used to argue that known specification does not introduce uncertainty.
Exception is attached to the original speech and does not accept causation (taʿlīl).
3
Apply the criterion: known vs. unknown
For known specifications, some argue the general remains authoritative. For unknown specifications, there are two sub-views: either the general becomes unknown (like exception) or the specifying text falls without affecting the general.
The distinction between known and unknown is key to the disagreement.
4
Consider the independent nature of speech
Independent speech (kalam mustaqill) can accept causation (taʿlīl), unlike exception which is attached. This affects whether the general remains or the specifying text falls.
Al-Karakhi's position relies on the independence introducing uncertainty.
5
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Example: the general 'Kill the polytheists' (Q 9:5) and the known specifying text for musta'min (Q 9:6). According to the view of al-baʿḍ, the general remains authoritative for other polytheists; according to al-Karakhi, it does not.
The practical difference is whether one can use the general as a proof for other polytheists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا المَخصُوصُ بِالْكَلَامِ فَعِنْدَ الْكَرُخِي لَا يَبْقَى حُجَّةً أَصْلًا مَعْلُومًا كَانَ أَوْ مَجْهُولًا كَالْمُسْتَأْمَنِ) حَيْثُ خُصَّ مِنْ قَوْله تَعَالَى ( اقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ ) بِقَوْلِهِ ( وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنْ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرُهُ ). أَوْ مَجْهُولًا كَالرِّبَا حَيْثُ خُصَّ مِنْ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) وَأَحَلَّ اللَّهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ . الرِّبَا ) ( لأَنَّهُ الْعَام كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ فَإِنَّهُ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّ الْمُسْتَنَى لَمْ يَدْخُلُ فِي صَدْرِ الكَلامِ ، وَالاسْتِثْنَاء إِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا يَكُونُ الْبَاقِي فِي صَدْرِ الْكَلَامِ مَجْهُولًا وَلَا يَثْبُتُ بِهِ الْحُكْمُ . ) وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعْلُومًا فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُعَلَّلًا ؛ لِأَنَّهُ كَلامٌ مُسْتَقِلٌ ) وَالْأَصْلُ فِي النُّصُوصِ التَّعْلِيلُ ) وَلَا يُدْرَى كَمْ يَخْرُجُ بِالتَّعْلِيلِ فَيَبْقَى الْبَاقِي مَجْهُولًا ، وَعِندَ الْبَعْضِ إِنْ كَانَ مَعْلُومًا بَقِيَ الْعَامُ فِيمَا وَرَاءِ الْمَخْصُوصِ كَمَا كَانَ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ ) فِى أَنَّهُ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَدْخُلُ ) فَلا يَقْبَلُ التَّعْلِيلَ ) إِذْ الاسْتِثْنَاءُ لَا يَقْبَلُ التَّعْلِيلَ ؛ لأنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُسْتَقِلْ بِنَفْسِهِ ، وَفِى صُورَةِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ الْعَامُ حُجَّةٌ فِي الْبَاقِي كَمَا كَانَ فَكَذَا التَّخْصِيصُ ( وَإِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا لَا يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةً لِمَا قُلْنَا ) إِنَّ التَّخْصِيصَ كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ وَالاسْتِثْنَاءِ الْمَجْهُولُ يَجْعَلُ الْبَاقِيَ مَجْهُولًا فَلا يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةٌ فِي الْبَاقِي ( وَعِندَ الْبَعْضِ إِنْ كَانَ مَعْلُومًا فَكَمَا ذَكَرُنَا آنِفًا ) إِنَّ الْعَامَّ يَبْقَى فِيمَا وَرَاءِ الْمَخْصُوصِ كَمَا كَانَ ) وَإِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا يَسْقُطُ المُخَصِّصُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ كَلامٌ مُسْتَقِلْ بِخِلَافِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ وَلَمَّا كَانَ الْمُخَصِّصُ كَلامًا مُسْتَقِلًا وَكَانَ مَعْنَاهُ مَجْهُولًا يَسْقُطُ هُوَ بِنَفْسِهِ وَلَا تَتَعَدَّى جَهَالَتُهُ إِلَى صَدْرِ الْكَلامِ بِخِلَافِ الاسْتِثْنَاءِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُسْتَقِلْ بِنَفْسِهِ ، بَلْ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِصَدْر الْكَلَامِ فَجَهَالَتُهُ تَتَعَدَّى إِلَى صَدْرِ الْكَلَامِ
As for the one specified by speech, according to al-Karakhi it does not remain a proof at all, whether it is known or unknown. Example of known: the musta'min, where it is specified from Allah's saying 'Kill the polytheists' by His saying 'And if one of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection.' Example of unknown: usury (riba), where it is specified from Allah's saying 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury.' (Because if it is unknown, the remainder becomes unknown. For specification is like exception, as it clarifies that the specified did not enter. That is, specification clarifies that the specified did not fall under the general, like exception, for it clarifies that the excepted did not enter into the beginning of the speech. And exception, if it is unknown, makes the remainder in the beginning of the speech unknown, and the ruling is not established by it. And if it is known, the apparent (opinion) is that it should be subject to causation (ta'lil), because it is independent speech, and the principle in texts is causation. And it is not known how many are excluded by causation, so the remainder remains unknown. And according to some, if it is known, the general remains with respect to what is beyond the specified as it was, because it is like exception in that it clarifies that it did not enter. So it does not accept causation, since exception does not accept causation because it is not independent by itself. And in the case of exception, the general is a proof in the remainder as it was, so too specification. And if it is unknown, the general does not remain a proof for what we said: that specification is like exception, and an unknown exception renders the remainder unknown, so the general does not remain a proof in the remainder. And according to some, if it is known, it is as we mentioned earlier: the general remains with respect to what is beyond the specified as it was. And if it is unknown, the specifying text falls, because it is independent speech, unlike exception. Since the specifying text is independent speech and its meaning is unknown, it falls by itself, and its ignorance does not transfer to the beginning of the speech, unlike exception, because it is not independent by itself, but rather it is attached to the beginning of the speech, so its ignorance transfers to the beginning of the speech.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of specification by an independent speech (kalam mustaqill) on the general term. It presents a dispute: al-Karakhi holds that such specification eliminates the general's authority entirely, whether the specifying text is known or unknown. Others differentiate. The passage provides examples: the known case of the musta'min (protected person) specified from the general command 'kill the polytheists' by a later verse granting protection; and the unknown case of riba (usury) specified from 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' — the term riba is ambiguous. The argument centers on whether specification is analogous to exception (istithna'). If the specifying text is known, some argue that the general remains authoritative in the remainder because specification, like exception, does not accept causation (ta'lil) and simply indicates that the specified was never included. If it is unknown, there are two views: one that the general becomes unknown (like exception), and another that the specifying text itself falls but the general remains unaffected because the specifying text is independent and its ambiguity does not taint the original speech. The passage is an expansion probe explaining the different positions.

Key Terms
مخصوص بالكلام (makhsūṣ bi al-kalām): A general term that has been specified by an independent speech (a separate text).
استثناء (istithnā’): An exceptive phrase that excludes some individuals from the general ruling.
تعليل (ta‘līl): The process of assigning a cause or ratio legis (ʻillah) to a ruling.
جهالة (jahālah): The quality of being unknown or ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of a known specifying text according to the view that it is like exception?
A) General becomes unknown
B) General remains a proof for the remainder
C) General loses authority entirely
D) Both general and specifying text become inoperative

Key Takeaway
Specification by independent speech sparks an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Karakhi rejects the general's authority entirely, while others differentiate based on whether the specifying text is known or unknown.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
7 min
Effect of Takhsis on the Authority of the General
Dispute over whether general remains hujjah after specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position on the hujjiyyah of a general text after specification from al-Karkhi's view and explain the role of ambiguity (shubhah).

Core Idea
After specification, the general is not void; ambiguity lingers, preventing absolute authority.

When Allah commands to 'kill the polytheists' (general), but then says 'if any polytheist seeks protection, grant it' (specifier), does the original command still obligate killing all other polytheists? This lesson unpacks the usul debate on the authority of a specified general. Al-Karkhi argued it loses all force; others distinguished known vs. unknown specifiers; the Hanafi school identifies ambiguity (shubhah) as the key intermediate position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
The debate is whether a general text ('amm) remains a hujjah (binding proof) for the remaining individuals after it has been specified (takhsis) by another evidence.
The issue hinges on whether specification is analogous to exception (istithna') and whether the specifier introduces uncertainty.
2
Understand al-Karkhi's View
Al-Karkhi holds that the general loses its authority entirely, whether the specifier is known or unknown. He reasons: specification is like exception; exception when unknown makes the remainder unknown; even when known, speculation about how many are excluded makes the remainder unknown.
Al-Karkhi treats the specifier as kalam mustaqil (independent) that is subject to ta'lil, leading to ambiguity.
3
Examine the Alternative View
Some scholars (al-ba'd) distinguish: if the specifier is known, the general remains authoritative (like exception), and the specifier does not accept ta'lil because it is dependent; if unknown, the specifier itself falls because it is independent, leaving the general intact.
This view treats the specifier differently based on whether it is independent (ta'lil accepted) or dependent (like exception, no ta'lil).
4
Grasp the Hanafi Position (indana)
The Hanafi school says there is an ambiguity (shubhah). We know the literal meaning (all individuals) is not intended, but we cannot fix a specific number below the total because any number would be arbitrary preference (tarjih bila murajjih). Hence, the general is not qat'i but retains some probative value.
The Hanafi position avoids both extremes: it does not discard the general nor treat it as untouched.
5
Compare Practical Consequences
The thamarah al-khilaf: for example, after the verse 'kill the polytheists' is specified by the protection verse, does the general still obligate killing all other polytheists? According to Hanafis, yes, but with possible limitations; according to al-Karkhi, no.
This affects how jurists derive rulings from similar general texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حَيْثُ خُصَّ مِنْ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) وَأَحَلَّ اللَّهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ . الرِّبَا ) ( لأَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا صَارَ الْبَاقِي مَجْهُولًا ؛ لِأَنَّ التَّخْصِيصَ كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ إذْ هُوَ ، وَالاسْتِثْنَاء إِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا يَكُونُ الْبَاقِي فِي صَدْرِ الْكَلَامِ مَجْهُولًا وَلَا يَثْبُتُ بِهِ الْحُكْمُ . ) وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعْلُومًا فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُعَلَّلًا؛ لِأَنَّهُ وَرَاءِ الْمَخْصُوصِ كَمَا كَانَ؛ لِأَنَّهُ كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ ) فِى أَنَّهُ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَدْخُلُ ) فَلا يَقْبَلُ التَّعْلِيلَ ) إِذْ الاسْتِثْنَاءُ لَا يَقْبَلُ التَّعْلِيلَ؛ لأنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُسْتَقِلْ بِنَفْسِهِ ، وَفِى صُورَةِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ الْعَامُ حُجَّةٌ فِي الْبَاقِي كَمَا كَانَ فَكَذَا التَّخْصِيصُ ( وَإِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا لَا يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةً لِمَا قُلْنَا ) إِنَّ التَّخْصِيصَ كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ وَالاسْتِثْنَاءِ الْمَجْهُولُ يَجْعَلُ الْبَاقِيَ مَجْهُولًا فَلا يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةٌ فِي الْبَاقِي ( وَعِندَ الْبَعْضِ إِنْ كَانَ مَعْلُومًا فَكَمَا ذَكَرُنَا آنِفًا ) إِنَّ الْعَامَّ يَبْقَى فِيمَا وَرَاءِ الْمَخْصُوصِ كَمَا كَانَ ) وَإِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا يَسْقُطُ المُخَصِّصُ؛ لِأَنَّهُ كَلامٌ مُسْتَقِلْ بِخِلَافِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ وَلَمَّا كَانَ الْمُخَصِّصُ كَلامًا مُسْتَقِلًا وَكَانَ مَعْنَاهُ مَجْهُولًا يَسْقُطُ هُوَ بِنَفْسِهِ وَلَا تَتَعَدَّى جَهَالَتُهُ إِلَى صَدْرِ الْكَلامِ بِخِلَافِ الاسْتِثْنَاءِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُسْتَقِلْ بِنَفْسِهِ ، بَلْ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِصَدْر الْكَلَامِ فَجَهَالَتُهُ تَتَعَدَّى إِلَى صَدْرِ الْكَلَامِ ( وَعِندَنَا تَمَكَّنَ فِيهِ شُبُهَةٌ؛ لأنَّهُ عُلِمَ أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مَحْمُولٍ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ) وَهُوَ إرَادَةُ الكُلِّ فَعْلِمَ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ الْبَعْضُ بِطَرِيقِ الْمَجَازِ مَثَلًا إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ أَفْرَادِهِ مِائَةٌ، وَعُلِمَ أَنَّ الْمِائَةَ غَيْرُ مُرَادَةٍ فَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَعْدَادِ الَّتِي دُونَ الْمِائَةِ مُسَاءٍ فِي أَنَّ اللَّفْظَ مَجَارٌ فِيهِ فَلَا يَبُتُ عَدَدٌ مُعَيَّنْ مِنْهَا؛ لِأَنَّهُ تَرْجِيحٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ مُرَجْحٍ.
ترجمہ :۔ ( اور بہر حال وہ عام کہ جس میں تخصیص کی گئی ہو کلام کے ذرعیہ سے پس امام کرخی کے ہاں وہ نہیں باقی رہتا حجت بالکل مخصوص معلوم ہو جیسے مستامن اس حیثیت سے کہ خاص کیا گیا اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول اقتلو المشرکین سے اس کے قول وان احد من المشرکین استجارک فاجرہ “ کے ساتھ (یا مجہول ہو جیسے ربط ) اس حیثیت سے کہ تخصیص کی گئی ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول واحـل اللـه البيع ۔۔۔ الآیہ سے ( کیونکہ اگر وہ مجہول ہو تو ہو جائیں گے باقی افراد مجہول کیونکہ تخصیص مثل استثناء کے ہے اس لیے کہ وہ بیان کرتی ہے کہ بے شک وہ داخل نہیں ہے ) یعنی تخصیص بیان کرتی ہے اس بات کو کہ بے شک مخصوص داخل نہیں ہے عام کے تحت اشتغناء کی طرح کیونکہ وہ بیان کرتے ہے کہ بے شک مستی نہیں ہے داخل صدر کلام میں اور استثناء جب مجہول ہو تو ہوں گے باقی افراد بھی صدر کلام سے مجہول اور نہیں ثابت ہوگا اس کے ساتھ حکم ( اور اگر وہ وہ معلوم تو ظاہر ہے کہ ہوگا وہ معلل کیونکہ وہ کلام مستقل ہے ) اور اصل نصوص میں تعلیل ہے ( اور نہیں ہے معلوم کتنے افراد نکلے ہیں تعلیل کے ساتھ پس بچ گئے باقی افراد مجہول اور بعض حضرات کے نزدیک اگر ہو وہ (مخصص ) معلوم تو باقی رہے گا عام مخصوص کے ماوراء افراد میں جیسا کہ وہ تھا کیونکہ وہ مثل استثناء کے ہے اس بات میں کہ بے شک وہ بیان کرتا ہے کہ بے شک وہ داخل نہیں ہے پس وہ نہیں قبول کرے گا تعلیل کو ) کیونکہ استثناء نہیں قبول کرتا تعلیل کو کیونکہ وہ بذات خود غیر مستقل ہے اور استثناء کی صورت میں عام حجت ہوتا ہے باقی افراد میں جیسا کہ وہ پہلے تھا پس اسی طرح ہوگا حکم تخصیص کا ( اور اگر ہو وہ مجہول تو نہیں باقی رہے گا عام حجت بوجہ اس کے جو ہم نے کہا) تحقیق تخصیص مثل استثناء کے ہے اور استثناء مجہول بنا دیتا ہے باقی کو مجہول پس نہیں باقی رہتا عام حجت باقی میں اور بعض حضرات کے نزدیک اگر وہ معلوم ہو تو پھر اسی طرح حکم ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے ابھی ذکر کیا ہے ) کہ بے شک عام باقی رہے گا مخصوص کے ماوراء میں جیسا کہ وہ تھا ( اور اگر وہ مجہول ہو تو ساقط ہو جائے گا مخصص کیونکہ وہ کلام مستقل ہے بخلاف استثناء کے ) اور جب ہو شخص کلام مستقل ہو اس کا معنی مجبول تو ساقط ہو جاتا ہے وہ بذات خود اور نہیں متعدی ہوتی اس کی جہالت صدر کلام کی طرف بخلاف استثناء کے کیونکہ وہ بذات خود غیر مستقل ہے بلکہ وہ متعلق ہوتا ہے صدر کلام کے ساتھ پس اس کی جہالت متعدی ہوگی صدر کلام کی طرف ( اور ہمارے ہاں پختہ ہو جاتا ہے اس
The specified (makhsus) is like the musta'man, where the general command 'kili the polytheists' is specified by 'if one of the polytheists seeks your protection, grant him protection'. Or unknown like riba, where the general 'God made sale lawful and forbade riba' is specified. Because if it is unknown, the remainder becomes unknown, for specification is like exception (istithna'), as it shows that the specified did not enter under the general. Exception, when unknown, makes the remainder in the first part of the statement unknown, and the ruling is not established by it. If it is known, then apparent that it is subject to ta'lil (causal reasoning), because it is an independent statement, and the principle in texts is ta'lil, and one does not know how many are excluded by ta'lil, so the remainder remains unknown. Some hold that if it is known, the general remains as it was over the remaining individuals, because it is like exception in that it shows non-entry, so it does not accept ta'lil, since exception does not accept ta'lil because it is not independent. In the case of exception, the general is a proof for the remainder as it was, so likewise specification. If it is unknown, the general does not remain a proof due to what we said: specification is like exception, and unknown exception makes the remainder unknown, so the general is not a proof for the remainder. Some hold: if known, as we mentioned, the general remains over what is beyond the specified; if unknown, the specifier (mukhassis) falls, because it is an independent statement unlike exception. Since the specifier is an independent statement and its meaning is unknown, it itself falls, and its unknownness does not extend to the first part of the statement, unlike exception because it is not independent but attached to the first part, so its unknownness extends. According to us, there is an ambiguity in it, because it is known that it is not taken literally (i.e., intending all), so it is known that only some is intended by way of metaphor. For example, if all its individuals are one hundred, and it is known that one hundred is not intended, then every number below one hundred is in doubt as to whether the word applies to it, so no specific number is established, because that would be preference without a preferrer.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tarwih discusses the effect of specification (takhsis) on the authority (hujjiyyah) of a general statement ('amm). The author presents the view of Imam al-Karkhi and others, and then gives the Hanafi position (indana). The central issue: when a general text (like 'kill the polytheists') is specified by a distinct evidence (like the verse about granting protection), does the general remain a binding proof for the remaining individuals not covered by the specification? Al-Karkhi holds that after specification, the general is no longer a hujjah for the remaining individuals, regardless of whether the specifying evidence is known (ma'lum) or unknown (majhul). His reasoning: specification is like exception (istithna') in that it clarifies that the specified items were never intended by the general. Exception, when unknown, makes the remainder unknown; similarly, specification—even when known—introduces uncertainty because it is an independent statement subject to causal reasoning (ta'lil), and one cannot determine the precise scope of exclusion, so the remainder remains unknown. In contrast, some scholars (al-ba'd) argue that if the specifier is known, the general remains authoritative for the remainder, exactly as in exception. They reason that just as exception does not accept ta'lil due to its dependence on the general statement, specification—being analogous—should not accept ta'lil either. However, if the specifier is unknown, they hold that the specifier itself falls (since it is independent and its meaning is ambiguous) but the general statement's authority over the remainder is unaffected, unlike exception where unknownness extends to the first part. Finally, the Hanafi position (indana) is that there is an ambiguity (shubhah) in the general after specification. Since it is known that the literal meaning (all members) is not intended, the intended number is uncertain. For example, if the general covers 100, and we know not all 100 are meant, we cannot pinpoint whether it is 99, 50, etc., because any specific number would be an arbitrary preference (tarjih bila murajjih). Hence, the general cannot serve as a definitive proof for a specific number of remaining individuals. This lesson is a classic usul al-fiqh debate on the linguistic and legal implications of specification.

Key Terms
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Specification: removing some individuals from the scope of a general term using a separate evidence.
المخصص (al-mukhassis): The evidence that specifies the general, e.g., a verse or hadith that limits a general command.
الاستثناء (al-istithna'): Linguistic exception: excluding something from a statement using 'illa' or similar particles.
الحجية (al-hujjiyyah): Authority or probative value of a text as evidence for legal rulings.
الشبهة (al-shubhah): Ambiguity or doubt about the exact scope of the general after specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi position (indana) on the general after specification?
A) The general becomes completely void and cannot be used as evidence.
B) The general remains fully authoritative for the remaining individuals exactly as before.
C) There is ambiguity (shubhah) because the literal meaning is not intended, so no specific number of remaining individuals can be fixed.
D) The specifier falls, and the general is unaffected.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a general text after specification retains some probative value but is clouded by ambiguity (shubhah), preventing it from being a definitive proof for a specific number of remaining individuals.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
The First Two Madhahib on the Authority of a Specified General Text ('Am Makhsus 'Inda al-Ba'd)
Explains two scholarly views (madhhab) on the authority of a general text specified by speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam al-Karkhi and al-ba'd regarding the authority of a general text specified by speech, and explain the analogical reasoning (qiyas) each school uses.

Core Idea
A general text that has been partially specified loses all authority according to al-Karkhi, but retains definitive authority if the specification is known according to al-ba'd.

This passage introduces a fundamental dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: what happens to a general ruling (hukm 'amm) when part of its scope is excluded by another textual evidence? Two views are presented: that of Imam al-Karkhi, who argues the general loses all authority, and that of 'some scholars' (al-ba'd), who distinguish based on whether the specification is known or unknown. The debate hinges on analogies with istithna' (exception) and naskh (abrogation), which are explained in a preface.

Guided Path
1
Understand the preface: istithna' and naskh
Identify the two types of istithna' (known/unknown excepted item) and naskh (known/unknown abrogator). Note that istithna' is non-independent (ghayr mustaqill) and does not admit ta'lil; naskh is independent (mustaqill) and admits ta'lil.
This distinction is the foundation for the analogies.
2
Identify Imam al-Karkhi's position
He holds that a general specified by speech (whether the specified part is known or unknown) does not remain a proof (hujjah) in the remaining individuals, neither definitively (qat'i) nor probabilistically (zanni).
3
Analyze Imam al-Karkhi's proof
If the specification is unknown, it resembles istithna' (causing uncertainty in the general). If known, it resembles naskh (which admits ta'lil); the possibility that the 'illah extends to other individuals creates uncertainty. Thus in both cases the general loses authority.
The Quranic examples illustrate the two cases: known (protected polytheist) and unknown (definition of riba).
4
Identify the second school's position (al-ba'd)
These scholars distinguish: if the specified part is known, the general remains a definitive proof for the remaining individuals; if unknown, the general loses authority altogether.
5
Analyze the second school's proof
They analogize specification entirely to istithna', which does not accept ta'lil. Thus even a known specification does not introduce uncertainty; the general remains definitive for all individuals except those explicitly excluded.
This view treats ta'lil as irrelevant to specification.

عام مخصوص عند البعض کے حکم کے بارے میں چار مذاہب کا بیان
تشریح:- ماتن عام خص عند البعض (وہ عام جس میں کلام کے ذریعہ تخصیص کی گئی ہو) کا حکم بیان فرمایا ہے اور اس کے حکم میں چار مذاہب ہیں ان چار مذاہب سے پہلے ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں۔
مقدمہ: استثناء دوطرح کا ہوتا ہے۔ بعض دفعہ تو مستثنی معلوم ہوتا ہے اور بعض دفعہ مجہول اگر مستثنی معلوم ہوتو مستثنی منہ کے تحت باقی افراد میں حکم قطعی طور پر ثابت ہوتا ہے اور اگر مستثنی مجہول ہوتو مستثنی منہ بھی مجہول ہو جاتا ہے اور حکم کسی فرد میں قطعا ثابت نہیں ہوتا اور استثناء دونوں صورتوں میں غیر مستقل ہوتا ہے یعنی صدر کلام پر معلق ہوتا ہے۔ اور نسخ بھی دو طرح کا ہوتا ہے بعض دفعہ تاریخ معلوم ہوتا اور بعض دفعہ تاریخ مجہول ہوتا اگر ناسخ معلوم ہو تو منسوخ قطعا ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ناسخ کا حکم باقی رہ جاتا ہے اور اگر ناسخ مجہول ہو تو یہ ناسخ خود ساقط ہو جاتا ہے منسوخ میں کوئی فرق نہیں پڑتا بلکہ اس کے تمام افراد میں حکم باقی رہتا ہے اور تاریخ دونوں صورتوں میں کلام مستقل ہوتا ہے۔
پہلا مذہب
عام خص عند البعض بالکلام کا حکم: اس میں چار مذہب ہیں۔ (۱) پہلا مذہب امام کرخی کا ہے یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ عام جس میں کلام کے ذریعہ سے تخصیص کی گئی ہو۔ اس میں مخصوص خواہ معلوم ہو خواہ مجہول ہو وہ عام باقی افراد میں حجت نہیں رہتا نہ قطعی طور پر نہ ظنی طور پر مخصوص معلوم ہو جیسے قرآن پاک میں ہے "اقتلوا المشركين حيث وجدتموهم"، اس میں سے مستامن کو خاص کیا گیا ہے ایک اور آیت کے ذریعہ اور وہ ہے "فإن أحد من المشركين استجارك فأجره" یہاں مخصوص معلوم ہے یعنی مستامن اور مخصوص مجہول ہو جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان "وأحل الله البيع وحرم الربا" بیع میں سے ربا کو مخصوص کیا گیا ہے لیکن یہ ربا مجہول ہے کیونکہ ربا کا معنی ہے زیادتی اور زیادتی ہر بیع میں ہوتی ہے تو یہاں کون سی زیادتی کو خاص کیا گیا ہے؟ یہ معلوم نہیں ہے۔
دلیل: امام کرخی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب عام میں کلام کے ذریعہ تخصیص کی جائے تو مخصوص میں دو احتمال ہیں۔ کہ وہ معلوم ہوگا یا مجہول اگر مخصوص مجہول ہو تو اس کو استثناء کے ساتھ مشابہت ہوگی اور استثناء میں یہ بات ہے کہ مستثنی مجہول ہو تو مستثنی منہ بھی مجہول ہو جاتا ہے اور حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا تو یہاں بھی جب مخصوص مجہول ہو گا تو اس کی وجہ سے عام کے باقی افراد میں جہالت آجائے گی اور کسی فرد میں حکم ثابت نہیں ہو گا اس لیے عام حجت نہیں رہے گا باقی رہی یہ بات کہ اس تخصیص کو استثناء کے ساتھ مشابہت کیوں ہے؟ تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح استثناء اس بات کو بیان کرتا ہے کہ مستثنیٰ صدر کلام (مستثنی منہ) میں داخل نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح تخصیص میں بھی اس بات کو بیان کیا جاتا ہے کہ مخصوص عام میں داخل نہیں ہے تو دونوں ایک دوسرے کے مشابہ ہوئے۔ اور اگر مخصوص معلوم ہو تو اس کو نسخ کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے اور ناسخ مستقل کلام ہوتا ہے اور مستقل کلام میں تعلیل کا احتمال ہوتا ہے لہذا یہ مخصوص بھی معلل ہو گا یعنی مطلب یہ ہے کہ جن افراد کو عام سے خاص کیا گیا ہے ان کو کسی علت کے تحت خاص کیا گیا ہے اور اس علت کے بارے میں احتمال ہے کہ یہ عام کے بقیہ افراد میں پائی جاسکتی ہے۔ تو بقیہ افراد میں سے جن جن میں علت پائی جائے گی وہ بھی عام سے نکل کر مخصوص بنتے جائیں گے تو اگر مخصوص معلوم ہو تو عام چونکہ مستقل کلام ہے اس لیے اس کے بقیہ افراد میں تعلیل کا احتمال ہو گا جب تعلیل کا احتمال ہے تو ہمیں یہ معلوم نہیں ہوگا کہ عام کے کتنے افراد میں تعلیل ہو رہی ہے اور کتنے افراد عام کے تحت باقی ہیں جب یہ معلوم نہیں ہو گا تو عام کے باقی افراد مجہول ہو گئے اور کسی فرد میں حکم ثابت نہیں ہو گا اس لیے امام کرخی فرماتے ہیں کہ عام کسی صورت میں بھی دلیل نہیں بنتا نہ قطعی طور پر نہ ظنی طور پر۔
دوسرا مذہب
(۲) وعند البعض: بعض حضرات نے یہ کہا ہے کہ عام میں جب کلام کے ذریعہ تخصیص کی جائے تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ مخصوص معلوم ہے یا مجہول۔ اگر مخصوص معلوم ہو تو عام باقی افراد میں حجت قطعیہ ہو گا اور اگر مخصوص مجہول ہو تو عام حجت نہیں رہے گا نہ قطعی طور پر نہ ظنی طور پر۔
دلیل: یہ حضرات تخصیص کو بالکل استثناء سے تشبیہ دیتے ہیں چاہے مخصوص معلوم ہو یا مجہول ہو اور وجہ یہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ جس طرح استثناء میں یہ بیان کیا جاتا ہے کہ مستثنیٰ مستثنی منہ میں داخل نہیں ہے اسی طرح تخصیص میں بھی یہ بیان کیا جاتا ہے کہ مخصوص عام میں داخل نہیں ہے لہذا دونوں ایک دوسرے کے مشابہ ہیں۔ تو جب تخصیص استثناء کی طرح ہے تو جس طرح مستثنی معلوم ہو تو مستثنی منہ میں حکم قطعاً ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں اگر مخصوص معلوم ہوگا تو عام کے باقی افراد میں حکم قطعا ثابت ہوگا اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ تعلیل کو قبول نہیں کرتا کیونکہ یہ استثناء کی طرح ہے اور استثناء تعلیل کو قبول نہیں کرتا کیونکہ تعلیل
Statement of the four schools regarding the ruling of the general specified for some. Explanation: The author (matn) states the ruling of 'am khuss 'inda al-ba'd (the general which is specified by speech). There are four schools regarding its ruling. Before these four schools, understand a preface. Preface: Istithna' (exception) is of two types: sometimes the excepted item is known, sometimes unknown. If the excepted item is known, the ruling is established with certainty among the remaining individuals of the excepted-from category. If the excepted item is unknown, the excepted-from also becomes unknown, and the ruling is not established with certainty in any individual. In both cases, istithna' is non-independent, i.e., it is attached to the earlier part of the speech. Naskh (abrogation) is also of two types: sometimes the date is known, sometimes unknown. If the abrogator is known, the abrogated is completely removed and the ruling of the abrogator remains. If the abrogator is unknown, the abrogator itself falls away, nothing changes in the abrogated, rather the ruling remains among all its individuals. In both cases, the speech is independent. First school: The ruling of 'am khuss 'inda al-ba'd bil kalam: There are four schools. (1) The first school is of Imam al-Karkhi. He says: That general which is specified by speech, whether the specified part is known or unknown, it does not remain a proof (hujjah) in the remaining individuals, neither definitively nor probabilistically. For example, when the specified is known, like the Quranic verse 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' (9:5), from which the protected polytheist is excluded by another verse 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection' (9:6). Here the specified (the protected person) is known. And when the specified is unknown, like the saying of Allah 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' (2:275), where usury is specified from trade but usury is unknown because usury means increase and increase occurs in every trade, so which specific increase is specified? That is not known. Proof: Imam al-Karkhi says: When a general is specified by speech, the specified part has two possibilities: it is either known or unknown. If the specified is unknown, it resembles istithna'. In istithna', if the excepted item is unknown, the excepted-from also becomes unknown and the ruling is not established. So here too, when the specified is unknown, ignorance enters the remaining individuals of the general and the ruling is not established in any individual, so the general does not remain a proof. As for why this specification resembles istithna', the reason is that just as istithna' indicates that the excepted item is not included in the earlier part of the sentence (the excepted-from), similarly specification indicates that the specified is not included in the general, so both are similar. And if the specified is known, it resembles naskh. An abrogator is independent speech, and independent speech admits ta'lil (rationale). So this specified part will also be mu'allal, meaning that the individuals excluded from the general are excluded due to some 'illah, and it is possible that this 'illah may be found in the remaining individuals. Then whichever remaining individuals possess the 'illah will also exit the general and become specified. So if the specified is known, since the general is independent speech, there is a possibility of ta'lil in its remaining individuals. When ta'lil is possible, we do not know how many individuals are subject to ta'lil and how many remain under the general. When that is unknown, the remaining individuals of the general become unknown, and the ruling is not established in any individual. Therefore Imam al-Karkhi says that the general does not serve as a proof in any case, neither definitively nor probabilistically. Second school: (2) 'And according to some': Some scholars have said: When a general is specified by speech, it is considered whether the specified is known or unknown. If the specified is known, the general is a definitive proof in the remaining individuals. If the specified is unknown, the general does not remain a proof, neither definitively nor probabilistically. Proof: These scholars liken specification entirely to istithna', whether the specified is known or unknown. They give the reason that just as in istithna' it is stated that the excepted item is not included in the excepted-from, similarly in specification it is stated that the specified is not included in the general, so both are similar. Thus, when specification is like istithna', just as when the excepted item is known, the ruling is definitively established in the excepted-from, similarly here if the specified is known, the ruling will be definitively established in the remaining individuals of the general. The reason is that it does not accept ta'lil because it is like istithna', and istithna' does not accept ta'lil because ta'lil...
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage discusses a key dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: what is the ruling of a general text ('am) that has been partially specified (makhsus) through another scriptural text (kalam)? The author first sets up a comparative framework by explaining two analogous concepts: istithna' (exception) and naskh (abrogation). In istithna', the excepted item may be known or unknown; if unknown, the excepted-from category also becomes ambiguous. In naskh, the abrogator may be known or unknown; if unknown, the abrogator itself is ineffective. The first madhhab, attributed to Imam al-Karkhi, argues that regardless of whether the specified part is known or unknown, a general that has been partially specified loses all authority (hujjiyah) in its remaining scope—neither definitive (qat'i) nor probable (zanni). His proof uses analogy: if the specified is unknown, it is like istithna' (causing ambiguity); if known, it is like naskh (allowing for ta'lil, which may extend the specification indefinitely). The second madhhab, attributed to 'some scholars' (al-ba'd), distinguishes: if the specified is known, the general remains a definitive proof; if unknown, it loses all authority. They argue that specification is entirely analogous to istithna', which does not accept ta'lil, so no extension occurs. The passage thus presents the first two of four schools, with detailed analogical reasoning. The Hanafi position on this issue is nuanced; many later Hanafis follow the second view when the specified is known, but the dispute shows the depth of usul thinking.

Key Terms
عام مخصوص عند البعض ('am makhsus 'inda al-ba'd): A general term (عام) that has been partially specified (خصص) by a separate textual evidence, leaving the remaining individuals ambiguous in authority according to some scholars.
استثناء (istithna'): A grammatical exception (e.g., 'except') that removes an item from a general ruling. In this context, it serves as an analogy for specification: both indicate non-inclusion of the excepted/specified item.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a previous ruling by a later revelation. In this passage, it is used as an analogy for specification when the specified is known: like naskh, it is independent and may admit ta'lil.
تعلیل (ta'lil): Providing a rationale or legal cause ('illah) for a ruling. In this passage, it is central: naskh admits ta'lil, istithna' does not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Karkhi, what is the status of a general text that has been partially specified by a separate text (kalam)?
A) It remains a definitive proof (hujjah qat'iyyah) in the remaining individuals.
B) It loses all authority, both definitive and probable, regardless of whether the specified part is known or unknown.
C) It loses authority only if the specified part is unknown; otherwise it remains a proof.
D) It remains a probable proof (hujjah zanniyyah) but not definitive.

Key Takeaway
The authority of a specified general text is disputed: Imam al-Karkhi holds it loses all authority, while al-ba'd holds it remains definitive if the specification is known.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Four Mazahib on Takhsis of 'Amm by Kalam
Presents four opinions on whether 'amm remains hujjah after verbal specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four positions on whether 'amm remains a proof after takhsis by kalam and apply the Hanafi view that it remains a zanni hujjah.

Core Idea
After takhsis by kalam, the 'amm remains a proof, but only speculative (zanni), not definitive.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute: Once a general text is specified by a separate speech, does its remaining generality still count as proof? Four schools answer differently. The Hanafi position, the fourth, holds that the 'amm continues to be a valid proof, but its strength is reduced to speculative (zanni). Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to evaluate the authority of general texts after specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four positions
List the four mazahib: (1) Imam al-Karkhi: 'amm is never a proof after takhsis; (2) some hold: if specific is known, 'amm is qati; if unknown, no proof at all; (3) some hold: if specific is known, 'amm is qati; if unknown, the specification itself falls away and 'amm remains fully general; (4) Hanafis: 'amm remains a proof but zanni regardless.
The dispute hinges on whether the 'amm is considered independent speech or dependent on the specification.
2
Analyze the analogical reasoning (qiyas)
Each position uses analogy to exception (istithna') or abrogation (naskh). For example, al-Karkhi compares unknown specific to unknown excepted; the second school compares specification exactly to exception; the third compares to abrogation; the Hanafis reject both as perfect analogies.
The Hanafis argue that specification is unlike exception because it is a separate speech, and unlike abrogation because it does not completely remove the ruling.
3
Understand the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafis state that after takhsis, the 'amm is no longer used in its original generic meaning. Therefore it cannot be qati. But it is still a valid proof because the remaining individuals are known through the specification; it is thus zanni. The proof relies on the fact that the 'amm is not completely nullified.
This reflects the Hanafi preference for istihsan and practical use of zanni proofs.
4
Apply to a real Quranic example
Consider the general command 'kill the polytheists' (9:5) specified by later verses or hadith. Hanafis say the remaining generality (e.g., polytheists who are not given quarter) is a zanni proof, not definitively binding.
Contrast with the Shafi'i view that the 'amm after specification remains qati if the specific is known.
