دوسرا مذہب
(۲) وعند البعض :۔ بعض حضرات نے یہ کہا ہے کہ عام میں جب کلام کے ذریعہ تخصیص کی جائے تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ مخصوص معلوم ہے یا مجہول ۔ اگر مخصوص معلوم ہو تو عام باقی افراد میں حجت قطعیہ ہو گا اور اگر مخصوص مجہول ہو تو عام حجت نہیں رہے گا نہ قطعی طور پر نہ ملنی طور پر ۔
دلیل: یہ حضرات تخصیص کو بالکل استثناء سے تشبیہ دیتے ہیں چاہے مخصوص معلوم ہو یا مجہول ہو اور وجہ یہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ جس طرح استثناء میں یہ بیان کیا جاتا ہے کہ مستغنی مستثنی منہ میں داخل نہیں ہے اسی طرح تخصیص میں بھی یہ بیان کیا جاتا ہے کہ مخصوص عام میں داخل نہیں ہے لہذا دونوں ایک دوسرے کے مشابہ ہیں۔ تو جب تخصیص استثناء کی طرح ہے تو جس طرح مستفی معلوم ہو تو مستثنی منہ میں حکم قطعاً ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں اگر مخصوص معلوم ہوگا تو عام کے باقی افراد میں حکم قطعا ثابت ہوگا اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ تعلیل کو قبول نہیں کرتا کیونکہ یہ استثناء کی طرح ہے اور استثناء تعلیل کو قبول نہیں کرتا کیونکہ تعلیل مستقل کلام میں ہوتی ہے اور مستقلی مستقل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صدر کلام کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے تو جب یہ مخصوص تعلیل کو قبول نہیں کرتا تو عام کے باقی افراد میں جہالت لازم نہیں آئے گی تو ان میں حکم قطعا ثابت ہو جائے گا اس لیے مخصوص معلوم ہونے کی صورت میں عام بقیہ افراد میں حجت قطعیہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر مخصوص مجہول ہو تو پھر چونکہ اس کو مستی مجہول کے ساتھ مشابہت ہو گی تو جس طرح مستقلی مجبول منتقلی منہ میں جہالت پیدا کرتا ہے اسی طرح مخصوص مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں یہ مخصوص عام کے بقیہ افراد میں جہالت پیدا کر دے گا تو مستثنی منہ کی طرح عام میں بھی حکم ثابت نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لیے اس صورت میں عام بالکل حجت نہیں رہے گا۔
تیسرا مذہب
(۳) وعند البعض : بعض حضرات کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اگر مخصوص معلوم ہو تو عام اپنے بقیہ افراد میں حجت قطعیہ رہے گا اور اگر مخصوص مجہول ہو تو مخصص ہی ساقط ہو جائے گا عام میں کچھ فرق نہیں آئے گا تو عام اپنے تمام افراد کو قطعا شامل ہو گا یعنی یہ سمجھنا جائے گا کہ تخصیص کی ہی نہیں گئی بلکہ عام اپنی اصل حالت میں باقی ہے۔
دلیل تخصیص شیخ کے مشابہ ہے کہ جس طرح شیخ میں پاسخ مستقل کلام ہوتا ہے اور شیخ میں یہ بات ہے کہ اگر تاریخ معلوم ہو تو منسوخ ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور حکم انہیں افراد میں ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ جو ناسخ کے تحت باقی رہتے ہیں۔ اس لیے یہاں بھی جب مخصوص معلوم ہوگا تو حکم انہیں افراد میں باقی رہ جائے گا جو عام کے تحت باقی ہیں تو عام ان میں حجت قطعی ہوگا ۔ اور اگر مخصص مجہول ہو تو یہ ناسخ مجہول کے مشابہ ہو جائے گا اور ناسخ مجہول خود ساقط ہو جاتا ہے منسوخ میں کچھ فرق نہیں پڑتا ۔ اس لیے یہاں مخصوص مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں مخصوص خود ساقط ہو جائے گا عاما کچھ فرق نہیں پڑے گا بلکہ وہ اپنے تمام افراد میں قطعی ہوگا۔
چوتھا مذ ہب احناف کا ہے
(۴) و عند ناممکن فیہ شبہہ :۔ احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ عام میں اگر کلام کے ذریعے تخصیص کر دی جائے تو مخصوص معلوم ہو یا مجہول دونوں صورتوں میں عام اپنے باقی افراد میں حجت ہوگا لیکن حجت خلفیہ ہوگا۔
دلیل:۔ عام میں جب تخصیص کر دی جائے تو وہ اپنے حقیقی معنی پرنہیں رہتا کیونکہ عام کا منی حقیقی اور معنی موضوع لہ عموم ہے لیکن جب اس میں تخصیص کر دی جائے گی تو یہ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں مستعمل نہیں رہتا مخصوص معلوم ہونے کی صورت میں
Proof: Imam al-Karkhi says that when the general is specified by speech, the specific [part] has two possibilities: it may be known or unknown. If the specific is unknown, it resembles exception, and in exception, if the excepted is unknown, the object of exception becomes unknown and the ruling is not established. So here too, when the specific is unknown, ignorance will occur in the remaining individuals of the general, and no ruling will be established. Therefore the general will not be a proof. As for why this specification resembles exception: just as exception indicates that the excepted is not included in the initial statement, specification indicates that the specific is not included in the general, so both resemble each other. And if the specific is known, it resembles abrogation (naskh); the abrogator is an independent statement, and an independent statement may be subject to illah reasoning. So this specific [part] will also be subject to illah, meaning those individuals that are excluded from the general are excluded due to some illah, and that illah may be found in remaining individuals. So whichever remaining individuals have the illah will also exit the general. Thus if the specific is known, the general—being an independent statement—its remaining individuals may have illah, so we cannot know how many remain. Hence the remaining individuals become unknown and no ruling is established. So Imam al-Karkhi says that the general is not a proof in any case, neither definitively nor speculatively.
Second school: (2) And according to some: Some said that when the general is specified by speech, it will be seen whether the specific is known or unknown. If the specific is known, the general is a definitive proof in its remaining individuals. If the specific is unknown, the general is not a proof, not definitively nor speculatively. Proof: These scholars compare specification exactly to exception, whether the specific is known or unknown. The reason: just as in exception it is stated that the excepted is not included in the object of exception, in specification it is stated that the specific is not included in the general. So both resemble each other. When specification is like exception, then just as when the excepted is known the ruling is definitively established in the object of exception, here if the specific is known the ruling will be definitively established. The reason is that it does not accept illah because it is like exception, which does not accept illah because illah occurs in independent statements and the exception is not independent but connected to the initial statement. Since this specific does not accept illah, ignorance does not necessarily follow in the remaining individuals, so the ruling is definitively established. Therefore when the specific is known, the general is a definitive proof. If the specific is unknown, then it resembles an unknown excepted, which creates ignorance, so the general will not be a proof at all.
Third school: (3) And according to some: Some hold that if the specific is known, the general remains a definitive proof in its remaining individuals. If the specific is unknown, the specific [part] itself falls away, the general is unaffected, and the general applies to all its individuals definitively—meaning it is as if specification did not occur and the general remains in its original state. Proof: Specification resembles abrogation: just as in abrogation the abrogator is an independent statement, and if the date is known, the abrogated is terminated, and the ruling remains in those individuals that stay under the general. So here too, if the specific is known, the ruling remains in those individuals that remain under the general, so the general is a definitive proof. If the specific is unknown, it resembles an unknown abrogator; the unknown abrogator falls away and does not affect the abrogated. So here, the specific falls away and the general is unaffected, and the general is definitive in all its individuals.
Fourth school: (4) And according to us: The Hanafis hold that when the general is specified by speech, whether the specific is known or unknown, the general is a proof in its remaining individuals, but it is a speculative (zanni) proof. Proof: When specification occurs in the general, it does not remain upon its original meaning, because the original meaning of 'amm is generality. But when specification occurs, it is no longer used in its original meaning.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage presents a classical usul dispute on the status of a general ('amm) statement after it has been specified (takhsis) by a separate speech (kalam). Four positions are documented. The first, attributed to Imam al-Karkhi, argues that specification by kalam renders the 'amm completely invalid as a proof—neither definitive (qati) nor speculative (zanni)—because the unknown specific part introduces ignorance into the remaining general individuals, analogous to an unknown exception. The second position distinguishes based on whether the specific (mukhasis) is known or unknown: if known, the 'amm remains a definitive proof (hujjah qatiyyah) because the specification is like exception and does not accept illah; if unknown, it is not a proof at all. The third position similarly distinguishes but argues that if the specific is unknown, it is the specification that falls away, leaving the 'amm fully general and definitive. The fourth position is that of the Hanafi school: regardless of whether the specific is known or unknown, the 'amm remains a proof (hujjah), but only of speculative (zanni) strength. The Hanafis base this on the fact that specification removes the 'amm from its original literal meaning, so it cannot be definitive, but it is still a valid legal proof. The discussion illustrates the interplay of analogy (qiyas) to exception and abrogation, and highlights the Hanafi commitment to istihsan and the practical use of zanni proofs in law.

Key Terms
عام ('Amm): A word that includes all individuals to which it applies without restriction
تخصیص (Takhsis): The act of excluding some individuals from the general scope of a word
مخصوص (Mukhasis): The specific part or individuals that are excluded from the 'amm
حجت (Hujjah): A proof or authoritative evidence in law
ظنی (Zanni): Speculative; probable but not certain
قطعی (Qati): Definitive; certain and conclusive

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a general ('amm) statement after it has been specified by a separate speech (kalam)?
A) It becomes completely invalid as a proof.
B) It remains a definitive (qati) proof in its remaining individuals.
C) It remains a proof, but only speculative (zanni).
D) The specification falls away, and the 'amm remains fully general.

Key Takeaway
After takhsis by kalam, the Hanafi school holds that the 'amm remains a speculative (zanni) proof, not definitive, but still valid for deriving rulings.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
The Specified General as a Proof: Hanafi Position and Dispute
Presents four madhhabs on the probative value of a specified general term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the probative value of a specified general term and distinguish it from three other madhhabs.

Core Idea
A specified general term remains a proof, but only a speculative one, like a metaphor.

When a general term (āmm) in the Quran or Sunnah is specified (mukhassis), does it still retain any probative value for its remaining individuals? Scholars differ. In this lesson, we explore four madhhabs on this question, focusing on the Hanafi view that the specified general remains a proof (ḥujja) but at the level of speculative certainty (ẓann), not definitiveness (qaṭʿ). Understanding this dispute sharpens our ability to evaluate arguments from general texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Recognize that the question is: after a general term is specified, what is the probative status of that term for the individuals not excluded? The answer affects whether we can use the general as a definitive or speculative proof.
2
Summarize each of the four madhhabs
List the four positions: (1) known specific → definitive, unknown → uncertain; (2) known → definitive, unknown → no proof; (3) known → definitive, unknown → specific dropped; (4) Hanafi: always speculative. Note the key difference in each.
Focus on the treatment of the unknown specific.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the Hanafi argument: specification removes the general from its literal meaning (generality), making it metaphorical (majāz). A metaphorical proof is speculative. The example of the word 'hundred' used for less than a hundred illustrates this.
The shift from ḥaqīqa to majāz is central.
4
Compare with opposing views
Understand why other schools treat the specified general as definitive when the specific is known, and how they handle an unknown specific. Contrast their use of analogy to naskh and istithnāʾ with the Hanafi focus on linguistic shift.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: Hanafīs allow using a specified general as a proof in ijtihād (e.g., deriving rulings from a verse after it is specified), while others treat it as either definitive or non-probative in certain cases.
This affects how we weigh evidence in fiqh derivation.

مستقل کلام میں ہوتی ہے اور مستقلی مستقل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صدر کلام کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے تو جب یہ مخصوص تعلیل کو قبول نہیں کرتا تو عام کے باقی افراد میں جہالت لازم نہیں آئے گی تو ان میں حکم قطعا ثابت ہو جائے گا اس لیے مخصوص معلوم ہونے کی صورت میں عام بقیہ افراد میں حجت قطعیہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر مخصوص مجہول ہو تو پھر چونکہ اس کو مستی مجہول کے ساتھ مشابہت ہو گی تو جس طرح مستقلی مجبول منتقلی منہ میں جہالت پیدا کرتا ہے اسی طرح مخصوص مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں یہ مخصوص عام کے بقیہ افراد میں جہالت پیدا کر دے گا تو مستثنی منہ کی طرح عام میں بھی حکم ثابت نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لیے اس صورت میں عام بالکل حجت نہیں رہے گا۔

چوتھا مذ ہب احناف کا ہے (۴) و عند ناممکن فیہ شبہہ :۔ احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ عام میں اگر کلام کے ذریعے تخصیص کر دی جائے تو مخصوص معلوم ہو یا مجہول دونوں صورتوں میں عام اپنے باقی افراد میں حجت ہوگا لیکن حجت خلفیہ ہوگا۔
دلیل:۔ عام میں جب تخصیص کر دی جائے تو وہ اپنے حقیقی معنی پرنہیں رہتا کیونکہ عام کا منی حقیقی اور معنی موضوع لہ عموم ہے لیکن جب اس میں تخصیص کر دی جائے گی تو یہ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں مستعمل نہیں رہتا مخصوص معلوم ہونے کی صورت میں واضح ہے کہ عام مخصوص افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوگا باقی افراد کو شامل ہوگا مجہول کی صورت میں بھی اگر چہ تعین نہیں ہوگی کہ عام کن افراد کو شامل نہیں ہے اور کن کو شامل ہے لیکن پھر بھی اتنی بات کو تو یقینی ہوگی کہ عام اپنے تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہے تو دونوں صورتوں میں جب عام تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہو گا تو گویا یہ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور جو لفظ معنی موضوع کہ میں استعمال نہ ہو وہ مجاز ہوتا ہے لہذا تخصیص کے بعد عام مجاز ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور مجاز دلیل نلنی ہوتی ہے دلیل قطعی نہیں ہوتا۔ یہ ایسے ہی ہے جیسے لفظ کا یہ " کا معنی موضوع نہ ہو (۱۰۰) ہے اگر یہ سو کو شامل ہوگا تو یہ حقیقیت ہوگا اگر مکمل سو اعداد کو شمال نہیں ہو گا بلکہ بعض کو شامل ہو تو اس کے بعد یہ معلوم ہو یا نہ ہو کہ ماہ یعنی سو سے کم کتنے افراد کو شامل ہے پچاس (۵۰) کو شامل ہے یا ساٹھ کو شامل ہے تو ان دونوں صورتوں مائی کو مجاز کہا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں مستعمل نہیں ہو گا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہے کہ اگر مخصوص مجبول ہو تو عام اپنے موضوع لہ سے ہٹ جائے گا تو مجاز بن جائے گا۔ ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ ثَمَرَةَ تَمَكُنِ الشُّبُهَةِ فِيهِ بِقَوْلِهِ ) فَيَصِيرُ عِنْدَنَا كَالْعَامُ الَّذِي لَمْ يُخَصَّ عِندَ الشَّافِعِي رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى حَتَّى يُخَصِّصَهُ خَبَرُ الْوَاحِدِ وَالْقِيَاسُ ) ثُمَّ أَرَادَ أَنْ يُبَيِّنَ أَنَّ مَعَ وُجُودِ هَذِهِ الشَّبْهَةِ لَا يَسْقُطُ الاحْتِجَاجُ بِهِ فَقَالَ ( لَكِنْ لَا يَسْقُطُ الاحْتِجَاجُ بِهِ ؛ لأنَّ الْمُخَصِّصَ يُشْبِهُ النَّاسِ بِصِيغَتِهِ ، وَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ بِحُكْمِهِ كَمَا قُلْنَا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا يَسْقُطُ فِى نَفْسِهِ لِلشَّبَهِ الأَوَّلِ ، وَيُوجِبُ جَهَالَةً فِى الْعَام لِلشَّبَهِ الثَّانِي فَيَدْخُلُ الشَّكُ فِي سُقُوطِ الْعَامِّ فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِهِ) أَى بِالشَّلِّ إِذْ قَبْلَ الشَّخْصِيصِ كَانَ مَعْمُولًا بِهِ فَلَمَّا خُصَّ دَخَلَ الشَّكُ فِي أَنَّهُ هَلْ بَقِيَ مَعْمُولًا بِهِ أَمُ بَطَلَ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِالشَّكْ ( وَإِنْ كَانَ ) أَى : الْمُخَصِّصُ ) مَعْلُومًا فَلِلشَّبَهِ الْأَوَّلِ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ) لَا يُرِيدُ بِقَوْلِهِ فَلِلشَّبَهِ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يُشَابِهُ النَّاسِخَ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ كَمَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يُعَلِّلَ النَّاسِحَ الَّذِي يَنْسَخُ بَعْضَ أَفْرَادِ الْعَامُ لِيَنْسَخَ بِالْقِيَاسِ بَعْضًا آخَرَ مِنْ أَفْرَادِ الْعَامُ فَإِنْ تَعْلِيلَ النَّاسِخِ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ لَا يَصِحُ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي هَذِهِ الصَّفْحَةِ ، بَلْ يُرِيدُ أَنَّهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ نَضٌ مُسْتَقِلْ بِنَفْسِهِ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ
[The first position:] In independent speech, it is not independent but related to the main speech. When it does not accept specification of the cause, ignorance does not necessarily occur in the remaining individuals of the general, so the ruling is definitively established in them. Therefore, when the specific [known] is known, the general is a definitive proof for the remaining individuals. And if the specific is unknown, then because it resembles the unknown independent, just as the unknown independent creates ignorance in the excepted-from, similarly when the specific is unknown, this specific creates ignorance in the remaining individuals of the general, so the ruling is not established in the general just like the excepted-from. Therefore, in this case the general is not a proof at all. 
Third madhhab: (3) According to some: The madhhab of some people is that if the specific is known, the general remains a definitive proof for its remaining individuals; and if the specific is unknown, the speciﬁc itself falls away, and the general is not affected at all, so the general includes all its individuals definitively—meaning it is permissible to consider that specification did not occur, and the general remains in its original state. 
Evidence: It resembles the abrogator (nāsikh). Just as the abrogator is independent speech, and it has the property that if the date is known, the abrogated (mansūkh) ceases, and the ruling is established only in those individuals that remain under the abrogator. So here too, when the specific is known, the ruling remains only in those individuals that remain under the general, so the general is a definitive proof for them. And if the specific is unknown, it resembles an unknown abrogator, and an unknown abrogator itself falls away, not affecting the abrogated. Therefore, in the case of an unknown specific, the specific itself falls away, the general is not affected, but rather it is definitive for all its individuals. 
Fourth madhhab, that of the Hanafis: (4) And according to us, there is an ambiguity in it: The madhhab of the Hanafis is that if specification is made in the general through speech, whether the specific is known or unknown, in both cases the general is a proof for its remaining individuals, but it is a speculative (ẓannī) proof. 
Evidence: When specification is made in the general, it does not remain on its real meaning, because the real meaning of the general is generality (ʿumūm). But when specification is made, it is not used in its original meaning. When the specific is known, it is clear that the general does not include the specified individuals but includes the remaining. In the case of an unknown specific, even though it is not determined which individuals are not included and which are, it is certain that the general does not include all its individuals. In both cases, when the general does not include all individuals, it is as if it is not used in its original meaning. And a word not used in its original meaning is metaphorical (majāz). Therefore, after specification, the general becomes metaphorical. And a metaphorical proof is speculative, not definitive. It is like the word "hundred" (mi'a): if it includes one hundred, it is real; if it does not include the complete hundred but only some, then whether it is known or not how many less than a hundred it includes—fifty or sixty—in both cases "hundred" is said to be metaphorical because it is not used in its original meaning. Similarly here, if the specific is unknown, the general departs from its original meaning and becomes metaphorical. Then he mentioned the result of the presence of ambiguity in it by his saying: "So according to us, it becomes like the general that was not specified according to al-Shāfiʿī, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him, until it is specified by a solitary report (khabar al-wāḥid) and analogy (qiyās)." Then he intended to show that with the existence of this ambiguity, using it as a proof does not drop, so he said: "But using it as a proof does not drop, because the speciﬁer resembles the abrogator in its form and the exception in its ruling, as we said. If it is unknown, it falls in itself due to the first resemblance, and causes ignorance in the general due to the second resemblance, so doubt enters about the dropping of the general, so it is not dropped by it—i.e., by doubt—since before specification it was acted upon, and when specified, doubt enters whether it remains acted upon or becomes void, so it is not voided by doubt. And if it—i.e., the speciﬁer—is known, then due to the first resemblance its illa derivation is valid." He does not mean by "due to the first resemblance" that because it resembles the abrogator, its illa derivation is valid, just as it is valid to derive the illa of the abrogator that abrogates some individuals of the general in order to abrogate other individuals of the general by analogy— indeed, deriving the illa of the abrogator in this way is not valid as will come on this page. Rather, he means that because it is an independent text, its illa derivation is valid.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilāf) on the probative status of a general term (‘āmm) after it has been specified (takhṣīṣ) by a specific (mukhassiṣ). Four madhāhib are presented: 

1) First madhhab: If the specific (mukhassiṣ) is known (ma‘lūm), the general remains a definitive (qaṭ‘ī) proof for the remaining individuals. If unknown (majhūl), the general becomes non-definitive because ignorance spreads. 

2) Second madhhab: Similar to the first but adds that an unknown specific creates ignorance in the general, so the general is not a proof at all. 

3) Third madhhab (some scholars): If the specific is known, the general is a definitive proof for the remainder. If unknown, the specific itself is dropped (sāqiṭ), and the general reverts to its original state of encompassing all individuals definitively. 

4) Fourth madhhab (the Hanafī position): In both cases (known or unknown specific), the general remains a proof (ḥujja) for the remaining individuals, but it is a speculative (ẓannī) proof, not definitive. The Hanafī evidence: specification removes the general from its original meaning (generality), so it becomes metaphorical (majāz). A metaphorical proof is speculative. This is analogous to the word "hundred" (mi'a) when used for less than a hundred—it becomes metaphorical. Despite this ambiguity, the general is still used as a proof because it resembles abrogation (naskh) in form and exception (istithnā') in ruling. Doubt does not void a previously established proof. This position is the relied-upon view in the Hanafī school.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A general term that covers all individuals of its category by its linguistic formulation.
مخصوص (mukhṣaṣ): The specific term that removes some individuals from the general’s scope.
مجاز (majāz): A word used in a meaning other than its original (ḥaqīqī) meaning due to a relation (qarīna).
حجت قطعیه (ḥujja qaṭ‘iyya): A proof that yields certainty and is not open to interpretation.
حجت ظنیہ (ḥujja ẓanniyya): A proof that yields probable knowledge and is open to ijtihād.
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): The act of specifying a general term, limiting its scope to some individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī madhhab, what is the status of a general term (ʿāmm) after it has been specified by a known specific (mukhṣaṣ maʿlūm)?
A) It becomes a definitive (qaṭʿī) proof for the remaining individuals.
B) It becomes a speculative (ẓannī) proof for the remaining individuals.
C) It becomes invalid as a proof altogether.
D) It remains a definitive proof for all individuals, including the excluded ones.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafī view: a specified general term is a metaphorical proof (majāz), thus speculative (ẓannī), but still a valid proof for its remaining individuals.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
The Specified 'Amm: From Haqiqa to Majaz, Yet Still a Proof
Arguing that specified 'amm is majaz but still a valid proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a specified 'amm remains a valid proof (hujja) despite becoming metaphorical (majaz), and evaluate the role of doubt (shubha) in preserving its probative force.

Core Idea
Specified 'amm is metaphorical but remains a proof; doubt cannot overturn prior certainty.

When a general term like 'believers' is specified by an exception (e.g., 'except the sinners'), does it lose all legal authority for the remaining cases? This passage tackles precisely that question, showing how the Hanafi school argues that despite the shift from literal to metaphorical usage, the specified 'amm continues to be a valid proof. The key lies in the nature of doubt (shubha) and the prior certainty of the general term before specification.

Guided Path
1
Establish that specified 'amm is majaz
Recognize that when a general term no longer covers all its original individuals, it is used in a non-literal sense, making it metaphorical (majaz). The author illustrates this with the example of 'mi'a' (hundred) used for a subset.
This is foundational: takhsis removes the 'amm from haqiqa.
2
Identify the dual resemblance of the mukhassis
The specifier (mukhassis) resembles both a nasikh (abrogator) in its wording and an istithna' (exception) in its ruling. This dual resemblance creates doubt (shubha) about the continued authority of the 'amm.
Understanding this resemblance is crucial for the next step.
3
Analyze the effect of shubha on the proof
Examine the two scenarios: mukhassis unknown (majhul) and mukhassis known (ma'lum). In both, the doubt from the resemblances does not invalidate the 'amm because it was a proof before specification, and doubt cannot undo certainty.
The principle is: yaqeen (certainty) is not removed by shak (doubt).
4
Evaluate the ta'lil dispute
When the mukhassis is known, the validity of ta'lil (stating its cause for qiyas) is debated. Hanafis and most scholars hold ta'lil valid; al-Jubba'i denies it. If ta'lil is valid, the remaining scope becomes unknown, but this does not invalidate the 'amm.
The passage then rebuts an objection: the mere possibility of ta'lil does not destroy the proof.
5
Conclude that the 'amm remains a hujja
Synthesize: the 'amm after takhsis is majaz (zanni) but still a binding proof for the remaining individuals. The doubt from resemblance and ta'lil does not erase its prior authority.
This is the core Hanafi position.

واضح ہے کہ عام مخصوص افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوگا باقی افراد کو شامل ہوگا مجہول کی صورت میں بھی اگر چہ تعین نہیں ہوگی کہ عام کن افراد کو شامل نہیں ہے اور کن کو شامل ہے لیکن پھر بھی اتنی بات کو تو یقینی ہوگی کہ عام اپنے تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہے تو دونوں صورتوں میں جب عام تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہو گا تو گویا یہ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور جو لفظ معنی موضوع کہ میں استعمال نہ ہو وہ مجاز ہوتا ہے لہذا تخصیص کے بعد عام مجاز ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور مجاز دلیل ظنی ہوتی ہے دلیل قطعی نہیں ہوتا۔ یہ ایسے ہی ہے جیسے لفظ مائہ کا معنی موضوع لہ (۱۰۰) ہے اگر یہ سو کو شامل ہوگا تو یہ حقیقت ہوگا اگر مکمل سو افراد کو شامل نہیں ہو گا بلکہ بعض کو شامل ہو تو اس کے بعد یہ معلوم ہو یا نہ ہو کہ ماہ یعنی سو سے کم کتنے افراد کو شامل ہے پچاس (۵۰) کو شامل ہے یا ساٹھ کو شامل ہے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں مائہ کو مجاز کہا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں مستعمل نہیں ہو گا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہے کہ اگر مخصص مجہول ہو تو عام اپنے موضوع لہ سے ہٹ جائے گا تو مجاز بن جائے گا۔ ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ ثَمَرَةَ تَمَكُنِ الشُّبُهَةِ فِيهِ بِقَوْلِهِ ) فَيَصِيرُ عِنْدَنَا كَالْعَامِ الَّذِي لَمْ يُخَصَّ عِندَ الشَّافِعِي رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى حَتَّى يُخَصِّصَهُ خَبَرُ الْوَاحِدِ وَالْقِيَاسُ ) ثُمَّ أَرَادَ أَنْ يُبَيِّنَ أَنَّ مَعَ وُجُودِ هَذِهِ الشَّبْهَةِ لَا يَسْقُطُ الاحْتِجَاجُ بِهِ فَقَالَ ( لَكِنْ لَا يَسْقُطُ الاحْتِجَاجُ بِهِ ؛ لأنَّ الْمُخَصِّصَ يُشْبِهُ النَّاسِخَ بِصِيغَتِهِ ، وَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ بِحُكْمِهِ كَمَا قُلْنَا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًا يَسْقُطُ فِى نَفْسِهِ لِلشَّبَهِ الأَوَّلِ ، وَيُوجِبُ جَهَالَةً فِى الْعَام لِلشَّبَهِ الثَّانِي فَيَدْخُلُ الشَّكُ فِي سُقُوطِ الْعَامِّ فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِهِ) أَى بِالشَّبَهِ إِذْ قَبْلَ التَّخْصِيصِ كَانَ مَعْمُولًا بِهِ فَلَمَّا خُصَّ دَخَلَ الشَّكُ فِي أَنَّهُ هَلْ بَقِيَ مَعْمُولًا بِهِ أَمْ بَطَلَ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِالشَّكْ ( وَإِنْ كَانَ ) أَى : الْمُخَصِّصُ ) مَعْلُومًا فَلِلشَّبَهِ الْأَوَّلِ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ) لَا يُرِيدُ بِقَوْلِهِ فَلِلشَّبَهِ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يُشَابِهُ النَّاسِخَ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ كَمَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يُعَلِّلَ النَّاسِخَ الَّذِي يَنْسَخُ بَعْضَ أَفْرَادِ الْعَامَّ لِيَنْسَخَ بِالْقِيَاسِ بَعْضًا آخَرَ مِنْ أَفْرَادِ الْعَامَّ فَإِنَّ تَعْلِيلَ النَّاسِخِ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ لَا يَصِحُ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي هَذِهِ الصَّفْحَةِ ، بَلْ يُرِيدُ أَنَّهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ نَصٌّ مُسْتَقِلٌّ بِنَفْسِهِ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ ) كَمَا هُوَ عِندَنَا ( فَإِنَّ عِندَنَا وَعِندَ أَكْثَرِ الْعُلَمَاء يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ خِلَافًا لِلْجُبَّانِيِّ وَإِذَا صَحَّ تَعْلِيلُهُ لَا يُدْرَى أَنَّهُ كَمْ يَخْرُجُ بِالتَّعْلِيلِ أَى بِالْقِيَاسِ وَكَمْ يَبْقَى تَحْتَ الْعَامِّ ) فَيُوجِبُ جَهَالَةً فِيمَا بَقِيَ تَحْتَ الْعَامِّ ، وَلِلشَّبَهِ الثَّانِي لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ كَمَا هُوَ عِندَ الْبَعْضِ فَدَخَلَ الشَّكُ فِي سُقُوطِ الْعَامِّ فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِهِ) أَى بِالشَّبَهِ الثَّانِي هُوَ شَبَهُ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ الْمُخَصِّصَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّ الْمُخَصَّصَ غَيْرُ دَاخِلٍ فِى الْعَامِّ ؛ فَلِهذَا الشَّبَهِ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ كَمَا هُوَ مَذْهَبُ الْجُبَّانِيِّ كَمَا لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُ الْمُسْتَثْنَى وَإِخْرَاجُ الْبَعْضِ الْآخَرِ بِطَرِيقِ الْقِيَاسِ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ يَصِيرُ الْبَاقِي تَحْتَ الْعَامِّ مَجْهُولًا فَلَا يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةً ، وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةً ، وَقَدْ كَانَ قَبْلَ التَّخْصِيصِ حُجَّةً فَوَقَعَ الشَّكُ فِي بُطُلَانِهِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِالشَّكْ هَذَا مَا قَالُوا ، وَيَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ الْمَذْهَبُ عِنْدَكُمْ ، وَعِندَ أَكْثَرِ الْعُلَمَاء صِحَّةَ تَعْلِيلٍ فَيَجِبُ أَنْ يَبْطُلَ الْعَامُ عِنْدَكُمْ بِنَاءً عَلَى زَعْمِكُمْ فِي صِحَّةِ تَعْلِيلِهِ ، وَلَا تَمَسُّكَ لَكُمْ بِزَعْمِ الْجُبَّانِيِّ أَنَّ عِنْدَهُ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ فَلِدَفْعِ هَذِهِ الشُّبُهَةِ قَالَ ) عَلَى أَنَّ احْتِمَالَ التَّعْلِيلِ لَا يُخْرِجُهُ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ حُجَّةً ؛ لأنَّ مَا اقْتَضَى الْقِيَاسُ تَخْصِيصَهُ يَخُصُّ وَمَا لَا فَلَا فَإِنَّ الْمُخَصِّصَ إِنْ لَمْ يُدْرَكَ فِيهِ عِلَّةٌ لَا يُعَلَّلُ فَيَبْقَى الْعَامُ فِي الْبَاقِي حُجَّةً ، وَإِنْ عُرِفَ فِيهِ عِلَّةٌ فَكُلُّ مَا تُوجَدُ الْعِلَّةُ فِيهِ يَخُصُّ قِيَاسًا وَمَا لَا فَلَا فَلَا يَبْطُلُ الْعَامُ بِاحْتِمَالِ التَّعْلِيلِ
It is clear that the general term does not include the specified individuals but includes the remaining individuals. Even in the unknown case, though it is not determined which individuals are excluded and which are included, it is certain that the general does not include all its individuals. So in both cases, when the general does not include all its individuals, it is not used in its literal meaning (al-ma'na al-mawdu' lahu). Any word not used in its literal meaning is metaphorical (majaz). Therefore, after specification, the general becomes majaz. And majaz is a speculative (zanni) proof, not a definitive proof. This is like the word 'mi'a' (hundred) whose literal meaning is 100. If it includes all hundred, it is haqiqa (literal). If it does not include all hundred but only some, whether it is known or unknown how many it includes (e.g., fifty or sixty), in both cases 'mi'a' is called majaz because it is not used in its literal meaning. Similarly here, if the specifier is unknown, the general departs from its literal meaning and becomes majaz. Then he mentioned the consequence of the doubt (shubha) occurring in it by his statement: 'So it becomes, in our view, like the general that was not specified according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, until a khabar al-wahid or qiyas specifies it.' Then he intended to clarify that despite the presence of this doubt, it does not cease to be a proof (hujja). He said: 'But it does not cease to be a proof because the specifier (mukhassis) resembles the abrogator (nasikh) in its form (sigha) and the exception (istithna') in its ruling (hukm), as we said. If the specifier is unknown, it itself ceases (to be a proof) due to the first resemblance (shabah al-awwal), and it causes ignorance (jahala) regarding the general due to the second resemblance, so doubt enters about the fall of the general, thus it does not fall by that.' Meaning, before specification it was acted upon, and when specified, doubt enters whether it remains acted upon or becomes invalid, so it is not invalidated by doubt. And if the specifier is known, then due to the first resemblance, its ta'lil (stating the cause) is valid. He does not mean by his statement 'due to the first resemblance' that because it resembles the abrogator, its ta'lil is valid, just as it is valid to state the cause of the abrogator that abrogates some individuals of the general in order to abrogate by qiyas another part of the general's individuals; indeed, stating the cause of the abrogator in this way is not valid, as will come on this page. Rather, he means that because it is an independent text (nass mustaqill bi nafsihi), its ta'lil is valid, as is our view. For in our view and the view of most scholars, its ta'lil is valid, contrary to al-Jubba'i. And when its ta'lil is valid, it is not known how many come out by ta'lil (i.e., by qiyas) and how many remain under the general, so it causes ignorance regarding what remains under the general. And due to the second resemblance, its ta'lil is not valid, as is the view of some, so doubt enters about the fall of the general, thus it does not fall by it. The second resemblance is the resemblance to istithna' in that the specifier clarifies that the specified is not included in the general. Because of this resemblance, its ta'lil is not valid, as is the madhhab of al-Jubba'i, just as ta'lil of the excepted (mustathna) and extracting another part by qiyas is not valid. So from the perspective that its ta'lil is valid, the remaining under the general becomes unknown, so the general is not a proof. And from the perspective that its ta'lil is not valid, the general remains a proof. And before specification it was a proof, so doubt occurred about its invalidity, so it is not invalidated by doubt. This is what they said. And it is objected: since the madhhab according to you and most scholars is the validity of ta'lil, then the general must become invalid according to you, based upon your claim about the validity of its ta'lil, and you have no recourse to al-Jubba'i's claim that in his view ta'lil is not valid. To repel this doubt, he said: 'Indeed, the possibility of ta'lil does not remove it from being a proof, because whatever qiyas necessitates its specification is specified, and whatever not, not. Indeed, if no cause is perceived in the specifier, it is not given a cause, so the general remains a proof in the remaining. And if a cause is known in it, then everything in which the cause is found is specified by qiyas, and whatever not, not. So the general is not invalidated by the possibility of ta'lil.'
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the nature of a general term ('amm) after it has been specified (takhsis). The author begins by establishing that when an 'amm is specified, it becomes metaphorical (majaz) because it is no longer used in its original literal meaning which encompassed all individuals. For example, the word 'mi'a' (hundred) literally means exactly one hundred; if it is used to refer to a subset, it is metaphorical regardless of whether the number is known or unknown. Similarly, a specified 'amm is majaz, and majaz yields only speculative (zanni) proof, not definitive. The main debate here is whether such a specified 'amm can still function as a valid proof (hujja). The author argues that it does remain a hujja because the specifier (mukhassis) bears a dual resemblance: it resembles an abrogator (nasikh) in that it restricts the scope, and it resembles an exception (istithna') in that it clarifies exclusion. Two scenarios are discussed: (1) If the mukhassis is unknown (majhul), the doubt (shubha) from both resemblances does not invalidate the 'amm; it was a proof before specification, and doubt cannot overturn certainty. (2) If the mukhassis is known (ma'lum), a dispute arises about whether its cause ('illa) can be stated (ta'lil) to apply the specification to other analogous cases by qiyas. The Hanafi school and most scholars hold that ta'lil is valid for a known mukhassis because it is an independent text. Al-Jubba'i, on the other hand, denies ta'lil because the mukhassis resembles istithna', which cannot be extended by qiyas. The tension is that if ta'lil is valid, the remaining scope of the 'amm becomes unknown (majhul), potentially rendering it useless as a proof. However, the author resolves this by stating that the mere possibility of ta'lil does not invalidate the 'amm; actual qiyas specification occurs only where the cause is found, leaving the rest of the 'amm intact as a proof. Thus, the 'amm after takhsis remains a hujja in the Hanafi view, contrary to al-Shafi'i's position that it requires specification by khabar al-wahid or qiyas.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A term that encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.
مخصص (mukhassis): The evidence that specifies a general term, excluding some individuals.
مجاز (majaz): A word used in a sense other than its original literal meaning, such as 'amm after takhsis.
تعلیل (ta'lil): Stating the 'illa (cause) of a ruling to extend it by qiyas to other cases.
حجت (hujja): A proof or evidence that can be used to derive a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why does a specified general term ('amm) remain a valid proof (hujja) despite being metaphorical?
A) Because it is still used in its literal meaning.
B) Because the specifier resembles both naskh and istithna', creating doubt that cannot invalidate certainty.
C) Because it has been abrogated entirely.
D) Because al-Shafi'i ruled that it remains a proof.

Key Takeaway
A general term after specification is metaphorical (majaz) but remains a binding proof (hujja) for the remaining individuals; doubt does not negate prior certainty.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
Takhṣīṣ and the Authority of the General: The Hanafī Defense
Debating whether the general remains a proof after specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafī school holds that the general (ʿāmm) remains a proof (ḥujja) after specification (takhṣīṣ) despite the possibility of applying qiyās to the mukhassiṣ, and evaluate the counterargument of al-Jubbā'ī.

Core Idea
The possibility of taʿlīl does not invalidate the general; only actual qiyās removes individuals.

This passage addresses a subtle but crucial question in Hanafī uṣūl al-fiqh: once a general text has been specified by a specific text (mukhassiṣ), does the general retain its authority as a proof for the remaining individuals? The answer is not straightforward because the mukhassiṣ resembles both an abrogator (nāsikh) and an exception (istithnā). Some scholars, like al-Jubbā'ī, argue that if taʿlīl (causal reasoning via qiyās) of the mukhassiṣ is valid, the scope of the general becomes unknown, thus invalidating it. In this commentary, the Hanafī position is firmly defended: the mere possibility of taʿlīl does not strip the general of its authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two resemblances
The mukhassiṣ resembles a nāsikh in wording and an istithnā in ruling. Both create doubt about the general's authority.
The first resemblance (shabah al-naskh) implies that taʿlīl is possible; the second (shabah al-istithnā) implies it is not.
2
Understand the opposing argument
Al-Jubbā'ī argues: if taʿlīl is valid, we do not know how many individuals remain under the general, so it becomes invalid. If taʿlīl is not valid, doubt about its validity also invalidates the general.
Both horns of the dilemma aim to show the general cannot remain a proof.
3
Identify the Hanafī response
The text states that the possibility of taʿlīl does not remove the general from being a proof because qiyās is only applied where the ʿilla is actually found.
The key phrase: 'iḥtimāl al-taʿlīl lā yukhrijuhu min an yakūna ḥujja'.
4
Apply the principle to a fiqh example
Consider the general command 'Kill the polytheists' (Q. 9:5) specified by an exemption for women and children. If the exemption has an ʿilla (e.g., not fighting), qiyās can extend it to others with that ʿilla. But the general remains a proof for all polytheists not covered by the explicit exemption or by such qiyās.
This shows the practical operation of the principle.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under the Hanafī view, the general remains binding for all not explicitly or analogically excluded. Under the opposing view, the general may be weakened or invalidated, leading to uncertainty.
This difference affects the scope of legal obligation.

) كَمَا هُوَ عِندَنَا ( فَإِنْ عِندَنَا وَعِندَ أَكْثَرِ الْعُلَمَاء يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ خِلَافًا لِلْجُبَّانِي وَإِذَا صَحْ تَعْلِيلُهُ لَا يُدْرَى أَنَّهُ كَمْ يَخْرُجُ بِالتَّعْلِيلِ أَى بِالْقِيَاسِ وَكَمْ يَبْقَى تَحْتَ الْعَام ) فَيُوجِبُ جَهَالَةٌ فِيمَا بَقِيَ تَحْتَ الْعَامُ ، وَلِلشَّبَهِ الثَّانِي لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ كَمَا هُوَ عِندَ الْبَعْضِ فَدَخَلَ الشَّكُ فِي سُقُوطٍ الْعَامٌ فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِهِ) أَى بِالشَّبَهِ الثَّانِي هُوَ شَبَهُ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ الْمُخَصِّصَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّ الْمُخَصِّصَ غَيْرُ دَاخِل فِى الْعَامّ ؛ فَلِهذَا الشَّبَهِ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ كَمَا هُوَ مَذْهَبُ الْجُبَّانِيُّ كَمَا لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُ الْمُسْتَتَنَى وَإِخْرَاجُ الْبَعْضِ الْآخَرِ بِطَرِيقِ الْقِيَاسِ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ يَصِيرُ الْبَاقِي تَحْتَ الْعَام مَجْهُولًا فَلا يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةً ، وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ يَبْقَى الْعَامُ حُجَّةً ، وَقَدْ كَانَ قَبْلَ التَّخْصِيصِ حُجَّةٌ فَوَقَعَ الشَّكُ فِي بُطُلَانِهِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بالشَّكْ هَذَا مَا قَالُوا ، وَيَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ الْمَذْهَبُ عِنْدَكُمْ ، وَعِندَ أَكْثَرِ الْعُلَمَاء صِحَّةَ تَعْلِيلٍ فَيَجِبُ أَنْ يَبْطُلَ الْعَامُ عِنْدَكُمْ بِنَاء عَلَى زَعْمِكُمْ فِي صِحَّةِ تَعْلِيلِهِ ، وَلَا تَمَسُّكَ لَكُمْ بِزَعْمِ الْجُبَّانِيُّ أَنَّ عِنْدَهُ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ فَلِدَفْعِ هَذِهِ الشُّبُهَةِ قَالَ ) عَلَى أَنَّ احْتِمَالَ التَّعْلِيلِ لَا يُخْرِجُهُ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ حُجَّةً ؛ لأنَّ مَا اقْتَضَى الْقِيَاسُ تَخْصِيصَهُ يَخُصُّ وَمَا لَا فَلا فَإِنَّ الْمُخَصِّصَ إِنْ لَمْ يُدْرَكَ فِيهِ عِلَّةٌ لا يُعَلَّلُ فَيَبْقَى الْعَامُ فِي الْبَاقِي حُجَّةٌ ، وَإِنْ عُرِفَ فِيهِ عِلَّةٌ فَكُلُّ مَا تُوجَدُ الْعِلَّهُ فِيهِ يَخُصُّ قِيَاسًا وَمَا لَا فَلَا فَلَا يَبْطُلُ الْعَامُ بِاحْتِمَالِ التَّعْلِيلِ

ترجمہ:۔ پھر ذکر فرمایا اس میں شبہ پیدا ہونے کے ثمرہ کو اپنے اس قول کے ساتھ (پس ہو جائے گا ہمارے نزدیک اس عام کی مثل جس میں تخصیص نہ کی گئی ہو امام شافعی کے نزدیک حتی کہ تخصیص کر دے گا اس کی خبر واحد اور قیاس ) پھر ارادہ کیا یہ کہ بیان کریں کہ بے شک با وجود اس شبہ کے پائے جانے کے نہیں ساقط ہو تا حجت پکڑنا اس عام کے ساتھ کیونکہ تخصص مشابہ ہے ناسخ کے اپنے صیغہ کے ساتھ اور استثناء کے اپنے حکم کے ساتھ بوجہ اس کے جو ہم نے کہا پس اگر مجہول ہوگا تو خود ساقط ہو جائے گا

صفحہ میں بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ بے شک وہ اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ بذات خود مستقل نص ہے صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل (جیسا کہ وہ ہے ہمارے نزدیک) کیونکہ ہمارے نزدیک اور اکثر علماء کے نزدیک صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل ، اختلاف کیا ہے اس میں جہاتی نے پس جب صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل تو نہیں ہوگی معلوم یہ بات کہ بے شک کتنے افراد خارج ہوئے تعلیل کے ساتھ یعنی قیاس کے ساتھ اور کتنے باقی ہیں عام کے تحت ( پس وہ ثابت کرے گا جہالت کو ان افراد میں جو بانی ہیں عام کے تحت اور دوسری مشابہت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے صحیح اس کی تعلیل جیسا کہ وہ بعض حضرات کے نزدیک ہے پس داخل ہو گیا شک عام کے ساقط ہونے میں پس نہیں ساقط ہو گا وہ اس کی وجہ سے ) یعنی دوسری مشابہت کی وجہ سے اور وہ استثناء کی مشابہت ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ بے شک مخصص بیان کرتا ہے یہ بات کہ بے شک مخصوص داخل نہیں ہے عام کے حکم میں پس اس شبہ کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے صحیح اس کی تعلیل جیسا کہ وہ جہائی کا مذہب ہے جیسا کہ نہیں ہے صحیح تعلیل مستی کی اور بعض دوسرے افراد کو نکالنا قیاس کے طریقہ کے ساتھ پس اس حیثیت سے کہ صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل ہو جائیں گے باقی افراد عام کے تحت مجبول پس نہیں باقی رہے گا عام حجت اور اس حیثیت سے کہ نہیں ہے صحیح اس کی تعلیل باقی رہے گا عام حجت اور تحقیق تھا تخصیص سے پہلے حجت پس شک واقع ہو گیا اس کے باطل ہونے میں پس نہیں وہ باطل ہو گا شک کی وجہ سے یہ وہ تفصیل جو علماء نے کہا اور وارد ہوتا ہے اس پر اعتراض کہ بے شک جب ہے مذہب آپ کے نزدیک اور اکثر علماء کے نزدیک اس کے تعلیل کے صحیح ہونے کا پس واجب ہے یہ کہ باطل ہو جائے عام تمہارے نزدیک اس کی تعلیل کے صحیح ہونے میں تمہارے گمان پر بنا ء کرتے ہوئے اور نہیں صحیح ہے تمہارے لیے استدلال پکڑنا جبائی کے گمان کے ساتھ کہ اس کے نزدیک بے شک نہیں ہے صحیح اس عام کی تعلیل اس شب کو دفع کرنے لیے فرمایا ( علاوہ اس کے کہ بے شک تعلیل کا احتمال نہیں نکالتا وہ اس کو اس بات سے کہ ہو وہ حجت کیونکہ وہ جو کہ تقاضا کرتا ہے قیاس اس کی تخصیص کا تو اس میں تخصیص کر دی جاتی ہے اور جہاں قیاس تقاضا نہ کرے تو وہاں تخصیص نہیں کی جاتی ہے) کیونکہ شخص کہ اگر نہ جانی جا سکے اس میں علت تو تعلیل نہیں کی جاتی پس
Then he mentioned the result of the doubt occurring with his statement: (So it will be, according to us, like the general that has not been specified – according to Imam al-Shafi'i, even if it is specified by khabar wahid and qiyas). Then he intended to explain that despite the existence of this doubt, the proof is not dropped because takhsis resembles nasikh in its wording and istithna in its ruling, for the reason we mentioned. So if it becomes unknown, it will drop itself. From the first resemblance, it will cause ignorance in the general; from the second resemblance, doubt enters into the falling of the general, so the general does not fall due to that doubt. Because before takhsis it was not acted upon, so when takhsis was made, doubt entered whether the general remains acted upon or becomes invalid, so it does not become invalid due to doubt. (And if it – i.e., the mukhassis – is known, then from the first resemblance its ta'lil is valid). They do not mean by their statement 'by the first resemblance' that because it resembles a dated abrogator, its ta'lil is valid, as it is correct to do ta'lil of that dated text which abrogates some individuals of the general so that other individuals from the general become abrogated by qiyas. For the ta'lil of the nasikh in this way is not valid, as will come on the same page. Rather, they mean that because it is itself an independent text, its ta'lil is valid (as it is according to us). For according to us and most scholars, its ta'lil is valid, contrary to al-Jubba'i. When its ta'lil is valid, it is not known how many individuals are excluded by ta'lil, i.e., by qiyas, and how many remain under the general. (So it causes ignorance in those individuals that remain under the general. And due to the second resemblance, its ta'lil is not valid, as it is according to some, so doubt enters into the falling of the general, so it does not fall because of it.) That is, due to the second resemblance, which is the resemblance of istithna, in that the mukhassis clarifies that the mukhassas is not included in the ruling of the general. Because of this resemblance, its ta'lil is not valid, as is the madhhab of al-Jubba'i, just as ta'lil of the mustathna is not valid and excluding other individuals by way of qiyas. So from the aspect that its ta'lil is valid, the remaining under the general becomes unknown, so the general does not remain a proof. And from the aspect that its ta'lil is not valid, the general remains a proof. And it was a proof before takhsis, so doubt occurs in its invalidity, so it does not become invalid by doubt. This is what they said. And an objection arises: When the madhhab according to you and most scholars is the validity of ta'lil, then it is necessary that the general becomes invalid according to you, based on your claim of the validity of its ta'lil, and you have no recourse to the claim of al-Jubba'i that according to him its ta'lil is not valid. So to repel this doubt, he said: (Moreover, the possibility of ta'lil does not remove it from being a proof, because what qiyas requires to be specified is specified, and what not, not. For if a 'illa is not perceived in the mukhassis, it is not reasoned, so the general remains a proof in the remainder. And if a 'illa is known in it, then wherever that 'illa is found, it is specified by qiyas, and where not, not. So the general does not become invalid by the mere possibility of ta'lil.)
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the relationship between takhsis (specification) of a general text (ʿāmm) and its continued authority (ḥujjiyya). The author addresses two shabah (resemblances) that cause doubt. The first resemblance compares the mukhassis (specifier) to a nāsikh (abrogator) because both remove some individuals from the scope of a general ruling. The second resemblance compares the mukhassis to istithnā (exception) because both clarify that some individuals were never intended by the general. The debate centers on whether the general can be subjected to taʿlīl (causal reasoning via qiyās) after specification. According to the Ḥanafī school and most scholars, taʿlīl of the mukhassis is valid when it is a known, independent text. This leads to the charge that the remainder under the general becomes unknown, potentially invalidating it. However, the Ḥanafī response maintains that the mere possibility of taʿlīl does not strip the general of its authority; instead, qiyās is applied only where the ʿilla (legal cause) is actually found. Thus, the general remains a proof for what is not covered by qiyās.

Key Terms
تعلیل (taʿlīl): Applying causal reasoning (qiyās) to a text to extend its ruling to other cases based on a shared ʿilla.
شبه (shabah): A resemblance between two legal concepts; here, the mukhassis resembles either a nāsikh or an istithnā.
عام (ʿāmm): A general word or expression that encompasses all individuals of a category without restriction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī position defended in this passage, what is the effect of the possibility of taʿlīl on the general (ʿāmm) after takhṣīṣ?
A) The general becomes invalid because its remaining scope is unknown.
B) The general remains a proof because qiyās is only applied where the ʿilla is actually found.
C) The general is suspended until the ʿilla is identified.
D) The general is abrogated by the mukhassis.

Key Takeaway
The general remains a proof (ḥujja) after specification; the mere possibility of taʿlīl does not diminish its authority.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
The Evidentiary Status of Specified General Text ('Amm Makhsus)
Debate on the authority of a specified general text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a specified general text remains a valid zanni proof by distinguishing its resemblance to naskh versus istithna'.

Core Idea
A specified general text remains a hujja because the specifier, like an unknown abrogator, drops itself without affecting the original.

This passage from Al-Tarweeh delves into a critical nuance in Hanafi usul: when a general text (amm) is specified by a specifier (mukhassis), does it still serve as a reliable proof? The author explores two analogies—one likening the specifier to an abrogator (nasikh) and another to an exception (istithna')—each leading to different conclusions. Understanding which analogy dominates determines whether the text can be used for legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two analogies
The passage presents two ways to view the mukhassis: akin to a nasikh (abrogator) which is an independent text, or akin to a mustathna (exception) which is dependent on the general statement.
The Hanafi position favors the naskh analogy.
2
Analyze the effect of an unknown mukhassis
If the mukhassis is unknown and resembles naskh, the specifier drops itself, leaving the general intact as a proof. If it resembles istithna', doubt enters and some scholars reject the general as a hujja.
The text rules that the first similarity (naskh) takes precedence.
3
Understand the role of ta'lil (causal reasoning)
When the mukhassis is known and allows ta'lil, one might think the general loses authority. The author counters that ta'lil only applies where the illah is present; otherwise, the general remains for other cases.
This refutes the objection that known specifier invalidates the general.
4
Conclude the Hanafi position
The text concludes that 'amm makhsus is a zanni proof but still valid for argumentation, as it was a hujja before specification and doubt does not remove certainty.
This parallels the Shafi'i view of unspecified general as zanni.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترويحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلُويْحِ پہلی مشابہت کی وجہ سے اور پیدا کرے گا جہالت کو عام میں دوسری مشابہت کو وجہ سے پس داخل ہو گا عام کے ساقط ہونے میں شک پس نہیں ساقط ہو گا وہ عام اس شک کی وجہ سے یعنی شک کی وجہ سے کیونکہ تخصیص سے پہلے وہ معمول بہ نہ تھا پس جب تخصیص کر دی گئی تو داخل ہو گیا شک اس بات میں کہ کیا باقی ہے وہ عام معمول یہ یا باطل ہو گیا پس نہیں باطل ہو گا شک کی وجہ سے ( اور اگر ہو وہ ) یعنی مخصص ( معلوم پس پہلی مشابہت سے صحیح ہوگی اس کی تعلیل ) نہیں مراد لیتے وہ اپنے قول فلشبہ الاول سے کہ بے شک وہ اس حیثیت سے کہ مشابہ ہے وہ تاریخ کے صحیح ہوگی اس کی تعلیل جیسا کہ صحیح یہ ہے کہ تعلیل کر دی جائے اس تاریخ میں جو منسوخ کرتا ہے عام کے بعض افراد کو تا کہ منسوخ ہو جائیں قیاس کے ساتھ عام میں سے بعض دوسرے افراد۔ کیونکہ ناسخ کی تعلیل اس طریقہ پر صحیح نہیں ہے جیسا کہ آ رہا ہے اسی صفحہ میں بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ بے شک وہ اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ بذات خود مستقل نص ہے صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل (جیسا کہ وہ ہے ہمارے نزدیک) کیونکہ ہمارے نزدیک اور اکثر علماء کے نزدیک صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل ، اختلاف کیا ہے اس میں جہاتی نے پس جب صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل تو نہیں ہوگی معلوم یہ بات کہ بے شک کتنے افراد خارج ہوئے تعلیل کے ساتھ یعنی قیاس کے ساتھ اور کتنے باقی ہیں عام کے تحت ( پس وہ ثابت کرے گا جہالت کو ان افراد میں جو بانی ہیں عام کے تحت اور دوسری مشابہت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے صحیح اس کی تعلیل جیسا کہ وہ بعض حضرات کے نزدیک ہے پس داخل ہو گیا شک عام کے ساقط ہونے میں پس نہیں ساقط ہو گا وہ اس کی وجہ سے ) یعنی دوسری مشابہت کی وجہ سے اور وہ استثناء کی مشابہت ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ بے شک مخصص بیان کرتا ہے یہ بات کہ بے شک مخصوص داخل نہیں ہے عام کے حکم میں پس اس شبہ کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے صحیح اس کی تعلیل جیسا کہ وہ جہائی کا مذہب ہے جیسا کہ نہیں ہے صحیح تعلیل مستی کی اور بعض دوسرے افراد کو نکالنا قیاس کے طریقہ کے ساتھ پس اس حیثیت سے کہ صحیح ہے اس کی تعلیل ہو جائیں گے باقی افراد عام کے تحت مجبول پس نہیں باقی رہے گا عام حجت اور اس حیثیت سے کہ نہیں ہے صحیح اس کی تعلیل باقی رہے گا عام حجت اور تحقیق تھا تخصیص سے پہلے حجت پس شک واقع ہو گیا اس کے باطل ہونے میں پس نہیں وہ باطل ہو گا شک کی وجہ سے یہ وہ تفصیل جو علماء نے کہا اور وارد ہوتا ہے اس پر اعتراض کہ بے شک جب ہے مذہب آپ کے نزدیک اور اکثر علماء کے نزدیک اس کے تعلیل کے صحیح ہونے کا پس واجب ہے یہ کہ باطل ہو جائے عام تمہارے نزدیک اس کی تعلیل کے صحیح ہونے میں تمہارے گمان پر بنا ء کرتے ہوئے اور نہیں صحیح ہے تمہارے لیے استدلال پکڑنا جبائی کے گمان کے ساتھ کہ اس کے نزدیک بے شک نہیں ہے صحیح اس عام کی تعلیل اس شب کو دفع کرنے لیے فرمایا ( علاوہ اس کے کہ بے شک تعلیل کا احتمال نہیں نکالتا وہ اس کو اس بات سے کہ ہو وہ حجت کیونکہ وہ جو کہ تقاضا کرتا ہے قیاس اس کی تخصیص کا تو اس میں تخصیص کر دی جاتی ہے اور جہاں قیاس تقاضا نہ کرے تو وہاں تخصیص نہیں کی جاتی ہے) کیونکہ شخص کہ اگر نہ جانی جا سکے اس میں علت تو تعلیل نہیں کی جاتی پس باقی رہے گا عام باقی میں حجت اور اگر پہچان لی جائے اس میں علت پس ہر وہ فرد کہ پائی جائے ملت اس فرد میں تو تخصیص کر دی جائے گی اس کی قیاس کے ساتھ اور جس فرد میں نہیں پائی جائے گی تو اس کی تخصیص کبھی نہیں کی جائے گی پس نہیں باطل ہو گا عام تعلیل کے احتمال کی وجہ سے۔ عام مخصوص عند البعض دلیل ظنی ہے تشریح :۔ یہاں سے ماتج احناف کے مذہب پر تفریح ذکر فرما رہے ہیں کہ جب عام خص عند البعض احناف کے نزدیک دلیل ظنی ہے یعنی اس میں شبہ ہے تو ایسے ہو گیا جیسے عام لم شخص عند البعض ( وہ عام جس میں تخصیص نہ کی گئی ہو ) امام شافعی کے نزدیک ہے اور عام لم تشخص عند البعض امام شافعی کے نزدیک ظنی تھا اور اس کی تخصیص خبر واحد سے بھی درست تھی اسی طرح عام خص عند ابعض کی تخصیص احناف کے نزدیک خبر واحد اور قیاس سے درست ہے کیونکہ اب یہ عام ظنی بن گیا ہے اور فنی کی تخصیص تمنی کے ساتھ جائز ہوتی ہے۔ جب عام خص عند البعض ظنی ہے تو اس سے استدلال کیوں درست ہے؟ ثم اراد ان مع وجود هذه الشبهة : یہاں سے ماتن ایک سوال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں۔ سوال :۔ جب احناف کے ہاں عام خص عند البعض دلیل فلنی ہے یعنی اس میں شبہ ہے تو اس سے استدلال (دلیل پکڑنا) درست نہیں ہونا چاہیے جیسا کہ بعض حضرات نے وہم بھی کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ اس سے استدلال درست ہے۔ جواب:۔ اگر چہ عام خص عند البعض دلیل ملنی ہے لیکن اس سے استدلال ساقط نہیں ہو گا۔ اس سے دلیل پکڑ نا پھر بھی صحیح ہے وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ تخصیص میں تخصص (جس کلام کے ذریعہ تخصیص کی جاتی ہے) کو ناسخ کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے صیغہ کے اعتبار ہے کہ جس طرح ناسخ کلام مستقل ہوتا ہے یہ بھی کلام مستقل ہے۔ اور مستقلی کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے حکم کے اعتبار سے کہ جس طرح مستقلی اس بات کا بیان ہوتا ہے کہ یہ افراد مستقلی منہ میں داخل نہیں ہیں اسی طرح مخصص بھی اس بات کو بیان کرتا ہے کہ مخصوص افراد عام میں داخل نہیں ہے۔ اب اگر تخصص مجہول ہو تو یہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ اس کو ناسخ کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے۔ اگر ہو تو اس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عام سے دلیل پکڑنا درست ہو یہ دلیل پکڑنے کے درجے سے ساقط نہ ہو کیونکہ ناسخ اگر مجہول ہو تو وہ خود ساقط ہو جاتا ہے منسوخ میں فرق نہیں آتا تو یہاں بھی مخصوص جب مجہول ہو تو مشخص خود کو ساقط ہو جانا چاہیے عام میں فرق نہیں آنا چاہیے۔ لیکن اگر یہ دیکھا جائے کہ اس کو مستثنیٰ کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے تو اسے دلیل پکڑ نا درست نہیں ہونا چاہیے بلکہ
Altarweeh for the solution of Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih: The first similarity (to nasikh) causes ignorance in the 'amm; the second similarity (to mustathna) causes doubt about the dropping of the 'amm, so it is not dropped due to doubt. Because before specification it was not acted upon, so when specification was made, doubt entered whether the 'amm remains acted upon or becomes void, so it does not become void due to doubt. And if the mukhassis is known, then the first similarity makes its ta'lil correct. They do not intend by their saying 'like the first' that it is correct as a ta'lil with regard to abrogation, as is correct: the ta'lil is made in that abrogation which abrogates some individuals of the 'amm by qiyas, so that other individuals of the 'amm are abrogated by qiyas. Because the ta'lil of the nasikh in this way is not correct, as will come. Rather, the meaning is that it is correct as a ta'lil because it is an independent text (as it is according to us), because according to us and most scholars, its ta'lil is correct. Al-Jahiz differed on this. So when its ta'lil is correct, it will not be known how many individuals are excluded by ta'lil (i.e., by qiyas) and how many remain under the 'amm. So it will cause ignorance about the individuals that remain under the 'amm. And due to the second similarity, its ta'lil is not correct (as according to some), so doubt enters about the dropping of the 'amm; thus it is not dropped due to it, i.e., due to the second similarity. That similarity is to istithna', in that the mukhassis expresses that the specified are not included in the ruling of the 'amm. Due to this doubt, its ta'lil is not correct, as is the madhhab of al-Jahiz. Just as the ta'lil of istithna' is not correct, and the exclusion of some individuals by way of qiyas is not correct. So from the perspective that its ta'lil is correct, the remaining individuals of the 'amm will be mu'awwal (interpreted), so the 'amm will not remain as a hujja. And from the perspective that its ta'lil is not correct, the 'amm remains a hujja. And it was a hujja before specification, so doubt about its becoming void occurs, so it does not become void due to doubt. This is the detail that the scholars stated. And an objection arises: Since according to you and most scholars the correctness of its ta'lil is the madhhab, then it is necessary that the 'amm becomes void according to you, based on your assumption of the correctness of its ta'lil. And it is not correct for you to argue with the assumption of al-Jabba'i that according to him the ta'lil of this 'amm is not correct. To repel this doubt, he said: Besides that, the possibility of ta'lil does not remove it from being a hujja, because qiyas requires its specification, so specification is done where qiyas demands, and where qiyas does not demand, specification is not done. Because if the 'illah cannot be known, no ta'lil is made, so the 'amm remains a hujja in the remainder. And if the 'illah is recognized, then every individual in which the 'illah is found will be specified by qiyas, and the individual in which it is not found will never be specified. So the 'amm does not become void due to the possibility of ta'lil. Specified general text ('amm makhsus) according to some is a zanni proof. Elucidation: From here, the author is expounding according to the madhhab of the Hanafis: When 'amm makhsus 'ind al-ba'd (according to some) is a zanni proof according to the Hanafis, i.e., it contains doubt, then it becomes like 'amm lam yukhas sas 'ind al-ba'd (the general that has not been specified) according to Imam al-Shafi'i. And 'amm lam yukhas sas 'ind al-ba'd was zanni according to Imam al-Shafi'i, and its specification by khabar wahid was valid. Similarly, the specification of 'amm makhsus 'ind al-ba'd according to the Hanafis is valid by khabar wahid and qiyas, because now this 'amm has become zanni, and the specification of a zanni is permitted with a zanni. When 'amm makhsus 'ind al-ba'd is zanni, why is it valid to argue from it? Then he intended: With the existence of this doubt... From here, the author is answering a question. Question: Since according to the Hanafis 'amm makhsus 'ind al-ba'd is a zanni proof, i.e., it contains doubt, then arguing from it (taking it as a proof) should not be valid, as some have mistakenly thought. However, arguing from it is valid. Answer: Even though 'amm makhsus 'ind al-ba'd is a zanni proof, argument from it is not invalidated. Taking it as a proof is still correct. The reason is that in specification, the specifier (the speech by which specification is made) resembles the abrogator in terms of wording: just as the abrogator is an independent speech, this is also an independent speech. And it resembles the independent in terms of ruling: just as the independent is a statement that these individuals are not included in the independent's scope, similarly the specifier states that the specified individuals are not included in the general. Now if the specifier is unknown, it will be seen whether it resembles the abrogator. If it does, its requirement is that arguing from the general is valid, it is not dropped from the level of proof, because if the abrogator is unknown, it itself is dropped and does not affect the abrogated. So here too, when the specifier is unknown, it should drop itself, not affect the general. But if it is seen that it resembles the excepted (mustathna), then arguing from it should not be valid, rather...
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion in Hanafi usul al-fiqh about the evidentiary status of a general text ('amm) that has been specified by a specifier (mukhassis). The author considers two analogies: the specifier is like a naskh (abrogator) or like an istithna' (exception). If the specifier is unknown and resembles a naskh, the general text remains a hujja (proof) because the specifier itself is dropped (like an unknown abrogator). If it resembles an istithna', doubt enters and some scholars hold it invalidates the general as proof. The Hanafi position, following the majority, is that specification does not remove the general from being a proof because the specifier is an independent text. The discussion then shifts to the Hanafi view that a specified general ('amm makhsus) is a zanni (probabilistic) proof, similar to an unspecified general according to al-Shafi'i. Despite being zanni, it remains a valid proof for argumentation because the possibility of ta'lil (causal reasoning) does not negate its authority. The author refutes an objection that if the specifier is known and allows for ta'lil, the general would lose authority; rather, ta'lil only applies where the 'illah is found, so the general still holds for remaining individuals.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A general term that includes all individuals of its category without exception.
مخصص (mukhassis): A text or evidence that specifies some individuals out of a general term.
ناسخ (nasikh): An abrogating text that supersedes an earlier ruling.
مستثنى (mustathna): An exception from a general statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, what is the effect of an unknown mukhassis that resembles a nasikh on the general text?
A) The general text becomes invalid as a proof.
B) The general text remains a valid proof because the specifier drops itself.
C) The general text becomes qat'i.
D) The general text can only be used if the specifier is known.

Key Takeaway
A specified general text ('amm makhsus) is a zanni proof but remains a valid hujja in Hanafi usul because the specifier, like an unknown abrogator, does not invalidate the original text for the unspecified individuals.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Evidential Value of a Specified General Text in Hanafi Usul
Explaining why a specified general text remains valid evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle 'al-yaqīn lā yazūl bi al-shakk' to justify the continued evidential value of a specified general text, and distinguish between the effects of known and unknown specification.

Core Idea
Certainty of a general text precedes specification; doubt does not invalidate original proof.

In this lesson, we delve into a foundational Hanafi usul principle: even after a general text is specified (making it probabilistic), it remains a valid proof. The passage answers a critical objection: if the text is now doubtful, why should it still be evidence? The answer lies in the legal maxim that certainty is not removed by doubt. We will explore the reasoning behind this and compare the specifying text to abrogation and exception.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the main claim: a specified general text is a probabilistic proof (zanni) but remains valid evidence (hujja). Note the contrast with those who think it becomes invalid.
Focus on the term 'عام مخصص عند البعض'.
2
Identify the operative principle
Locate the maxim 'al-yaqīn lā yazūl bi al-shakk'. Understand that before specification, the general was certain; doubt after specification does not remove that original certainty.
This maxim is universal in Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish between known and unknown specification
Follow the author's analysis: when specification is unknown, the analogy with nasikh preserves the general; when known, the analogy with mustathna determines validity. Note the different outcomes.
Key: unknown specification does not harm the general; known specification may affect it depending on the analogy.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
Recognize that for Shafi'i, an unspecified general is already probabilistic, so they do not face this issue in the same way. The Hanafi position on specified general is a distinct contribution.
This illustrates the madhhab-specific nature of usul categories.
5
Apply the principle to a new case
Use the maxim to argue that a general verse (e.g., 'اقطعوا يد السارق') remains evidence for most thieves even after specification (e.g., exclusion of the poor).
This shows practical relevance.

اختلاف ہے اس لیے کہ اس کے نزدیک اس میں تعلیل درست ہی نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال جب اس میں تعلیل صحیح ہے تو معلوم نہیں ہوگا کہ تعلیل کے بعد عام کے تحت کتنے افراد باقی ہیں اس لیے حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ اور عام سے دلیل پکڑنا درست نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر اس کو دیکھا جائے کہ یہ مستعفی کے مشابہ ہے تو اس سے دلیل پکڑنا درست ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ یہاں مخصوص معلوم ہے اور مستقلی کے معلوم ہونے کی صورت میں مستعلی منہ میں حکم سے پہلے چونکہ یقینا اس سے استدلال صحیح تھا اور الیانین لایز دل پا لٹک " اس لیے اس عام سے استدلال بالکل درست ہے۔ کیا ناسخ میں تعلیل ہوسکتی ہے؟
لا يريد بقوله : اس عبارت میں ماتن نے ایک اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے۔ اعتراض: ماتن نے کہا کہ اول مشابہت کی وجہ سے اس کی تعلیل درست ہے اول مشابہت سے مراد ناسخ کی مشابہت ہے تو اسے معلوم ہوا کہ تاریخ میں بھی تعلیل ہوتی ہے کیونکہ مخصوص میں تعلیل ہو رہی ہے ناسخ کی مشابہت کی وجہ سے تو مشابتہ کی وجہ سے تعلیل اسی صورت میں ہی درست ہو سکتی ہے کہ تاریخ میں بھی تعلیل صحیح ہو کہ نسخ کے بعد تاریخ میں جو افراد بچ گئے ہیں ان میں سے بھی بعض کو تیاس کے ذریعے منسوخ کیا جاسکے حالانکہ تاریخ میں اس طرح کی تعلیل درست نہیں ہے۔
A general text that has been specified according to some (Hanafis) is a probabilistic proof (zanni). Explanation: From here, the author (matn) elaborates on the Hanafi madhhab: when a general text is specified according to some (the Hanafis), it is a probabilistic proof (zanni) meaning there is doubt in it. So it becomes like an unspecified general text according to Imam al-Shafi'i. And the unspecified general text according to Imam al-Shafi'i was probabilistic, and its specification by khabar al-wahid was valid. Similarly, the specification of a specified general text according to some (Hanafis) is valid by khabar al-wahid and qiyas, because now this general has become probabilistic, and specification of a probabilistic text is permissible. When a specified general text is probabilistic, why is using it as evidence valid? Then he said: even with the existence of this doubt: From here the author responds to a question. Question: When according to the Hanafis a specified general text is a probabilistic proof (zanni) meaning there is doubt in it, then using it as evidence (istidlal) should not be valid, as some have erroneously thought, while in fact using it as evidence is valid. Answer: Even though a specified general text is a probabilistic proof, using it as evidence is not invalid. Using it as evidence is still valid. The reason is that the specification (takhsis) resembles an abrogating text (nasikh) in terms of its form, because just as a nasikh is an independent speech, this (mukhasis) is also an independent speech. And in terms of ruling, an abrogating text (nasikh) states that certain individuals are not included in the abrogated ruling; similarly, a specifying text (mukhasis) states that the specified individuals are not included in the general. Now if the specification (takhsis) is unknown, we look: does it resemble a nasikh? If it does, then the requirement is that using the general as evidence is valid; it does not fall from the level of proof, because if a nasikh is unknown, it itself falls (is invalid), but does not affect the abrogated text. Similarly, when the specification is unknown, the specifying text itself should fall, without affecting the general. But if it is seen that it resembles an exception (mustathna), then using it as evidence should not be valid; rather, it should fall from the level of proof because if the exception is unknown, the excepted-from (mustathna minhu) becomes ambiguous and no ruling is established. Therefore, when the specification is unknown, no ruling is established in the general, and it falls from the level of proof. So after specification, there arises doubt about whether the general falls from the level of proof. Before specification, it was certain that this general was a definitive proof; so before specification, it was certain that it does not fall from the level of proof. Now doubt arises about its falling. And the principle is: certainty is not removed by doubt. Therefore, due to doubt, the general does not fall from the level of proof, and using it as evidence is not invalid. And if the specification is known, then if it is seen to resemble a nasikh, using it as evidence should not be valid, because in that case, like a nasikh, it is also an independent speech, and an independent speech has the possibility of ta'lil (reasoning by cause), and this ta'lil is valid according to us, although 'Allama al-Shafi'i disagreed, because for him ta'lil in this context is not valid. In any case, when ta'lil is valid, it will not be known how many individuals remain under the general after the ta'lil, so the ruling is not established, and using the general as evidence is not valid. But if it is seen to resemble an exception (mustathna), then using it as evidence should be valid, because here the specification is known, and when the exception is known, the ruling is definitively established in the excepted-from; so when the specification is known, the ruling is definitively established in the remaining individuals of the general, because in this case ta'lil is not valid, just as it is not valid in the exception: one cannot use qiyas to exclude other individuals from the excepted-from. So due to the first resemblance, ta'lil should be valid and using it as evidence should also be valid; thus doubt arises about the validity of using this general as evidence. But before specification, it was certain that using it as evidence was correct, and al-yaqin la yuzal bi al-shakk, so using this general as evidence is absolutely valid. Can ta'lil occur in a nasikh? The author says: 'He does not mean by his statement...' In this phrase, the author responds to an objection. Objection: The author said that due to the first resemblance, its ta'lil is valid. The first resemblance refers to resemblance to a nasikh, so it is understood that ta'lil also occurs in the remaining (baqi) because ta'lil is occurring in the specified text due to resemblance to nasikh. So ta'lil can only be valid in that case if ta'lil is also valid in the remaining after abrogation: after abrogation, some individuals remain, and they could be abrogated again by qiyas, while in fact such ta'lil in the remaining is not valid.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul explanation of the evidential value of a general text ('amm) that has been specified (mukhasṣaṣ) according to the Hanafi view. The author addresses a key question: if such a general text becomes probabilistic (ẓannī) due to specification, how can it still be used as evidence? The answer relies on the usul principle 'al-yaqīn lā yazūl bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt). Before specification, the general text was certain (qaṭ‘ī) in its generality. Specification introduces doubt about whether the remaining individuals are still covered, but since certainty prevailed beforehand, the doubt does not invalidate the evidence. The author then compares the specifying text (mukhaṣṣiṣ) to either a nāsikh (abrogating text) or a mustathnā (exception) to determine its effect when the specification is unknown or known. This detailed analysis shows the sophistication of Hanafi legal theory in preserving the utility of revealed texts even after partial specification.

Key Terms
عام مخصوص عند البعض (ʿāmm mukhaṣṣaṣ ʿinda al-baʿḍ): A general text that has been specified (by evidence) according to some scholars, specifically the Hanafis, meaning that the specification is not definitive for all.
ظنی (ẓannī): Probabilistic; a level of certainty below qaṭʿī (definitive), subject to doubt and susceptible to specification.
الیقین لا یزول بالشک (al-yaqīn lā yazūl bi al-shakk): A foundational legal maxim: certainty is not removed by doubt. Used here to preserve the probative value of a specified general text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a specified general text remain valid evidence according to Hanafi usul?
A) Because specification does not affect the original general at all
B) Because certainty is not removed by doubt
C) Because specified texts are always stronger than unspecified
D) Because qiyās overrides any doubt

Key Takeaway
A specified general text ('āmm mukhaṣṣaṣ) remains a valid proof in Hanafi usul because the original certainty of its authority is not overcome by the doubt created by specification.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Distinguishing Takhsis and Naskh in Ta'lil
Analyzing the effect of ta'lil on makhsus and nasikh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between takhsis and naskh regarding the validity of ta'lil and apply the Hanafi principle that qiyas can specify but not abrogate.

Core Idea
Ta'lil is valid in mukhassis but not in nasikh because qiyas can specify but not abrogate a text.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a key distinction exists between specification (takhsis) and abrogation (naskh) of a general text ('amm). This passage from Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih addresses whether reasoning by 'illah (ta'lil) is valid in each case. The discussion revolves around the epistemological status of the general after specification or abrogation, and how the principle 'certainty is not removed by doubt' (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk) preserves its evidentiary value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage examines whether ta'lil (reasoning by 'illah) is valid in a general text ('amm) that has been specified (makhsus) or abrogated (mansukh). The Hanafi position is that ta'lil is valid in the case of takhsis but invalid in naskh.
This is a dispute about the epistemological weight of a general after specification.
2
Analyze the two scenarios for makhsus
The author considers two subcases for a specified general: (1) the specified portion is unknown (majhul), and (2) the specified portion is known (ma'lum). In the first, doubt arises but the general remains a proof due to the principle 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk'. In the second, if the specific resembles a nasikh, ta'lil is possible but still does not invalidate the general; if it resembles an excepted item (mustathna), ta'lil is not valid and the general is definite.
The resemblance to nasikh or mustathna determines the possibility of ta'lil.
3
Understand the role of qiyas in ta'lil
Ta'lil operates through qiyas, which can only specify individuals that possess the 'illah; it cannot abrogate the text because qiyas is weaker than the text. Thus, after takhsis, the general remains a proof for the remaining individuals not covered by the 'illah.
This is a key Hanafi principle: qiyas can specify but not abrogate.
4
Distinguish between mukhassis and nasikh
The passage concludes by stating the distinction: ta'lil of a mukhassis (specifier) is valid because it only clarifies that certain individuals were never intended, whereas ta'lil of a nasikh (abrogator) is invalid because qiyas cannot abrogate a text.
The 'illah in a nasikh would attempt to abrogate further, which is impermissible.

قبول کرنے میں نہیں دی بلکہ اس بات میں تشبیہ دی ہے کہ یہ دونوں کلام مستقل ہیں۔ علامہ جہائی کے مذہب سے استدلال کیوں کیا ؟ ويرد عليه انه لما كان المذهب : یہاں سے ماتن اگلی عبارت کا ربط بیان کرتے ہوئے
