يخرجه .... اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ عام میں تعلیل صحیح ہے تو اس بات کو لیتے ہوئے بھی یہ نہیں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ عام حجت نہیں بن سکتا کیونکہ تعلیل کا احتمال عام کو حجت ہونے سے نہیں نکالتا وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ تعلیل قیاس کے ذریعہ سے ہوتی ہے تو ہم یہ کہیں گے کہ جن افراد میں قیاس تقاضا کرے گا وہ خاص ہو جائیں گے باقی افراد میں حکم ثابت رہے گا یعنی اگر تو تخصیص کے بعد کسی فرد میں بھی علت نہ پائی جائے تو جس جس فرد میں علت پائی جائے گی وہ خاص ہوتا جائے گا اور باقی افراد میں عام حجت ہوگا تو تعلیل کے احتمال سے بھی عام حجت بننے سے نہیں نکلتا۔ ( فَظَهَرَ هُنَا الْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ التَّخْصِيصِ وَالنَّسْخِ ) أَى : لَمَّا ذَكَرُنَا أَنْ تَعْلِيلَ الْمُخَصَّصِ صَحِيحٌ ظَهَرَ مِنْ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ الْفَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْمُخَصِّصِ وَالنَّاسِخِ ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُ النَّاسِخِ الَّذِى يَنْسَخُ الْحُكْمَ فِى بَعْضِ أَفْرَادِ الْعَامِّ لِيُثْبِتَ النَّسْخَ فِي بَعْضٍ آخَرَ قِيَاسًا صُورَتُهُ أَنْ يَرِدَ نَضٌ خَاصٌ حُكْمُهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِحُكْمِ الْعَامِّ ، وَيَكُونَ وُرُودُهُ مُتَرَاحِيًا عَنْ وُرُودِ الْعَام فَإِنَّا نَجْعَلَهُ نَاسِخًا لَا مُخَصِّصًا عَلَى مَا سَبَقَ فَإِنَّ الْعَامُ الَّذِى نُسِحَ بَعْضُ مَا تَنَاوَلَهُ لَا يُنْسَحُ بِالْقِيَاسِ لأَنَّ الْقِيَاسَ لَا يَنْسَخُ النَّصَّ إِذْ هُوَ لَا يُعَارِضُهُ لِأَنَّهُ دُونَهُ لَكِنْ يُخَصِّصُهُ وَلَا يَلْزَمُ بِهِ الْمُعَارَضَةُ لِأَنَّهُ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَدْخُلُ .
Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: It should fall from the rank of evidence because if the excluded [item] is unknown, then ignorance enters the subject of exclusion and the ruling is not established; so here also when the specified [general] is unknown, the ruling is not established in the general and it falls from the rank of evidence. So after specification, doubt arises about the general falling from the rank of evidence, while before specification there was certainty that it is decisive evidence. Certainty existed that it did not fall, now doubt arises about its falling. The principle is that certainty is not removed by doubt. Therefore, due to doubt it will not fall from the rank of evidence, and using it as evidence is not invalid. And if the specified is known: if it is seen as resembling the abrogator, then using it as evidence should not be valid, because in that case, like the abrogator, it is independent speech, and independent speech admits the possibility of ta'lil (rationale). And this ta'lil is valid in our view, although 'Allama al-Juhai disagrees, as in his view ta'lil is not valid. In any case, when ta'lil is valid, it will not be known how many individuals remain under the general after ta'lil, so the ruling is not established, and using the general as evidence is not valid. But if it is seen as resembling the excepted [from an exception], then using it as evidence should be valid, because here the specified is known, and in the case of a known excepted item, the ruling in the excepted-from is definitely established. So when the specified is known, the ruling in the remaining individuals of the general is definitely established, because in that case ta'lil is not valid, just as in the excepted item, ta'lil and excluding other individuals from the excepted-from via qiyas is not valid. So from the perspective of the first resemblance, ta'lil should be valid, and using it as evidence should also be valid. Thus doubt arises about the validity of using the general as evidence, but before specification it was certainly valid, and certainty is not removed by doubt, so using the general as evidence is completely valid. Can there be ta'lil in the abrogator? He says: In this passage, the matn answers an objection. Objection: The matn said that due to the first resemblance, its ta'lil is valid; first resemblance refers to resemblance to the abrogator. So it is understood that ta'lil occurs in the secondary [abrogated] as well, because ta'lil in the specified is due to resemblance to the abrogator. So ta'lil due to resemblance can only be valid if ta'lil is also valid in the secondary [abrogated], so that after abrogation, some of the remaining individuals can be abrogated by qiyas, although such ta'lil is not valid in the secondary. Answer: The person we likened to the abrogator, we did so not in accepting ta'lil, but in that both are independent speech. Why is istidlal made from the school of 'Allama al-Juhai? He replies: and it is replied that when the school is... Here the matn explains the connection of the next phrase: the next phrase is an answer to an objection. Objection: In your view, ta'lil in a general specified with respect to some is valid, but in 'Allama al-Juhai's view it is not valid. When ta'lil is valid in your view, the general should become invalid; using it as evidence should not be valid. But you said the general will not become invalid. This shows that you have preferred 'Allama al-Juhai's school and taken his school as evidence. Answer: That the possibility of ta'lil does not remove it... If it is said that ta'lil in the general is valid, even then it cannot be said that the general cannot be a proof, because the possibility of ta'lil does not remove the general from being a proof. The reason is that ta'lil occurs through qiyas. We will say that the individuals in which qiyas requires [the 'illah] will become specified; the ruling remains established in the remaining individuals. That is, if after specification no 'illah is found in any individual, then in whichever individual the 'illah is found, that individual becomes specified, and in the remaining individuals the general is a proof. Thus even the possibility of ta'lil does not prevent the general from being a proof. (Thus here the distinction between takhsis and naskh became evident.) That is: When we mentioned that ta'lil of the specified is valid, from this ruling the difference between the specified and the abrogator became evident. For ta'lil of the abrogator that abrogates the ruling in some individuals of the general to establish abrogation in others by qiyas is not valid. Its form: a specific text comes whose ruling contradicts the general, and its occurrence is later than the occurrence of the general; then we make it an abrogator, not a specifyer, as preceded. For the general, some of which was abrogated, cannot be abrogated by qiyas, because qiyas does not abrogate the text, as it does not oppose it, since it is inferior to it. Rather it specifies it, and opposition is not necessitated because it clarifies that it did not enter [under the general].
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is an expansion on the distinction between takhsis (specification) and naskh (abrogation) regarding the validity of ta'lil (reasoning by 'illah). It is a usul al-fiqh discussion about how a general text ('amm) retains its evidentiary value after specification, even when its specified portion is unknown or known, and how this differs from abrogation. The author begins by analyzing the case where the specified (makhsus) is unknown (majhul). He argues that if the excepted item is unknown, the ruling in the excepted-from (mustathna minhu) is not established, so by analogy, when the specified portion of a general text is unknown, the ruling in the general also becomes unestablished, and the general falls from being evidence. However, before specification, there was certainty that the general was decisive evidence. After specification, doubt arises about its evidentiary status. The principle 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt) applies, so the general remains valid as evidence. Next, the author considers the case where the specified is known (ma'lum). Two scenarios are compared: resembling an abrogator (nasikh) or resembling an excepted item (mustathna). If it resembles a nasikh, ta'lil is possible because it is independent speech, and ta'lil is valid in the Hanafi school (unlike 'Allama al-Juhai who rejects it). Nonetheless, the general's evidentiary value becomes uncertain, but again the principle of certainty saves it. If it resembles an excepted item, ta'lil is not valid, so the general's proof is definite. The author then addresses an objection: why does the author liken the specified to the abrogator in terms of independent speech, and does that imply ta'lil is valid in the abrogator? The answer clarifies that the resemblance is only in the independence of speech, not in acceptance of ta'lil. Another objection asks why the author seems to prefer 'Allama al-Juhai's view when he holds that ta'lil does not invalidate the general. The response explains that the possibility of ta'lil does not remove the general from being a proof, because ta'lil operates through qiyas, which only specifies individuals that possess the 'illah; the rest remain under the general. Finally, the passage concludes with a clear distinction: ta'lil of a mukhassis (specifier) is valid because it only clarifies that certain individuals were never intended by the general, whereas ta'lil of a nasikh (abrogator) is invalid because qiyas cannot abrogate a text; it can only specify. This is a key Hanafi usul principle.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): The act of specifying some individuals of a general text, clarifying they were never intended by the general.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of the ruling of a text for some individuals, removing the ruling's application for those individuals.
تعليل (ta'lil): Reasoning by 'illah (effective cause) to extend or restrict a ruling, often via qiyas.
اليقين لا يزول بالشك (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk): A legal maxim: certainty is not removed by doubt. Used here to preserve the general's evidentiary status after speculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the possibility of ta'lil not invalidate a general text that has been specified?
A) Because ta'lil is not valid at all in such cases.
B) Because ta'lil only specifies individuals through qiyas, and the general remains a proof for the rest; certainty from before specification is not removed by doubt.
C) Because the general is always abrogated by any later specification.
D) Because 'Allama al-Juhai's view is preferred, which holds that ta'lil invalidates the general.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ta'lil is valid for specification (takhsis) but invalid for abrogation (naskh) because qiyas can specify but not abrogate a text.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
Distinction Between Takhsis and Naskh Regarding Ta'lil
Explaining the difference between specification and abrogation regarding causation by analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between takhsis and naskh with respect to the permissibility of ta'lil via qiyas and apply the Hanafi rule that qiyas can specify but cannot abrogate.

Core Idea
Qiyas can specify (takhsis) a general text but cannot abrogate (naskh) it because abrogation requires contradiction between equal texts.

In this passage, the author resolves an important confusion: if ta'lil (causal reasoning) is valid for a mukhassis (specifier), why does the general text remain authoritative? The answer reveals a fundamental distinction between specification and abrogation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying qiyas in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two processes
Recognize that takhsis excludes some individuals from a general ruling without lifting the ruling for the rest, whereas naskh abrogates the ruling entirely for those individuals.
Both affect the scope of a general text, but their mechanisms differ.
2
Understand the role of ta'lil
Ta'lil identifies the 'illa (effective cause) to extend or restrict a ruling via qiyas. The passage states that ta'lil is valid for a mukhassis but not for a nasikh.
Focus on why qiyas can specify but cannot abrogate.
3
Recognize the basis of naskh: mu'arada
Naskh operates on the basis of mu'arada (contradiction) between two texts of equal authority. Qiyas is inferior to nass, so it cannot create a contradiction.
Equality is required for mu'arada; qiyas is of lower rank.
4
Recognize the basis of takhsis: bayan
Takhsis is a bayan (clarification) that some individuals were never included in the general ruling. It does not involve contradiction, so qiyas can specify.
This is why qiyas is allowed for takhsis.
5
Apply the rule
If a specific text (khass) arrives later and contradicts the general, it becomes a nasikh (if equal). But qiyas alone cannot abrogate; it can only specify where the 'illa is present.
The practical outcome: a general text remains hujja for all individuals not excluded by qiyas.

التَّرُويْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلُويْحِ
جواب:۔ ہم نے جوشخص کو ناسخ کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی ہے یہ تعلیل کو قبول کرنے میں نہیں دی بلکہ اس بات میں تشبیہ دی ہے کہ یہ دونوں کلام مستقل ہیں۔
علامہ جہائی کے مذہب سے استدلال کیوں کیا ؟
ويرد عليه انه لما كان المذهب : یہاں سے ماتن اگلی عبارت کا ربط بیان کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ اگلی عبارت ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔
اعتراض:۔ آپ کے نزدیک عام خص عند البعض میں تعلیل درست ہے اور علامہ جہائی کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں ہے جب آپ کے نزدیک تعلیل درست ہے تو عام کو باطل ہونا چاہیے اس سے دلیل پکڑ نا درست نہیں ہونا چاہیے لیکن آپ نے کہا کہ عام باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ اس سے معلوم ہتا ہے کہ آپ نے علامہ جہائی کے مذہب کو ترجیح دی ہے اور اس کے مذہب کو حجت بنایا ہے۔ جواب:۔ على ان احتمال التعليل لا يخرجه .... اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ عام میں تعلیل صحیح ہے تو اس بات کو لیتے ہوئے بھی یہ نہیں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ عام حجت نہیں بن سکتا کیونکہ تعلیل کا احتمال عام کو حجت ہونے سے نہیں نکالتا وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ تعلیل قیاس کے ذریعہ سے ہوتی ہے تو ہم یہ کہیں گے کہ جن افراد میں قیاس تقاضا کرے گا وہ خاص ہو جائیں گے باقی افراد میں حکم ثابت رہے گا یعنی اگر تو تخصیص کے بعد کسی فرد میں بھی علت نہ پائی جائے تو جس جس فرد میں علت پائی جائے گی وہ خاص ہوتا جائے گا اور باقی افراد میں عام حجت ہوگا تو تعلیل کے احتمال سے بھی عام حجت بننے سے نہیں نکلتا۔ ( فَظَهَرَ هُنَا الْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ التَّخْصِيصِ وَالنَّسْخِ ) أَى : لَمَّا ذَكَرُنَا أَنْ تَعْلِيلَ الْمُخَصَّصِ صَحِيحٌ ظَهَرَ مِنْ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ الْفَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْمُخَصِّصِ وَالنَّاسِخِ ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُ النَّاسِخِ الَّذِى يَنْسَخُ الْحُكْمَ فِى بَعْضِ أَفْرَادِ الْعَامِّ لِيُثْبِتَ النَّسْخَ فِي بَعْضٍ آخَرَ قِيَاسًا صُورَتُهُ أَنْ يَرِدَ نَضٌ خَاصٌ حُكْمُهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِحُكْمِ الْعَامِّ ، وَيَكُونَ وُرُودُهُ مُتَرَاحِيًا عَنْ وُرُودِ الْعَام فَإِنَّا نَجْعَلَهُ نَاسِخًا لَا مُخَصِّصًا عَلَى مَا سَبَقَ فَإِنَّ الْعَامُ الَّذِى نُسِحَ بَعْضُ مَا تَنَاوَلَهُ لَا يُنْسَحُ بِالْقِيَاسِ لأَنَّ الْقِيَاسَ لَا يَنْسَخُ النَّصَّ إِذْ هُوَ لَا يُعَارِضُهُ لِأَنَّهُ دُونَهُ لَكِنْ يُخَصِّصُهُ وَلَا يَلْزَمُ بِهِ الْمُعَارَضَةُ لِأَنَّهُ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَدْخُلُ .
ترجمہ:۔ (پس ظاہر ہو گیا یہاں فرق تخصیص اور نسخ کے درمیان ) یعنی جب ہم نے ذکر کیا کہ بے شک مخصص کی تعلیل صحیح ہے تو ظاہر ہو گیا اس حکم سے فرق مخصص اور ناسخ کے درمیان کیونکہ نہیں ہے صحیح تعلیل اس تاریخ کی جو منسوخ کر دیتا ہے حکم کو عام کے بعض افراد میں تاکہ ثابت کرنے نسخے بعض دوسرے افراد میں قیاس کے ساتھ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ وارد ہو ایک ایسی خاص نص کہ اس کا حکم مخالف ہو عام کے حکم کے اور ہو اس کا وارد ہونا متراخی عام کے وارد ہونے سے کیونکہ ہم بناتے ہیں اس کو ناسخ نه متخصص جیسا کہ گزر چکا۔ ( کیونکہ وہ عام کہ منسوخ ہو جائیں اس کے بعض افراد جن کو شامل ہے تو وہ نہیں منسوخ ہوتا قیاس کے ساتھ ) کیونکہ قیاس نہین منسوخ کر تا نص کو ( کیونکہ وہ قیاس نہیں ہے معارض اس نص کا اس لیے کہ وہ اس سے کم ہے لیکن وہ اس میں تخصیص کر دے گا اور اس سے معارضہ بھی لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ وہ تخصیص بیان کرتی ہے اس بات کو کہ وہ داخل نہیں ہے)
مخصص و ناسخ کے درمیان فرق
تشریح:۔ یہاں سے ماتن ایک فائدہ ذکر فرمارہے ہیں۔
فائدہ :۔ ہماری اس تقریر سے کہ شخص کی تعلیل درست ہے یہ بات بھی واضح ہوگئی کہ شخص اور ناسخ کے درمیان فرق ہے؟ اور وہ فرق یہ ہے کہ تاریخ تعلیل کو قبول نہیں کرتا یعنی ایسا نہیں ہو سکتا کہ وہ ناسخ جس نے عام کے بعض افراد میں حکم کو منسوخ کیا ہے اس تاریخ میں قیاس کے ذریعہ تعلیل کی جائے تاکہ ان منسوخ افراد کے علاوہ بعض دوسرے افراد میں بھی حکم کو قیاس کے ذریعہ منسوخ کیا جا سکے ہاں شخص کی تعلیل درست ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ تعلیل میں حکم کو قیاس کے ذریعہ خاص کیا جاتا ہے اور قیاس کے ذریعہ تخصیص تو ہو سکتی ہے شیخ نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ شیخ معارضہ کے طریقہ پر ہوتا ہے یعنی دو حکم جو ایک دوسرے کے مخالف ہوں لیکن وہ ایک دوسرے کے مساوی ہوں تو ان کے درمیان معارضہ پیدا ہوتا ہے ۔ اس کے بعد ایک کو تاریخ اور دوسرے کو منسوخ قرار دیا جاتا ہے۔ لیکن تخصیص بیان کے طریقہ پر ہوتی ہے نہ کہ معارضہ کے طریقہ پر اب اگر ہم نسخ میں تعلیل کو درست کہیں تو قیاس سے نص کو منسوخ کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ اور یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ نسخ معارضہ کے طریقہ پر ہوتا ہے اور قیاس اور نص کا معارضہ نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ قیاس نص سے کم درجے کا ہے اور معارضہ کے لیے برابری شرط ہے لیکن تخصیص بیان کے طریقہ پر ہوتی ہے۔ معارضہ کے طریق پر نہیں ہوتی اس لیے اس میں برابری کی شرط نہیں ہے لہذا نص کی تخصیص قیاس کے ذریعہ ہو سکتی ہے۔ اب اگر ایک عام کے بعد خاص نص وارد ہو اور اس کی خاص کا حکم عام کے حکم کے مخالف ہو اور یہ خاص عام کے بعد وارد ہوا ہو تو خاص اور عام چونکہ برابر ہوتے ہیں اس لیے یہاں معارضہ واقع ہو جائے گا لہذا اس خاص کو عام کے لیے
(Thus the distinction between takhsis and naskh becomes apparent here.) That is: When we mentioned that ta'lil of the mukhassis is valid, from this ruling the difference between the mukhassis and the nasikh became apparent. For ta'lil is not valid for the nasikh that abrogates the ruling in some individuals of the general to establish abrogation in other individuals by analogy. Its form: a specific text comes whose ruling contradicts the ruling of the general, and its occurrence is later than the occurrence of the general. Then we consider it an abrogator, not a specifier, as has preceded. For the general whose some individuals have been abrogated cannot be abrogated by analogy, because analogy does not abrogate the text, since it does not contradict it, because it is inferior to it. Rather, it specifies it, and contradiction does not necessarily follow because it clarifies that it was not included.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the fundamental distinction between takhsis (specification) and naskh (abrogation) concerning the permissibility of ta'lil (causal reasoning) via qiyas (analogy). The author begins by addressing an objection: if ta'lil is valid for a mukhassis (specifier), why does the general (amm) still remain authoritative? The answer is that ta'lil through qiyas only removes those individuals that satisfy the 'illa (cause), leaving the rest under the general ruling. Then the author explicitly states the key distinction: ta'lil is valid for a mukhassis but not for a nasikh (abrogator). The reason is that abrogation operates on the basis of mu'arada (contradiction) between two equal texts, whereas specification is a bayan (clarification) that some individuals were never intended. Qiyas is of lower rank than nass (explicit text); it cannot abrogate a nass because abrogation requires equal strength and contradiction. However, qiyas can specify a nass because specification is not contradiction but clarification. Thus, if a specific text (khass) arrives later and contradicts the general, it becomes a nasikh (abrogating part of the general) if both are of equal authority. But if one attempts to use qiyas to abrogate further individuals, that is invalid because qiyas is inferior to the text and cannot oppose it. The commentary in Urdu reinforces this: ta'lil in takhsis is fine; in naskh it is not, because naskh is based on mu'arada which requires equality, while takhsis is based on bayan which does not.

Key Terms
تخصیص (takhsīṣ): Specification: excluding some individuals from the generality of a general term without abrogating the ruling for the rest.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation: lifting a ruling by a later text of equal authority, requiring contradiction and temporal posteriority.
تعلیل (ta'līl): Causal reasoning: identifying the effective cause ('illa) of a ruling to extend or restrict it via qiyas.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction: extending a ruling from a proven source to a new case based on shared 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is ta'lil via qiyas not valid for abrogation (naskh) but valid for specification (takhsis)?
A) Because abrogation requires mu'arada (contradiction) between equal texts, and qiyas is inferior to nass, so no contradiction.
B) Because qiyas can only be used for general rulings, not specific ones.
C) Because abrogation is a stronger form of specification.
D) Because the 'illa in naskh is always hidden.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas can specify a general text (takhsis) but cannot abrogate it (naskh) because abrogation requires equal authority and contradiction, whereas specification is clarification.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Sale with Exception: The Two Reasons for Invalidity
Explains the two reasons for the nullity of sale when an exception is made.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principles of jahl (ignorance) and shart fasid (invalid condition) to identify why a sale with an exception is invalid and derive the ruling using istihsan.

Core Idea
A sale with exception is invalid due to either ignorance in the price or an invalid condition contradicting the contract.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih examines two related sale scenarios where an exception (istithna') is made. The commentator explains the legal reasoning (istidlal) behind the invalidity, highlighting two distinct grounds: division of price leading to ignorance (jahl) and insertion of an invalid condition (shart fasid). Understanding these grounds is essential for recognizing how Hanafi usul principles govern contract validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Recognize the two scenarios: (1) selling a free person and a slave together for a lump sum, (2) selling two slaves with an exception of one slave. Both involve an exception, though the first is not a true exception but analogous.
In Hanafi usul, the real exception (istithna') requires the excluded to be part of the genus; a free person is not sellable so it's not a true exception.
2
Analyze the first reason: jahl
The price was set for both items together. When one item is excluded, the remaining item must be sold with a share of that price. This allocation is done initially (ibtida'an) before the contract, causing ignorance (jahl) about the exact price for that item. Since jahl in the price invalidates a sale, the contract becomes fasid.
This is called bay' bi al-hissah ibtida'an. Contrast with bay' bi al-hissah baqa'an (subsequent division) which is valid.
3
Analyze the second reason: shart fasid
In both cases, the acceptance of a non-sold item (the free person or the excluded slave) is made a condition for accepting the sale of the sold item. This condition contradicts the nature of a sale contract (muqtada al-'aqd), which requires the sold item to be known and owned. Such a condition is shart fasid and renders the sale invalid.
Hanafi: any condition that contradicts the contract's requirements makes it fasid.
4
Distinguish from valid subsequent share sale
The commentator mentions that sale by share subsequently (baqa'an) is valid, as will be seen in the context of naskh (abrogation). This distinction shows that the invalidity is specific to the initial allocation, not a general rule.
5
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The ruling that such a sale is invalid is derived through rational reasoning (dalil 'aqli) based on the principles of jahl and shart fasid. This exemplifies istihsan and the application of general usul maxims to specific cases.
The two reasons are independent; either one alone suffices to invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے استثناء کی حقیقت لیکن مناسب ہے استثناء کے اس بات میں بے شک استثناء روک دیتا ہے مستعفی کے داخل ہونے کو صدر کلام کے حکم میں اور اس مسئلہ میں نہیں داخل ہوتا آزاد ایجاب کے تحت باوجود یکہ صدر کلام اس کو شامل ہوتا ہے پس یہ ایسے ہو گیا گویا کہ یہ متمنی ہے اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں وہ یہ ہے کہ جب بیچ کرے دو غلاموں کی مگر اس کی استثناء کی حقیقت موجود ہے پس جب نہیں ہے داخل ان میں سے ایک بیچ میں تو نہیں ہے صحیح بھیج دوسرے میں دو وجہ سے ہے۔ ان دو میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ ہو جائے گی بیچ دوسرے میں اس کے حصہ کے ساتھ اس ثمن میں سے جو مقابل تھا ان دونوں کے اور بیچ بالحصہ ابتداء باطل ہے جہالت کی وجہ سے اور سوائے اس کے نہیں ہم نے کہا ابتداء کیونکہ بیع بالحصہ بقاء صحیح ہے جیسا کہ آرہا ہے اس مسئلہ میں جو نسخ کی نظیر ہے اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ بے شک بیچ دوسرے میں بیج ہے ایسی شرط کے ساتھ جو مخالف ہے عقد کے مقتضی کے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ بے شک قبول کرنا اس چیز کو جو مبیع نہیں ہے اور وہ آزاد ہے یا عبد مستعفی ہے بنایا ہے اس کو شرط صحیح کو قبول کرنے کے لیے۔
تشریح : استثناء کی نظیر:۔ ایک آدمی نے آزاد اور غلام کو مل کر کسی کو کہا کہ میں تجھے یہ دونوں غلام ایک ہزار کے بدلے میں بیچتا ہوں اور اس نے قبول کر لیا۔ یا کسی آدمی نے دو غلاموں کے بارے میں کسی کو کہا کہ بعت هــديــن الـعــديـن بــالـف الا هذا بحضته ، کہ میں تجھے یہ دو غلام ہزار کے بدلے میں بیچتا ہوں لیکن یہ غلام اس کے حصہ کے ساتھ نہیں بیچتا یعنی ایک غلام کا استثناء کر لیا۔ یہ دونوں مسئلے استثناء کی نظیر ہیں ہیں۔ کیونکہ استثناء میں یہ بات بیان کی جاتی ہے۔ کہ مستعفی صدر کلام (مستعلی منہ میں داخل نہیں ہے۔ اور یہاں ثانی صورت میں تو حقیقتا استثناء موجود ہے اس میں تو کوئی خفا نہیں ہے۔ اور مسئلہ اول میں حقیقتا تو استثناء نہیں ہے لیکن استثناء کے مناسب ہے کیونکہ اس میں صدر کلام یعنی بیچ آزاد اور غلام دونوں کو شامل ہے لیکن آزاد آدمی ایجاب میں داخل نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں بیچ نہیں ہوتی تو یہ استثناء کی طرح ہی ہو گیا۔
بیچ کی عدم جواز پر دلیل
فاذا لم يدخل : یہاں سے ماتن مسئلہ بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ مذکورہ بالا دو صورتوں میں سے اول صورت میں آزاد آدمی بیچ میں داخل نہیں ہورہا اور ثانی صورت میں ایک غلام بیع میں داخل نہیں ہورہا تو دونوں صورتوں میں بیع جائز نہیں ہوگی اور اس کی دو وجوہات ہیں۔
(i) دونوں صورتوں میں ایک میں بیچ صحیح نہیں ہے پہلی صورت میں حر تحت العقد داخل نہیں اور دوسری صورت میں عبد مستثنی داخل نہیں ہے اور دوسرے آدمی میں بھی صحیح ہورہی ہے من میں سے اس کے حصہ کے بدلے اور پیشین ایسا ہے کہ اس کو دونوں کے مقابلے میں مقرر کیا گیا ہے لیکن اب ایک کا حصہ علیحدہ کیا جا رہا ہے تو یہ بیچ بالحصہ ابتداء ہے یعنی معاملہ نام ہونے سے پہلے شمن کو تقسیم کیا گیا ہے اور بیچ بالحصہ ابتداء ہو تو جائز نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ اس میں جہالت آجاتی ہے کہ جس کو طبیع بنایا گیا ہے اس کا شمن متعین تو تھا نہیں تو اس کے ثمن میں جہالت آجائے گی اور ثمن میں جہالت کی وجہ سے بیع صحیح نہیں ہوتی ہاں اگر بیع بالحصہ بقاء ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ بعد میں آئے گا۔
(ii) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں ایسی شرط لگائی جارہی ہے جو بیع کے منافی ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ غیر طبیع میں بیع کو قبول کرنا مبیع میں بیچ کو قبول کرنے کے لیے شرط بنایا جارہا ہے۔ اول صورت میں مبیع نہیں ہے لیکن اس کو قبول کرنا غلام کے قبول کرنے کے لیے شرط بنایا جارہا ہے ۔ اور دوسری صورت میں جس غلام کومستثنی کیا گیا ہے اس میں بیج کو قبول کرنا دوسرے غلام کو قبول کرنے کے لیے شرط بنایا جارہا ہے حالانکہ مستثنی غلام مبیع نہیں ہے۔ تو دونوں صورتوں میں ایک شرط فاسد لگائی جا رہی ہے۔ اور شرط فاسد سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ تو یہ بیع درست نہیں ہوگی۔
It is the reality of exception, but it is appropriate for exception. Indeed, exception prevents the excluded from entering under the ruling of the primary statement. In this case, the free person does not enter under the offer, even though the primary statement includes him. So it became as if it is an exception. In the second case, it is that when one sells two slaves, but the reality of exception is present. So when one of them does not enter the sale, then the sale in the other is not valid for two reasons. One of them is that the sale in the other would be with its share of the price that was in exchange for both, and sale by share initially is invalid due to ignorance. And we said initially only because sale by share subsequently is valid, as will come in the case that is analogous to abrogation. The second reason is that indeed the sale in the other is a sale with a condition that contradicts the requirement of the contract, and that is that accepting that which is not the sold item—whether it is a free person or an excluded slave—is made a condition for accepting the sale. Explanation: The analogy of exception: A man together with a free person and a slave said to someone, 'I sell you these two slaves for a thousand,' and he accepted. Or a man said regarding two slaves, 'I sell you these two slaves for a thousand except this one with his share,' meaning he excluded one slave. These two cases are analogies of exception. Because in exception, it is stated that the excluded is not included in the primary statement. In the second case, the exception is actually present, no doubt. In the first case, there is no actual exception, but it is suitable for exception because the primary statement includes both the free person and the slave, but the free person does not enter the offer because a free person cannot be sold, so it became like an exception. Proof of the non-permissibility of the sale: 'So when it does not enter' — from here the matn author states that in the two mentioned cases, in the first case the free person does not enter the sale, and in the second case one slave does not enter the sale, so in both cases the sale is not permissible, and there are two reasons for it. (i) In both cases, the sale in one is not valid: in the first case, the free person does not enter the contract, and in the second case, the excluded slave does not enter. And in the other subject, the sale is valid with its share of the price that was set for both. But now the share of one is separated, so this is a sale by share initially—meaning the price is divided before the transaction is complete—and a sale by share initially is not permissible because ignorance arises: the price of what is made the sold item was not determined, so ignorance enters the price, and due to ignorance in the price, the sale is not valid. However, if the sale by share is subsequent, there is no harm, as will come later. (ii) The second reason is that in both cases, a condition is being placed that contradicts the sale, and that is that accepting the sale in something that is not the sold item is made a condition for accepting the sale in the sold item. In the first case, the free person is not the sold item, but accepting him is made a condition for accepting the slave. In the second case, the excluded slave is not the sold item, but accepting the sale in him is made a condition for accepting the other slave. So in both cases, an invalid condition is being placed, and an invalid condition makes the sale void. Thus, this sale is not valid.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining a ruling from the matn. It discusses two cases of sale where an exception (istithna) is made: (1) selling a free person and a slave together for a fixed price, and (2) selling two slaves with an exception of one slave. In both cases, the sale is not permissible. The commentator gives two reasons for the impermissibility. First, the sale becomes a sale by share initially (bay' bi al-hissah ibtida'an), which introduces ignorance (jahl) in the price because the price is not allocated to the specific sold item, and ignorance in price invalidates the sale. Second, an invalid condition (shart fasid) is present: accepting the sale of a non-sold item (the free person or the excluded slave) is made a condition for accepting the sale of the sold item. Such a condition contradicts the nature of the sale contract and renders it void. The commentator also clarifies that sale by share subsequently (bay' bi al-hissah baqa'an) is valid, as will be seen in the analogy to abrogation (naskh). The passage follows the author's order by first explaining the two cases, then providing the two reasons.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): A legal exception where part of the subject matter is excluded from the sale contract.
جهالت (jahl): Ignorance regarding the price or subject matter that invalidates a contract.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that contradicts the requirements of the contract and renders it void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the sale of a free person and a slave together for a lump sum considered invalid in the first case?
A) Because the free person is not included in the sale at all.
B) Because it becomes a sale by share initially, introducing ignorance in the price.
C) Because the free person cannot be sold, so the contract is void from the start.
D) Because the condition of accepting the free person is valid, but the sale is invalid due to lack of consent.

Key Takeaway
A sale with an exception is invalid because it either introduces ignorance in the price or imposes an invalid condition, both of which violate fundamental Hanafi contract principles.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Analogy of Takhsis: Sale with Option as a Dual Resemblance
Analogy of takhsis using a sale with option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the analogy between takhsis and a conditional sale option, identifying how it mirrors both naskh and istithna'.

Core Idea
Takhsis resembles naskh in wording and istithna' in effect; a sale with option mirrors this duality.

This passage presents a fiqh case that serves as an analogy (nazir) for the usul concept of takhsis. By examining how a slave sold with an option enters the offer but not the ruling, we uncover the dual resemblance that makes it akin to specification. Understanding this analogy helps clarify the nature of takhsis as distinct from naskh and istithna'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario and ruling
The case: a seller sells two slaves for one thousand, with an option (khiyar) on one. The ruling: valid only if the subject of the option and its price are known; otherwise invalid.
The condition of knowledge ensures certainty, which is required for validity.
2
Extract the key principle
The author states that the sold item with an option 'enters the offer but not the ruling' (يدخل في الإيجاب لا في الحكم). This means it is initially included in the contract formation but not fully integrated into the legal effect until the option is exercised.
This dual status is the core of the analogy.
3
Compare to naskh and istithna'
Because the optioned item enters the offer (cause/sabab), its removal by option resembles naskh (which changes a ruling). Because it does not enter the ruling (hukm), its exclusion resembles istithna' (exception). Thus, the case has a dual resemblance.
Naskh operates on the ruling itself; istithna' excludes from a general statement.
4
Connect to takhsis
Takhsis (specification) similarly resembles naskh in its wording (the general term is narrowed) and istithna' in its effect (some individuals are excluded). The parallel is exact: both involve an initial inclusion that is then qualified.
Takhsis does not cancel the ruling but limits its scope.
5
Conclude why the analogy holds
Because the sale with option and takhsis share the same duality, the former serves as a clear illustrative example (nazir) for the latter. Knowing the conditions of the sale (knowledge of subject/price) similarly clarifies the requirements for valid takhsis.
This reinforces the Hanafi understanding of takhsis as bayan (clarification).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنَظِيرُ التَّخْصِيصِ مَا إِذَا بَاعَ عَبْدَيْنِ بِأَلْفِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ بِالْخِيَارِ فِي أَحَدِهِمَا صَحْ إنْ عَلِمَ مَحَلَّ الْخِيَارِ وَثَمَنَهُ؛ لِأَنَّ الْمَبِيعَ بِالْخِيَارِ يَدْخُلُ فِي الْإِيجَابِ لَا فِي الْحُكْمِ فَصَارَ فِي السَّبَبِ كَالنَّسْخِ، وَفِي الْحُكْمِ كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ فَإِذَا جَهِلَ أَحَدُهُمَا لَا يَصِحُّ لِشَبَهِ الاسْتِثْنَاءِ، وَإِذَا عَلِمَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَصِحُّ لِشَبَهِ النَّسْخِ وَلَمْ يُعْتَبَرُ هَهُنَا شَبَهُ الاسْتِنَاء حَتَّى يَفْسُدَ بالشَّرْطِ الْفَاسِدِ بخِلافِ الحُرِّ وَالْعَبْدِ إذَا بَيْنَ حِصَّةَ كُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَبَيَانُ مُنَاسَبَتِهَا التَّخْصِيصَ أَنَّ التَّخْصِيضَ يُشَابِهُ النَّسْخَ بِصِيغَتِهِ، وَالاسْتِثْنَاءَ بِحُكْمِهِ، وَهَهُنَا الْعَبْدُ الَّذِي فِيهِ الْخِيَارُ دَاخِل فِى الْإِيجَابِ لَا الْحُكْمِ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ دَاخِلٌ فِي الإِيجَابِ يَكُونُ رَدُّهُ بِخِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ تَبْدِيلًا فَيَكُونُ كَالنَّسْخِ وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ غَيْرُ دَاخِل فِى الْحُكْمِ يَكُونُ رَدُّهُ بِخِيَارِ الشَّرَطِ بَيَانَ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَدْخُلُ فَيَكُونُ كَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ وَإِذَا كَانَ لَهُ شَبَهَانِ يَكُونُ كَالتَّخْصِيصِ الَّذِى لَهُ شَبَة بِالنَّسْخِ وَشَبَة بِالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ
(The analogy of takhsis is: when one sells two slaves for one thousand on the condition that he has an option regarding one of them, it is valid if he knows the subject of the option and its price; because the sold item with an option enters the offer but not the ruling, so it becomes like naskh in terms of cause, and like istithna' in terms of ruling. So if one of them is unknown, it is not valid due to resemblance to istithna', and if each of them is known, it is valid due to resemblance to naskh. The resemblance to istithna' is not considered here such that it would become invalid due to a corrupt condition, unlike the case of a free person and a slave when the share of each is specified according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And the explanation of its suitability for takhsis: takhsis resembles naskh in its wording and istithna' in its ruling. Here, the slave in whom there is an option enters the offer but not the ruling, as known. So from the perspective that it enters the offer, its rejection by the condition of option is a change, so it is like naskh. And from the perspective that it does not enter the ruling, its rejection by the condition of option shows that it did not enter, so it is like istithna'. And since it has two resemblances, it becomes like takhsis, which has a resemblance to naskh and a resemblance to istithna'.)
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of analogizing fiqh cases to usul concepts, now focusing on takhsis (specification). The scenario: a person sells two slaves for one thousand with the condition that he retains an option (khiyar) regarding one of them. The ruling: the sale is valid only if the slave subject to the option and its price are known; otherwise invalid. The author explains that the slave under option enters the offer (ijab) but not the judicial effect (hukm). This duality gives it two resemblances: in the cause (sabab) it resembles naskh (because the option can change the initial inclusion), and in the ruling (hukm) it resembles istithna' (exception, because the slave is effectively excluded from the legal effect). This dual resemblance is exactly what characterizes takhsis—takhsis similarly resembles naskh in its form (the general wording) and istithna' in its effect (exclusion of a specific). Therefore, the sale is valid when the details are known. Additionally, the author contrasts this with the case of selling a free person and a slave together, where Abu Hanifa holds that the share of each must be specified; without specification, the sale is invalid due to the corrupt condition of mixing free and slave. This further illustrates how the principle of takhsis operates differently from istithna' in contracts.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification: the process of excluding some individuals from a general term, resembling both naskh (in form) and istithna' (in effect).
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option allowing one party to rescind a contract within a specified period.
استثناء (istithna'): Exception: excluding something from a general statement, akin to takhsis but only in effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes the sale of two slaves with an option on one analogous to takhsis?
A) Both involve a conditional cancellation.
B) The option creates a resemblance to naskh in cause and to istithna' in ruling.
C) The price is unknown.
D) The sale is invalid without specification.

Key Takeaway
The sale with option illustrates takhsis's dual resemblance: like naskh in form of inclusion, like istithna' in effect of exclusion.
